        // LinkedHashSet preserves insertion order
        Set<String> uniqueSet = new LinkedHashSet<>(urls);
        List<String> uniqueList = new ArrayList<>(uniqueSet);

        System.out.println("Original: " + urls);
        System.out.println("Unique:   " + uniqueList);
    }
}

Output:

Original: [/login, /dashboard, /login, /settings, /dashboard]
Unique:   [/login, /dashboard, /settings]

Complexity: Time O(n), Space O(n)

Q2: Find Duplicate Elements

Problem: Find all duplicate test case IDs in a list.

Approach: HashSet.add() returns false when the element already exists — that's a duplicate.

import java.util.*;

public class FindDuplicates {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        List<String> testIds = Arrays.asList("TC001", "TC002", "TC001", "TC003", "TC002", "TC004");

        Set<String> seen = new HashSet<>();
        Set<String> duplicates = new HashSet<>();

        for (String id : testIds) {
            if (!seen.add(id)) {  // add returns false = duplicate
                duplicates.add(id);
            }
        }

        System.out.println("Duplicate test IDs: " + duplicates);
    }
}

Output:

Duplicate test IDs: [TC001, TC002]

Complexity: Time O(n), Space O(n)

Q3: Character Frequency Using HashMap

Problem: Count frequency of each character in a test string (e.g., validate password complexity rules).

Approach: Iterate characters, use HashMap<Character, Integer>, increment count with getOrDefault.

import java.util.*;

public class CharFrequency {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        String password = "Test@123Test";

        Map<Character, Integer> freqMap = new HashMap<>();
        for (char c : password.toCharArray()) {
            freqMap.put(c, freqMap.getOrDefault(c, 0) + 1);
        }

        freqMap.forEach((ch, count) ->
            System.out.println("'" + ch + "' → " + count)
        );
    }
}

Output:

'T' → 2
'e' → 2
's' → 1
't' → 2
'@' → 1
'1' → 1
'2' → 1
'3' → 1

Complexity: Time O(n), Space O(k) where k = unique characters

Q4: Sort List of Employees (Comparable vs Comparator)

Problem: Sort automation team members by salary, then by name.

import java.util.*;

class Employee implements Comparable<Employee> {
    String name;
    int salary;

    Employee(String name, int salary) {
        this.name = name;
        this.salary = salary;
    }

    // Natural ordering: by salary ascending
    @Override
    public int compareTo(Employee other) {
        return Integer.compare(this.salary, other.salary);
    }

    @Override
    public String toString() {
        return name + " ($" + salary + ")";
    }
}

public class SortEmployees {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        List<Employee> team = new ArrayList<>(Arrays.asList(
            new Employee("Alice", 90000),
            new Employee("Bob", 75000),
            new Employee("Charlie", 90000)
        ));

        // Approach 1: Comparable (natural order — by salary)
        Collections.sort(team);
        System.out.println("By salary (Comparable): " + team);

        // Approach 2: Comparator (custom — by name)
        team.sort(Comparator.comparing(e -> e.name));
        System.out.println("By name (Comparator):   " + team);

        // Approach 3: Comparator chaining — salary desc, then name asc
        team.sort(Comparator.comparingInt((Employee e) -> e.salary).reversed()
                          .thenComparing(e -> e.name));
        System.out.println("Salary desc, name asc:  " + team);
    }
}

Output:

By salary (Comparable): [Bob ($75000), Alice ($90000), Charlie ($90000)]
By name (Comparator):   [Alice ($90000), Bob ($75000), Charlie ($90000)]
Salary desc, name asc:  [Alice ($90000), Charlie ($90000), Bob ($75000)]

Complexity: Time O(n log n), Space O(1)

Q5: Sort HashMap by Value

Problem: Sort test failure counts by frequency (value) descending.

Approach: Stream API on entrySet(), sort by value, collect to LinkedHashMap.

import java.util.*;
import java.util.stream.*;

public class SortMapByValue {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Map<String, Integer> failures = new HashMap<>();
        failures.put("testLogin", 15);
        failures.put("testCheckout", 8);
        failures.put("testSearch", 22);
        failures.put("testProfile", 3);

        Map<String, Integer> sorted = failures.entrySet().stream()
            .sorted(Map.Entry.<String, Integer>comparingByValue().reversed())
            .collect(Collectors.toMap(
                Map.Entry::getKey,
                Map.Entry::getValue,
                (a, b) -> a,
                LinkedHashMap::new
            ));

        sorted.forEach((test, count) ->
            System.out.println(test + " → " + count + " failures")
        );
    }
}

Output:

testSearch → 22 failures
testLogin → 15 failures
testCheckout → 8 failures
testProfile → 3 failures

Complexity: Time O(n log n), Space O(n)

Q6: Count Word Frequency in Paragraph

Problem: Count word frequency in an error log paragraph to find most common errors.

import java.util.*;

public class WordFrequency {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        String log = "timeout timeout element not found stale element timeout connection refused";

        Map<String, Integer> wordCount = new HashMap<>();
        for (String word : log.split("\\s+")) {
            word = word.toLowerCase();
            wordCount.put(word, wordCount.getOrDefault(word, 0) + 1);
        }

        // Find most frequent word
        String maxWord = Collections.max(wordCount.entrySet(),
            Map.Entry.comparingByValue()).getKey();

        System.out.println("Word frequencies: " + wordCount);
        System.out.println("Most frequent:    " + maxWord);
    }
}

Output:

Word frequencies: {timeout=3, element=2, not=1, found=1, stale=1, connection=1, refused=1}
Most frequent:    timeout

Complexity: Time O(n), Space O(k) where k = unique words

Interview Q&A — Section 6 (15+ Questions)

Q: What is the difference between Collection and Collections?

A: Collection is the root interface of the framework hierarchy. Collections is a utility class with static methods like sort(), reverse(), synchronizedList(). In automation, you use Collections.sort() to sort test data lists.

Q: Why is ArrayList preferred over Vector?

A: Vector is synchronized (thread-safe but slow). ArrayList is faster for single-threaded test execution. For parallel tests, use thread-safe alternatives like CopyOnWriteArrayList, not Vector.

Q: Can we store null in ArrayList?

A: Yes. ArrayList allows multiple nulls. Useful when parsing optional fields from test data where some columns may be empty.

Q: How does HashSet maintain uniqueness?

A: It uses hashCode() to find the bucket and equals() to compare within the bucket. If equals() returns true, the element is not added. Override both in custom test data objects.

Q: What happens if two keys in HashMap have the same hashCode?

A: Collision occurs. Java stores them in a linked list within the same bucket. If the bucket exceeds 8 entries (Java 8+), it converts to a Red-Black tree for O(log n) performance.

Q: Why doesn't HashMap implement Collection interface?

A: Map stores key-value pairs, not individual elements. It has its own hierarchy with Map.Entry for iterating entries.

Q: When would you use LinkedHashMap over HashMap in a framework?

A: When config property order matters — e.g., test execution order defined in a properties file, or maintaining insertion order of API request parameters for debugging.

Q: Is HashMap thread-safe?

A: No. In parallel TestNG/Cucumber execution, use ConcurrentHashMap for shared config or report data.

Q: What is fail-fast vs fail-safe iterator?

A: Fail-fast (ArrayList, HashMap) throws ConcurrentModificationException on structural modification during iteration. Fail-safe (ConcurrentHashMap) works on a clone — no exception but may not reflect latest changes.

Q: How do you convert ArrayList to Array and vice versa?

A: list.toArray(new String[0]) and new ArrayList<>(Arrays.asList(array)) or Arrays.asList() (fixed-size).

Q: What is the initial capacity of ArrayList and why does it matter?

A: Default is 10. If you know you'll store 500 test data rows, set initial capacity to avoid repeated resizing: new ArrayList<>(500).

Q: Comparable vs Comparator — when to use which?

A: Comparable = natural ordering defined inside the class (one sort logic). Comparator = external, multiple sort strategies without modifying the class. In frameworks, use Comparator for flexible test data sorting.

Q: How do you iterate a HashMap?

A: Four ways: (1) entrySet() — best, (2) keySet() then get value, (3) values(), (4) Java 8 forEach. Prefer entrySet() for config iteration.

Q: What is ConcurrentModificationException and how to avoid it?

A: Thrown when a collection is structurally modified during iteration (except via Iterator.remove()). In automation, common when filtering WebElements during for-each. Fix: use Iterator, stream filter, or removeAll with a separate list.

Q: Can TreeMap have null keys?

A: No. TreeMap uses comparison — null key causes NullPointerException. Use HashMap if null keys are needed.

Q: How would you find the intersection of two lists of test data?

A: list1.retainAll(list2) modifies list1 to keep only common elements. Or use streams: list1.stream().filter(list2::contains).collect(Collectors.toList()).

Q: What collection would you use to store WebElements and why?

A: ArrayList<WebElement> — because findElements() returns a list, you need index access for specific rows, and you iterate sequentially. No need for Set (duplicates aren't an issue) or Map (no key-value relationship).

Section 7: Exception Handling

Exception handling separates fragile test scripts from production-grade automation frameworks. Every Selenium and REST Assured exception you handle gracefully is a test suite that runs reliably in CI/CD.

Exception Hierarchy

                        Throwable
                       /         \
                  Exception       Error
                  /    |    \         \
         IOException  |  RuntimeException  OutOfMemoryError
         SQLException |       |            StackOverflowError
         ClassNotFound|       |
                      |   ┌───┴────────────────┐
                      |   |                    |
                      | NoSuchElement    NullPointerException
                      | TimeoutException IllegalArgumentException
                      | StaleElementRef  IndexOutOfBoundsException
                      | ElementClickInt. ArrayIndexOutOfBounds
                      | WebDriverException NumberFormatException
                      |
              (Checked Exceptions)
         Must handle or declare (throws)

Checked vs Unchecked Exceptions

FeatureCheckedUnchecked (Runtime)
Parent classException (not RuntimeException)RuntimeException
Compile-time checkYes — must handle or declareNo — optional handling
ExamplesIOException, SQLExceptionNoSuchElementException, NPE
When thrownRecoverable external failuresProgramming errors, framework failures
Automation contextReading config files, DB connectionsElement not found, stale element
Must declare in signature?Yes (or try-catch)No

Exception Handling Keywords

try-catch

try {
    WebElement loginBtn = driver.findElement(By.id("login"));
    loginBtn.click();
} catch (NoSuchElementException e) {
    logger.error("Login button not found: " + e.getMessage());
    takeScreenshot("login_failure");
    throw e;  // re-throw to fail the test
}

Multiple catch blocks — order matters: Most specific first, most general last.

try {
    driver.findElement(By.id("submit")).click();
} catch (StaleElementReferenceException e) {
    // handle stale
} catch (NoSuchElementException e) {
    // handle not found
} catch (WebDriverException e) {
    // handle any other WebDriver issue
}

finally

Always executes — even if exception occurs or return statement is hit. Used for resource cleanup.

WebDriver driver = null;
try {
    driver = new ChromeDriver();
    // test logic
} catch (Exception e) {
    logger.error("Test failed", e);
} finally {
    if (driver != null) {
        driver.quit();  // ALWAYS close browser
    }
}

throw

Explicitly throw an exception from your code.

public void login(String user, String pass) {
    if (user == null || user.isEmpty()) {
        throw new TestDataException("Username cannot be empty");
    }
    // proceed with login
}

throws

Declares that a method may throw checked exceptions — caller must handle.

public Map<String, String> loadConfig(String path) throws IOException {
    Properties prop = new Properties();
    prop.load(new FileInputStream(path));
    // convert to Map and return
}

try-with-resources (Java 7+)

Auto-closes resources implementing AutoCloseable. No finally needed.

// Auto-close file stream
try (FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream("config.properties")) {
    Properties prop = new Properties();
    prop.load(fis);
}

// Auto-close WebDriver (if WebDriver implements AutoCloseable — it does in Selenium 4+)
try (WebDriver driver = new ChromeDriver()) {
    driver.get("https://example.com");
    // test logic — driver.quit() called automatically
}

Custom Exceptions for Frameworks

Custom exceptions make framework errors self-documenting and catchable at the right level.

// Base framework exception
public class FrameworkException extends RuntimeException {
    public FrameworkException(String message) {
        super(message);
    }
    public FrameworkException(String message, Throwable cause) {
        super(message, cause);
    }
}

// Specific exceptions
public class PageNotFoundException extends FrameworkException {
    public PageNotFoundException(String pageName) {
        super("Page not loaded: " + pageName);
    }
}

public class ConfigException extends FrameworkException {
    public ConfigException(String key) {
        super("Config key not found: " + key);
    }
}

public class TestDataException extends FrameworkException {
    public TestDataException(String message) {
        super("Test data error: " + message);
    }
}
When to create custom exceptions in automation:
  • Config file missing a required key → ConfigException
  • Page object isLoaded() returns false → PageNotFoundException
  • Data provider returns empty/invalid data → TestDataException
  • Wrapping Selenium exceptions with business context → FrameworkException

Selenium Exceptions — Deep Dive

NoSuchElementException

AspectDetail
WhatElement not found in DOM
WhenLocator is wrong, element not yet loaded, element removed
Code causing itdriver.findElement(By.id("nonexistent"))
FixAdd explicit wait, verify locator in DevTools, check iframe context
PreventionUse Page Objects with waits built in; never raw findElement in tests

TimeoutException

AspectDetail
WhatExplicit wait condition not met within timeout
WhenElement takes too long to appear/clickable
Code causing itwait.until(ExpectedConditions.visibilityOfElementLocated(By.id("slow-load")))
FixIncrease timeout for slow pages, verify element exists, check for loading spinners
PreventionConfigure reasonable default timeouts in framework config

StaleElementReferenceException

AspectDetail
WhatElement reference is no longer attached to DOM
WhenPage refresh, AJAX update, navigation after finding element
Code causing itFind element → page refreshes → click same reference
FixRe-find element before interaction (retry pattern)
PreventionWrap actions in retry utility; use fresh findElement for each action
 
// Re-find pattern to handle stale elements
public void safeClick(By locator) {
    for (int i = 0; i < 3; i++) {
        try {
            driver.findElement(locator).click();
            return;
        } catch (StaleElementReferenceException e) {
            // retry — re-find on next iteration
        }
    }
    throw new FrameworkException("Failed to click after 3 retries: " + locator);
}

ElementClickInterceptedException

AspectDetail
WhatAnother element is overlaying the target
WhenCookie banner, modal popup, sticky header covers button
Code causing itdriver.findElement(By.id("submit")).click() with overlay present
FixWait for overlay to disappear, scroll into view, JavaScript click
PreventionBasePage dismisses popups in navigateTo() before any action
 
// JavaScript click fallback
JavascriptExecutor js = (JavascriptExecutor) driver;
js.executeScript("arguments[0].click();", element);

ElementNotInteractableException

AspectDetail
WhatElement exists but cannot be interacted with
WhenHidden (display:none), disabled, zero size, off-screen
FixScroll into view, wait for enabled state, use JS for hidden inputs
PreventionWait for elementToBeClickable not just presenceOfElementLocated

WebDriverException

AspectDetail
WhatGeneric WebDriver failure
WhenBrowser crash, driver-browser version mismatch, network issue
FixUse Selenium Manager (auto driver management), restart browser
PreventionLet Selenium 4+ manage drivers; don't hardcode driver paths

NoSuchWindowException

AspectDetail
WhatTarget window/tab no longer exists
WhenWindow closed programmatically or by application
FixValidate window handles before switch: driver.getWindowHandles()
PreventionStore original window handle in @BeforeMethod, validate before switch

NoSuchFrameException

AspectDetail
WhatFrame/iframe not found
WhenWrong frame name/index, frame not yet loaded
FixWait for frame, verify with DevTools, use driver.switchTo().parentFrame() to reset
PreventionAlways switch back to default content after frame operations

InvalidSelectorException

AspectDetail
WhatMalformed XPath or CSS selector
WhenSyntax error in locator string
Code causing itBy.xpath("//div[@id='test'") — missing closing bracket
FixValidate selector in browser DevTools console first
PreventionStore locators as constants; code review locator syntax

REST Assured Exceptions

JsonPathException

What: Invalid JSON path expression or path doesn't exist in response.

// ❌ Path doesn't exist
String name = response.jsonPath().getString("data.user.name");
// Fix: validate response structure first
assertEquals(response.getStatusCode(), 200);
String name = response.jsonPath().getString("data.user.name");

AssertionError

What: REST Assured assertion failed (status code, body, header mismatch).

response.then()
    .statusCode(200)
    .body("data.id", equalTo(123));  // AssertionError if id != 123

Exception Handling Best Practices for Frameworks

  1. Catch specific, not generic — catch NoSuchElementException, not Exception
  2. Always log before re-throwing — include context (page name, locator, test name)
  3. Take screenshot on failure — in catch block or TestNG listener
  4. Use custom exceptions — wrap Selenium exceptions with business meaning
  5. Never swallow exceptions — empty catch blocks hide failures
  6. Clean up in finally or @AfterMethod — quit driver, close connections
  7. try-with-resources — for file streams, readers, WebDriver (Selenium 4+)
  8. Retry for transient failures — stale element, intermittent timeout
  9. Fail fast for config errors — throw ConfigException at startup, not mid-test
  10. Use TestNG listeners — centralized exception handling, reporting, screenshots

Interview Q&A — Section 7 (15+ Questions)

Q: What is the difference between throw and throws?

A: throw explicitly creates and throws an exception instance inside a method. throws declares in the method signature that checked exceptions may propagate to the caller.

Q: Can we have try without catch?

A: Yes — try with finally only, or try-with-resources (Java 7+). Both are valid.

Q: Does finally always execute?

A: Almost always. Exceptions: System.exit(), JVM crash, infinite loop in try, daemon thread killed.

Q: What happens if catch and finally both throw exceptions?

A: The exception from finally suppresses the one from catch. The catch exception is added as suppressed (Java 7+).

Q: Why are Selenium exceptions unchecked?

A: They extend RuntimeException. Selenium doesn't force you to handle them at compile time — you handle them at the framework design level with waits and retry utilities.

Q: How do you handle StaleElementReferenceException in a framework?

A: Implement a retry wrapper in BasePage that re-finds the element and retries the action up to N times before failing.

Q: What is exception chaining?

A: Wrapping one exception inside another: throw new FrameworkException("Login failed", originalException). Preserves the root cause stack trace.

Q: Can we catch Error?

A: Technically yes, but you shouldn't. Errors (OutOfMemoryError, StackOverflowError) indicate serious JVM problems that tests cannot recover from.

Q: What is multi-catch (Java 7+)?

A: catch (NoSuchElementException | TimeoutException e) — single catch block for multiple exception types.

Q: How do you handle exceptions in TestNG?

A: (1) try-catch in test/page methods, (2) @Test(expectedExceptions=...) for negative tests, (3) ITestListener.onTestFailure() for screenshots/reports, (4) @Test(retryAnalyzer=...) for flaky test retry.

Q: What is the difference between Error and Exception?

A: Error = serious JVM problems (not recoverable). Exception = conditions apps can handle (file not found, element not found).

Q: When would you use checked exceptions in automation?

A: Reading config files (IOException), database connections (SQLException), parsing XML test data. Wrap in custom ConfigException or TestDataException for cleaner framework API.

Q: How do you log exceptions properly?

A: logger.error("Failed to click login button on page: {}", pageName, exception) — include context message AND pass the exception object for full stack trace.

Q: What is try-with-resources?

A: Java 7 feature that auto-closes AutoCloseable resources. Compiler generates finally block with close(). Use for file readers, DB connections, WebDriver.

Q: How do you design exception handling in a Page Object Model?

A: BasePage provides safe action methods (safeClick, safeSendKeys) with built-in waits and retry. Page-specific methods throw custom exceptions (PageNotFoundException). Tests never catch Selenium exceptions directly.

Q: Can finally block change the return value?

A: Yes — if finally has a return statement, it overrides try/catch return value. Avoid return in finally — it's a bad practice.

Section 8: Access Modifiers

Access modifiers control visibility of classes, methods, and variables. In automation frameworks, choosing the right modifier is a design decision that affects maintainability, encapsulation, and extensibility of Page Objects, utilities, and base classes.

Access Modifier Table

ModifierSame ClassSame PackageSubclassOther Package
private✅ Yes❌ No❌ No❌ No
default (no modifier)✅ Yes✅ Yes❌ No❌ No
protected✅ Yes✅ Yes✅ Yes❌ No
public✅ Yes✅ Yes✅ Yes✅ Yes

Framework Usage for Each Modifier

private

Internal implementation details — hidden from outside the class.

  • WebDriver driver instance in Page Object
  • Internal helper methods (e.g., private void waitForAjax())
  • Locator fields: private By loginBtn = By.id("login");
  • Screenshot capture logic inside a page class
public class LoginPage {
    private WebDriver driver;                    // internal state
    private By usernameField = By.id("user");    // locators hidden
    private By passwordField = By.id("pass");

    private void enterCredentials(String u, String p) {  // internal helper
        driver.findElement(usernameField).sendKeys(u);
        driver.findElement(passwordField).sendKeys(p);
    }

    public void login(String u, String p) {      // public API
        enterCredentials(u, p);
        driver.findElement(By.id("submit")).click();
    }
}

default (package-private)

Visible within the same package only. Used for package-level utilities and internal test helpers.

// In package com.framework.pages — visible to all pages, not to tests
class PageHelper {
    void dismissCookieBanner(WebDriver driver) { /* ... */ }
}

protected

Accessible to subclasses — the backbone of BasePage/BaseTest inheritance.

public abstract class BasePage {
    protected WebDriver driver;
    protected WebDriverWait wait;

    protected BasePage(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
        this.wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(10));
    }

    protected void click(By locator) { /* shared click logic */ }
    protected String getText(By locator) { /* shared get text */ }

    protected abstract boolean isLoaded();  // force child implementation
}

public class LoginPage extends BasePage {
    public LoginPage(WebDriver driver) { super(driver); }

    @Override
    protected boolean isLoaded() {
        return driver.findElement(By.id("login-form")).isDisplayed();
    }
}

public

Accessible everywhere — the framework's API surface.

  • Page action methods: public void login(String user, String pass)
  • Test methods: @Test public void testLogin()
  • Utility methods: public static String getProperty(String key)
  • Constants: public static final String BASE_URL

Design Decision Table

WhatModifierWhy
WebDriver in DriverManagerprivate + public getterEncapsulate driver lifecycle; controlled access
Locators in Page ObjectsprivateHide implementation; change locator without breaking tests
Locators in extended pagesprotectedAllow subclass pages to reuse/override locators
Action methods in PagespublicTests call these — they're the page API
BaseTest setup/teardownprotectedChild test classes inherit but external code doesn't access
Utility methodspublic staticCalled from anywhere without instantiation
Constantspublic static finalGlobal access, immutable
Internal wait helpersprivateImplementation detail of the page class

Common Mistakes

  • Making everything public — breaks encapsulation; locators and helpers should be private/protected
  • Using default accidentally — forgetting a modifier makes it package-private; test classes in a different package can't access it
  • private test methods — TestNG needs public test methods (or at least non-private)
  • protected locators when private suffices — only use protected if subclasses genuinely need them
  • public WebDriver field — always private with a getter, or pass via constructor

Interview Q&A — Section 8 (10+ Questions)

Q: What is the most restrictive access modifier?

A: private — accessible only within the same class.

Q: Can a top-level class be private?

A: No. Top-level classes can only be public or package-private (default). private applies to inner/nested classes.

Q: Why are locators private in Page Objects?

A: Encapsulation — if a locator changes, you update one private field. Tests use public action methods and never reference locators directly.

Q: protected vs default — what's the difference?

A: Both are accessible in the same package. protected additionally allows access from subclasses in other packages. Critical for BasePage in com.framework.base extended by pages in com.framework.pages.

Q: Can constructors be private?

A: Yes — used in Singleton pattern (e.g., DriverManager) and utility classes to prevent instantiation.

Q: What access modifier for TestNG @Test methods?

A: public (convention) or package-private. TestNG can invoke non-private methods. Never private.

Q: How do access modifiers relate to encapsulation?

A: Encapsulation = hide internal state, expose public API. Access modifiers enforce it: private fields, public getters/setters, protected for inheritance hierarchy.

Q: Can an interface method be protected?

A: Pre-Java 9: all interface methods are implicitly public. Java 9+ allows private methods in interfaces.

Q: Why use protected for BaseTest @BeforeMethod?

A: So child test classes in the same or different package can override setup/teardown while keeping it hidden from unrelated classes.

Q: What happens if DriverManager.driver is public?

A: Any class can directly modify the driver reference — breaks encapsulation, causes thread-safety issues in parallel execution, makes debugging harder.

Q: Can we reduce visibility when overriding a method?

A: No. Overridden method cannot have a more restrictive modifier. If parent method is protected, override must be protected or public.

Section 9: Static Keyword

The static keyword belongs to the class, not to any instance. In automation frameworks, static is used for constants, utility methods, and config loading — but misused static WebDriver is the #1 cause of parallel execution failures.

Static Variable

Shared across ALL instances of the class — one copy in memory, class-level scope.

public class FrameworkConfig {
    public static final String BASE_URL = "https://staging.example.com";
    public static final int DEFAULT_TIMEOUT = 10;
    public static final String BROWSER = "chrome";

    // Counter shared across all test instances
    public static int testsExecuted = 0;
}
⚠️ DANGER: Static WebDriver 
public class DriverFactory {
    public static WebDriver driver;  // ❌ NEVER DO THIS
}

In parallel TestNG execution, ALL threads share the same static driver. Thread 1 opens Chrome, Thread 2 overwrites it with Firefox, Thread 1's test fails with wrong browser or stale session.

  PARALLEL EXECUTION WITH static WebDriver (BROKEN):

  Thread-1 (Test A)          Thread-2 (Test B)
       |                          |
       v                          v
  driver = Chrome            driver = Firefox  ← overwrites!
       |                          |
  driver.get("/login")       driver.get("/cart")
       |                          |
  ❌ FAILS — driver now       ✅ Works on Firefox
     points to Firefox        but broke Test A

  SHARED static driver ──→ ONE WebDriver for ALL threads

Solution: Use ThreadLocal<WebDriver> (covered in Section 14) — each thread gets its own driver instance.

Static Method

Called without creating an object. Cannot access instance variables or use this/super.

public class ConfigReader {
    private static Properties prop = new Properties();

    public static String getProperty(String key) {
        return prop.getProperty(key);
        // Cannot access instance fields here
    }

    public static WebDriver createDriver(String browser) {
        switch (browser.toLowerCase()) {
            case "chrome":  return new ChromeDriver();
            case "firefox": return new FirefoxDriver();
            default:        throw new IllegalArgumentException("Unknown browser: " + browser);
        }
    }
}

// Usage — no object needed
String url = ConfigReader.getProperty("base.url");
WebDriver driver = ConfigReader.createDriver("chrome");

Automation usage:

  • Utility methods: ExcelUtils.readSheet(), RandomDataGenerator.generateEmail()
  • Factory methods: DriverFactory.createDriver()
  • Config readers: ConfigReader.getProperty()

Static Block

Executes once when the class is first loaded by JVM — before any static method or object creation.

public class ConfigReader {
    private static Properties prop;

    static {
        prop = new Properties();
        try (FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream("src/test/resources/config.properties")) {
            prop.load(fis);
            System.out.println("Config loaded successfully");
        } catch (IOException e) {
            throw new ConfigException("Failed to load config.properties", e);
        }
    }

    public static String getProperty(String key) {
        return prop.getProperty(key);
    }
}

Automation usage: Load config once at class load time — avoids re-reading the file for every test method.

Static Import

import static org.testng.Assert.*;
import static org.openqa.selenium.By.*;

// Now use directly without class prefix
assertEquals(actual, expected);
assertTrue(condition);
driver.findElement(id("login"));
driver.findElement(xpath("//button[@type='submit']"));

Static in Framework Design

Constants Class

public final class Constants {
    private Constants() {}  // prevent instantiation

    public static final String BASE_URL = "https://example.com";
    public static final int TIMEOUT = 10;
    public static final String SCREENSHOT_DIR = "screenshots/";
}

Utility Class

public final class StringUtils {
    private StringUtils() {}  // no constructor — all static

    public static String generateRandomEmail() {
        return "test" + System.currentTimeMillis() + "@mail.com";
    }

    public static boolean isEmpty(String s) {
        return s == null || s.trim().isEmpty();
    }
}

Singleton Pattern

public class ReportManager {
    private static ReportManager instance;

    private ReportManager() {}  // private constructor

    public static ReportManager getInstance() {
        if (instance == null) {
            instance = new ReportManager();
        }
        return instance;
    }
}

Static vs Instance — Decision Table

FeatureStaticInstance (Non-static)
Belongs toClassObject (instance)
MemoryOne copyOne copy per object
AccessClassName.method()object.method()
Can access instance vars?NoYes
Can use this/super?NoYes
Override?No (hidden, not overridden)Yes (polymorphism)
Framework useUtils, constants, configPage Objects, test classes
Thread safetyShared state — dangerousEach instance isolated

Interview Q&A — Section 9 (12+ Questions)

Q: Can we override static methods?

A: No — static methods are hidden, not overridden. Method resolution is compile-time (based on reference type), not runtime polymorphism.

Q: Why is static WebDriver bad for parallel execution?

A: Static = one shared instance across all threads. Parallel tests overwrite each other's driver, causing random failures. Use ThreadLocal instead.

Q: Can a class be static?

A: Top-level classes cannot be static. Only nested classes can be declared static — they don't need an outer class instance.

Q: When does static block execute?

A: Once, when the class is first loaded by ClassLoader — before main(), before any static method call, before first object creation.

Q: Can static methods be synchronized?

A: Yes — locks on the Class object. Used in Singleton double-checked locking. Rare in automation.

Q: What is static variable default value?

A: Default initialized by JVM: 0 for numbers, false for boolean, null for objects. Instance variables get defaults too, but static has one shared copy.

Q: Why do utility classes have private constructors?

A: To prevent instantiation — all methods are static, so creating an object is meaningless. Example: private ConfigReader() {}.

Q: Can we access static variable through object reference?

A: Yes syntactically (obj.staticVar) but it's bad practice. Always use ClassName.staticVar — clearer intent.

Q: Difference between static import and normal import?

A: Normal import brings class name into scope. Static import brings static members — use assertEquals() instead of Assert.assertEquals().

Q: Can main method access non-static variables?

A: No directly — main is static, non-static variables belong to objects. Must create an object first: new MyClass().instanceMethod().

Q: How is static used in TestNG assertions?

A: All Assert methods are static: Assert.assertEquals(actual, expected). With static import: assertEquals(actual, expected).

Q: Static variable vs instance variable — memory?

A: Static: one copy in method area (metaspace). Instance: one copy per object on the heap. Static survives until class is unloaded.

Q: Can abstract class have static methods?

A: Yes — static methods in abstract classes are common for factory methods: public static LoginPage create(WebDriver driver).

Section 10: Interface vs Abstract Class

Interfaces and abstract classes are the foundation of framework architecture — BasePage, WebDriver, listener contracts, and report interfaces all rely on choosing the right abstraction.

Interface

A 100% contract (pre-Java 8). Defines what a class must do, not how. A class can implement multiple interfaces.

public interface IPageActions {
    void navigateTo();
    boolean isLoaded();
    String getPageTitle();
}

public interface IValidatable {
    void validateRequiredFields();
    List<String> getValidationErrors();
}

// Multiple interfaces
public class LoginPage implements IPageActions, IValidatable {
    @Override
    public void navigateTo() { /* ... */ }

    @Override
    public boolean isLoaded() { /* ... */ }

    @Override
    public String getPageTitle() { return driver.getTitle(); }

    @Override
    public void validateRequiredFields() { /* ... */ }

    @Override
    public List<String> getValidationErrors() { /* ... */ }
}

Default Methods (Java 8+)

Add behavior to interfaces without breaking existing implementations.

public interface IPageActions {
    void navigateTo();
    boolean isLoaded();

    // Default method — optional override
    default void waitForPageLoad() {
        new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(10))
            .until(d -> ((JavascriptExecutor) d)
                .executeScript("return document.readyState").equals("complete"));
    }
}

Static Methods in Interface

public interface BrowserUtils {
    static boolean isBrowserOpen(WebDriver driver) {
        try {
            driver.getTitle();
            return true;
        } catch (Exception e) {
            return false;
        }
    }
}

// Call without implementation
boolean open = BrowserUtils.isBrowserOpen(driver);

Functional Interface

@FunctionalInterface
public interface ElementAction {
    void perform(WebElement element);
    // Exactly ONE abstract method — enables lambdas
}

// Usage with lambda
ElementAction click = el -> el.click();
ElementAction getText = el -> System.out.println(el.getText());

elements.forEach(el -> click.perform(el));

Selenium Example: WebDriver Interface

WebDriver driver = new ChromeDriver();    // Interface reference
driver = new FirefoxDriver();           // Different implementation
driver = new EdgeDriver();              // Same interface, different browser

// WebDriver is an interface — ChromeDriver, FirefoxDriver implement it
// SearchContext, TakesScreenshot, JavascriptExecutor are sub-interfaces

Framework Examples

  • IPageActions — contract for all page objects
  • IConfigurable — contract for config-driven components
  • IReportable — contract for test reporting listeners

Abstract Class

Partial implementation — mix of concrete methods (shared code) and abstract methods (force subclass implementation). Can have constructors, instance variables, any access modifier.

public abstract class BasePage {
    protected WebDriver driver;
    protected WebDriverWait wait;

    // Constructor — YES, abstract classes CAN have constructors
    protected BasePage(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
        this.wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(10));
    }

    // Concrete method — shared by ALL pages
    public void click(By locator) {
        wait.until(ExpectedConditions.elementToBeClickable(locator)).click();
    }

    protected void sendKeys(By locator, String text) {
        wait.until(ExpectedConditions.visibilityOfElementLocated(locator)).sendKeys(text);
    }

    protected String getText(By locator) {
        return wait.until(ExpectedConditions.visibilityOfElementLocated(locator)).getText();
    }

    // Abstract method — force each page to implement
    public abstract boolean isLoaded();
    public abstract String getPageUrl();
}

Comparison Table

FeatureInterfaceAbstract Class
MethodsAbstract + default + staticAbstract + concrete
Variablespublic static final onlyAny type (instance, static)
ConstructorNoYes
Multiple inheritanceYes (implements multiple)No (extends one only)
Access modifiersPublic (Java 9+ allows private)Any (private, protected, public)
Instance variablesNot allowed (only constants)Allowed (driver, wait, etc.)
When to useContract across unrelated classesBase class with shared code + forced overrides
Keywordimplementsextends
Real framework exampleIPageActions, WebDriverBasePage, BaseTest
Can have main method?Yes (static method)Yes (static or instance)
PolymorphismYes — interface referenceYes — abstract class reference
Design roleCAN-DO relationship (capability)IS-A relationship (inheritance)

Real Framework Decisions

  • BasePage → ABSTRACT CLASS — has shared code (click, sendKeys, wait) + forces isLoaded() implementation
  • IPageActions → INTERFACE — pure contract, no shared state, multiple unrelated classes can implement
  • WebDriver → INTERFACE — Selenium's core design; ChromeDriver, FirefoxDriver, RemoteWebDriver all implement it
  • BaseTest → ABSTRACT CLASS — shared @BeforeMethod/@AfterMethod + abstract test configuration
  • ITestListener → INTERFACE — TestNG listener contract

Design Pattern: Interface + Abstract Class Combination

The most powerful framework pattern — interface defines the contract, abstract class provides shared implementation, concrete class completes it.

// 1. Interface — the contract
public interface IPageActions {
    void navigateTo();
    boolean isLoaded();
    void validatePage();
}

// 2. Abstract class — shared implementation
public abstract class BasePage implements IPageActions {
    protected WebDriver driver;
    protected WebDriverWait wait;

    protected BasePage(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
        this.wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(10));
    }

    protected void click(By locator) {
        wait.until(ExpectedConditions.elementToBeClickable(locator)).click();
    }

    protected void type(By locator, String text) {
        WebElement el = wait.until(ExpectedConditions.visibilityOfElementLocated(locator));
        el.clear();
        el.sendKeys(text);
    }

    // Default implementation — can be overridden
    @Override
    public void validatePage() {
        if (!isLoaded()) {
            throw new PageNotFoundException(this.getClass().getSimpleName());
        }
    }

    // Force subclass to implement
    @Override
    public abstract boolean isLoaded();
}

// 3. Concrete class — page-specific
public class LoginPage extends BasePage {
    private By usernameField = By.id("username");
    private By passwordField = By.id("password");
    private By loginButton   = By.id("login-btn");

    public LoginPage(WebDriver driver) {
        super(driver);
    }

    @Override
    public void navigateTo() {
        driver.get(ConfigReader.getProperty("base.url") + "/login");
        validatePage();
    }

    @Override
    public boolean isLoaded() {
        return driver.findElement(loginButton).isDisplayed();
    }

    public void login(String username, String password) {
        type(usernameField, username);
        type(passwordField, password);
        click(loginButton);
    }
}

When to Choose Which?

  Decision Flow:

  Need shared state (driver, wait)?
       |
      YES ──→ ABSTRACT CLASS (BasePage)
       |
      NO
       |
  Need shared method implementations?
       |
      YES ──→ ABSTRACT CLASS or Interface with default methods
       |
      NO
       |
  Need multiple inheritance?
       |
      YES ──→ INTERFACE (implements A, B, C)
       |
      NO
       |
  Define a contract/capability?
       |
      YES ──→ INTERFACE (IPageActions)
       |
      NO
       |
  IS-A relationship with shared code?
       |
      YES ──→ ABSTRACT CLASS (BaseTest extends...)

Interview Q&A — Section 10 (12+ Questions)

Q: Can an interface extend another interface?

A: Yes — interface inheritance is supported. interface IAdvancedActions extends IPageActions, IValidatable.

Q: Can an abstract class implement an interface?

A: Yes — and it can leave interface methods abstract. abstract class BasePage implements IPageActions — provides some implementations, leaves rest abstract.

Q: Can we create an object of an abstract class?

A: No — must subclass and implement all abstract methods. BasePage page = new BasePage(driver) is a compile error.

Q: Can an interface have a constructor?

A: No — interfaces cannot have constructors. Only abstract and concrete classes can.

Q: Why is WebDriver an interface and not an abstract class?

A: Selenium supports many browsers (Chrome, Firefox, Edge, Safari, Remote). Interface allows each browser driver to implement independently without sharing a common base class hierarchy. Also, WebDriver extends multiple interfaces: SearchContext, TakesScreenshot.

Q: What is a marker interface?

A: Empty interface with no methods — marks a capability. Serializable, Cloneable. In automation, you might create IScreenshotable as a marker for pages that support screenshot capture.

Q: Can an abstract class be final?

A: No — abstract and final are contradictory. Abstract means "must be extended"; final means "cannot be extended."

Q: Interface vs abstract class — Java 8 changes?

A: Java 8 added default and static methods to interfaces, blurring the line. But interfaces still can't have instance variables or constructors. Use abstract class when you need state (driver, wait).

Q: How does BasePage benefit from being abstract?

A: (1) Provides shared methods (click, type, wait) — DRY principle. (2) Forces each page to implement isLoaded() — compile-time enforcement. (3) Cannot be instantiated directly — must create specific pages.

Q: Can a concrete class extend an abstract class without implementing all abstract methods?

A: Only if the concrete class is also declared abstract. Otherwise, compile error — must implement all abstract methods.

Q: What is the diamond problem and how does Java handle it?

A: Multiple inheritance causes ambiguity if two interfaces have same default method. Java resolves by requiring explicit override: @Override public void method() { InterfaceA.super.method(); }.

Q: Why implement IPageActions interface if BasePage already has the methods?

A: Interface enables polymorphism — you can pass any IPageActions to a method without knowing the concrete page class. Enables generic page validation: void verifyPage(IPageActions page) { assertTrue(page.isLoaded()); }.

Q: Functional interface — why important in automation?

A: Enables lambda expressions for cleaner code: elements.forEach(el -> el.click()), custom wait conditions: wait.until(driver -> driver.findElement(By.id("x")).isDisplayed()), and callback patterns in retry utilities.

Section 11: File Handling

Why File Handling in Automation?

In test automation frameworks, almost every layer touches files. Configuration drives browser selection, URLs, and timeouts. Test data lives in Excel, JSON, or CSV. Reports and logs capture execution results. Screenshots attach to failure reports. A robust framework abstracts file I/O behind utility classes so tests stay clean and maintainable.

Framework Rule: Never hardcode paths or read files directly inside test methods. Centralize all file access in dedicated reader/writer utilities under a utils or config package.

Common File Types in Automation

  • Properties — environment config (browser, URL, timeouts)
  • JSON — API payloads, REST test data, schema validation
  • Excel — data-driven UI tests (TestNG DataProvider)
  • CSV — lightweight test data exports
  • Text/Log — log analysis, baseline comparisons

Properties File — Most Used in Automation

The .properties file is the backbone of framework configuration. Key-value pairs are simple, human-readable, and require no external library.

config.properties Example

# config.properties
browser=chrome
url=https://qa.myapp.com
timeout=30
environment=qa
headless=false
screenshot.on.failure=true

Complete ConfigReader Utility (Singleton Pattern)

import java.io.FileInputStream;
import java.io.IOException;
import java.util.Properties;

public class ConfigReader {

    private static Properties prop;

    static {
        try {
            prop = new Properties();
            prop.load(new FileInputStream("src/test/resources/config/config.properties"));
        } catch (IOException e) {
            throw new RuntimeException("Failed to load config.properties", e);
        }
    }

    public static String get(String key) {
        return prop.getProperty(key);
    }

    public static String get(String key, String defaultValue) {
        return prop.getProperty(key, defaultValue);
    }

    public static int getInt(String key) {
        return Integer.parseInt(prop.getProperty(key));
    }

    public static boolean getBoolean(String key) {
        return Boolean.parseBoolean(prop.getProperty(key));
    }
}

Usage in BaseTest:

public class BaseTest {
    protected WebDriver driver;

    @BeforeMethod
    public void setup() {
        String browser = ConfigReader.get("browser");
        String url = ConfigReader.get("url");
        driver = DriverFactory.createDriver(browser);
        driver.get(url);
    }
}

Environment-Specific Configs

Maintain separate property files per environment and load dynamically:

  • qa.properties — QA URLs, test credentials
  • staging.properties — pre-production settings
  • prod.properties — production smoke test config (read-only)
public class ConfigReader {

    private static Properties prop;

    static {
        String env = System.getProperty("env", System.getenv("ENV"));
        if (env == null) env = "qa";

        String filePath = "src/test/resources/config/" + env + ".properties";
        try {
            prop = new Properties();
            prop.load(new FileInputStream(filePath));
        } catch (IOException e) {
            throw new RuntimeException("Failed to load: " + filePath, e);
        }
    }

    public static String get(String key) {
        return prop.getProperty(key);
    }
}

Run with: mvn test -Denv=staging or set ENV=staging in CI pipeline.

JSON File Handling

JSON is standard for API automation — request bodies, response validation, and structured test data. Use Jackson (ObjectMapper) in Maven/Gradle projects.

Reading Test Data from JSON

// testdata/login_users.json
// [
//   {"username": "admin", "password": "admin123", "expectedUrl": "/dashboard"},
//   {"username": "guest", "password": "guest", "expectedUrl": "/home"}
// ]

import com.fasterxml.jackson.core.type.TypeReference;
import com.fasterxml.jackson.databind.ObjectMapper;
import java.io.File;
import java.util.List;

public class JsonDataReader {

    private static final ObjectMapper mapper = new ObjectMapper();

    public static <T> T read(String filePath, Class<T> clazz) {
        try {
            return mapper.readValue(new File(filePath), clazz);
        } catch (Exception e) {
            throw new RuntimeException("Failed to read JSON: " + filePath, e);
        }
    }

    public static <T> List<T> readList(String filePath, Class<T> clazz) {
        try {
            return mapper.readValue(new File(filePath),
                mapper.getTypeFactory().constructCollectionType(List.class, clazz));
        } catch (Exception e) {
            throw new RuntimeException("Failed to read JSON list: " + filePath, e);
        }
    }

    public static String toJson(Object obj) {
        try {
            return mapper.writeValueAsString(obj);
        } catch (Exception e) {
            throw new RuntimeException("Failed to serialize object", e);
        }
    }
}

API Request Body from JSON File

// payloads/create_user.json
// {"name": "John Doe", "email": "john@test.com", "role": "admin"}

import io.restassured.RestAssured;
import static io.restassured.RestAssured.*;

public class UserApiTest {

    @Test
    public void createUser() {
        String payload = JsonDataReader.read(
            "src/test/resources/payloads/create_user.json", String.class);

        // Or read as Map/Object and serialize
        Map<String, Object> body = JsonDataReader.read(
            "src/test/resources/payloads/create_user.json",
            new TypeReference<Map<String, Object>>() {});

        given()
            .contentType("application/json")
            .body(body)
        .when()
            .post("/api/users")
        .then()
            .statusCode(201);
    }
}

Excel File Handling (Apache POI)

Excel remains the most common format for business-authored test data. Apache POI provides XSSFWorkbook for .xlsx files.

Complete ExcelReader Class

import org.apache.poi.ss.usermodel.*;
import org.apache.poi.xssf.usermodel.XSSFWorkbook;
import java.io.FileInputStream;
import java.util.ArrayList;
import java.util.HashMap;
import java.util.List;
import java.util.Map;

public class ExcelReader {

    private String filePath;
    private String sheetName;

    public ExcelReader(String filePath, String sheetName) {
        this.filePath = filePath;
        this.sheetName = sheetName;
    }

    public int getRowCount() {
        try (FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream(filePath);
             Workbook workbook = new XSSFWorkbook(fis)) {
            Sheet sheet = workbook.getSheet(sheetName);
            return sheet.getLastRowNum();
        } catch (Exception e) {
            throw new RuntimeException(e);
        }
    }

    public String getCellData(int rowNum, int colNum) {
        try (FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream(filePath);
             Workbook workbook = new XSSFWorkbook(fis)) {
            Sheet sheet = workbook.getSheet(sheetName);
            Row row = sheet.getRow(rowNum);
            Cell cell = row.getCell(colNum);

            switch (cell.getCellType()) {
                case STRING:  return cell.getStringCellValue();
                case NUMERIC: return String.valueOf((int) cell.getNumericCellValue());
                case BOOLEAN: return String.valueOf(cell.getBooleanCellValue());
                default:      return "";
            }
        } catch (Exception e) {
            throw new RuntimeException(e);
        }
    }

    public Object[][] getTestData() {
        int rowCount = getRowCount();
        int colCount = getColumnCount();
        Object[][] data = new Object[rowCount][colCount];

        for (int i = 1; i <= rowCount; i++) { // skip header row 0
            for (int j = 0; j < colCount; j++) {
                data[i - 1][j] = getCellData(i, j);
            }
        }
        return data;
    }

    public List<Map<String, String>> getTestDataAsMaps() {
        List<Map<String, String>> rows = new ArrayList<>();
        int colCount = getColumnCount();

        // Build header map
        List<String> headers = new ArrayList<>();
        for (int j = 0; j < colCount; j++) {
            headers.add(getCellData(0, j));
        }

        for (int i = 1; i <= getRowCount(); i++) {
            Map<String, String> row = new HashMap<>();
            for (int j = 0; j < colCount; j++) {
                row.put(headers.get(j), getCellData(i, j));
            }
            rows.add(row);
        }
        return rows;
    }

    private int getColumnCount() {
        try (FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream(filePath);
             Workbook workbook = new XSSFWorkbook(fis)) {
            return workbook.getSheet(sheetName).getRow(0).getLastCellNum();
        } catch (Exception e) {
            throw new RuntimeException(e);
        }
    }
}

TestNG DataProvider Integration

import org.testng.annotations.DataProvider;
import org.testng.annotations.Test;

public class LoginTest {

    @DataProvider(name = "loginData")
    public Object[][] getLoginData() {
        ExcelReader reader = new ExcelReader(
            "src/test/resources/testdata/LoginData.xlsx", "Sheet1");
        return reader.getTestData();
    }

    @Test(dataProvider = "loginData")
    public void testLogin(String username, String password, String expectedResult) {
        LoginPage loginPage = new LoginPage(driver);
        loginPage.login(username, password);
        Assert.assertEquals(loginPage.getMessage(), expectedResult);
    }
}

CSV Handling (OpenCSV)

import com.opencsv.CSVReader;
import java.io.FileReader;
import java.util.ArrayList;
import java.util.List;

public class CsvReader {

    public static List<String[]> readAll(String filePath) {
        try (CSVReader reader = new CSVReader(new FileReader(filePath))) {
            List<String[]> rows = new ArrayList<>();
            String[] line;
            reader.readNext(); // skip header
            while ((line = reader.readNext()) != null) {
                rows.add(line);
            }
            return rows;
        } catch (Exception e) {
            throw new RuntimeException(e);
        }
    }
}

File Read/Write with Java NIO

import java.nio.file.*;
import java.util.List;
import java.io.*;

// Read all lines — good for small config/text files
List<String> lines = Files.readAllLines(Paths.get("logs/test.log"));

// Write lines
Files.write(Paths.get("reports/summary.txt"), List.of("Test: PASS", "Duration: 45s"));

// BufferedReader — large log files (memory efficient)
try (BufferedReader br = Files.newBufferedReader(Paths.get("logs/app.log"))) {
    String line;
    while ((line = br.readLine()) != null) {
        if (line.contains("ERROR")) {
            System.out.println(line);
        }
    }
}

File Handling Comparison

FormatLibraryUse CaseComplexity
Propertiesjava.util.PropertiesFramework config, env settingsLow
JSONJackson / GsonAPI payloads, structured test dataMedium
Excel (.xlsx)Apache POIBusiness-authored data-driven testsHigh
CSVOpenCSVSimple tabular data, exportsLow
Text/Logjava.nio.FilesLog analysis, baseline filesLow
XMLtestng.xml, JAXBTestNG suite config, legacy APIsMedium

Interview Q&A — File Handling

  1. Q: Why use properties files instead of hardcoding values?
    A: Separation of config from code; change environment without recompiling; CI can inject different configs per pipeline stage.
  2. Q: How do you load different configs for QA vs Prod?
    A: Pass -Denv=qa or read ENV environment variable; load corresponding {env}.properties file.
  3. Q: What is the Singleton pattern in ConfigReader?
    A: Static block loads properties once at class load time; single shared Properties instance across all tests.
  4. Q: Jackson vs Gson — which do you prefer?
    A: Jackson is more feature-rich (annotations, streaming); Gson is simpler. Most enterprise frameworks use Jackson.
  5. Q: How do you handle numeric cells in Excel?
    A: Check CellType.NUMERIC; cast or use DataFormatter to avoid decimal formatting issues.
  6. Q: Why skip row 0 in Excel DataProvider?
    A: Row 0 typically contains column headers, not test data.
  7. Q: How do you read JSON array into List of objects?
    A: Use ObjectMapper.readValue() with TypeReference<List<MyClass>> or constructCollectionType.
  8. Q: When to use CSV over Excel?
    A: Simple data, version-control friendly (text diffs), no POI dependency, faster parsing.
  9. Q: Files.readAllLines vs BufferedReader?
    A: readAllLines loads entire file into memory — fine for small files. BufferedReader streams line-by-line — required for large log files.
  10. Q: How do you write test results to a file?
    A: Use Files.write() with StandardOpenOption.APPEND for incremental logging, or a reporting library like ExtentReports.
  11. Q: Where should config files live in a Maven project?
    A: src/test/resources/config/ — available on classpath at runtime.
  12. Q: How do you handle file-not-found in framework utilities?
    A: Wrap in RuntimeException with descriptive message; fail fast during test setup rather than mid-test.

Section 12: Java 8 Features — Very Important for SDET Interviews

Why Java 8 Matters for Automation

Java 8 introduced lambda expressions, functional interfaces, and the Streams API — transforming how automation code is written. Explicit waits become one-liners. Element filtering replaces verbose loops. API response processing becomes declarative. Interviewers expect SDET candidates to fluently use these features.

Interview Tip: Be ready to rewrite a traditional for-loop as a Stream pipeline. This is the #1 Java 8 coding question in SDET interviews.

Lambda Expressions

Syntax: (params) -> expression or (params) -> { statements; }

Before Lambda vs After Lambda

// Example 1: Filtering displayed elements
// BEFORE
List<WebElement> visible = new ArrayList<>();
for (WebElement el : elements) {
    if (el.isDisplayed()) {
        visible.add(el);
    }
}

// AFTER
List<WebElement> visible = elements.stream()
    .filter(WebElement::isDisplayed)
    .collect(Collectors.toList());

// Example 2: Sorting elements by text
// BEFORE
Collections.sort(elements, new Comparator<WebElement>() {
    public int compare(WebElement e1, WebElement e2) {
        return e1.getText().compareTo(e2.getText());
    }
});

// AFTER
elements.sort((e1, e2) -> e1.getText().compareTo(e2.getText()));
// OR
elements.sort(Comparator.comparing(WebElement::getText));

// Example 3: Explicit wait
// BEFORE
wait.until(new ExpectedCondition<Boolean>() {
    public Boolean apply(WebDriver d) {
        return d.findElement(By.id("submit")).isDisplayed();
    }
});

// AFTER
wait.until(d -> d.findElement(By.id("submit")).isDisplayed());

Functional Interfaces

A functional interface has exactly one abstract method. Java 8 provides built-in interfaces in java.util.function.

InterfaceMethodInputOutputAutomation Example
Predicate<T>test(T)Tbooleane -> e.isEnabled() — filter clickable elements
Function<T,R>apply(T)TRWebElement::getText — extract text
Consumer<T>accept(T)Tvoidel -> el.click() — click all elements
Supplier<T>get()noneT() -> new ChromeDriver() — lazy driver creation
BiPredicate<T,U>test(T,U)T, Uboolean(el, text) -> el.getText().equals(text)
BiFunction<T,U,R>apply(T,U)T, UR(driver, locator) -> driver.findElement(locator)
BiConsumer<T,U>accept(T,U)T, Uvoid(el, value) -> el.sendKeys(value)
 
@FunctionalInterface
public interface CustomValidator {
    boolean validate(String input);
    // Only ONE abstract method allowed
}

Streams API — Most Important

Creating Streams

List<String> names = Arrays.asList("Alice", "Bob", "Charlie");
Stream<String> stream1 = names.stream();
Stream<String> stream2 = Stream.of("a", "b", "c");
Stream<int[]> stream3 = Arrays.stream(new int[]{1, 2, 3});

Intermediate Operations

List<WebElement> elements = driver.findElements(By.cssSelector(".item"));

// filter — keep matching elements
elements.stream().filter(WebElement::isDisplayed);

// map — transform each element
elements.stream().map(WebElement::getText);

// sorted — natural order or custom Comparator
elements.stream().sorted(Comparator.comparing(WebElement::getText));
elements.stream().sorted(Comparator.comparing(WebElement::getText).reversed());

// distinct — remove duplicates
testData.stream().distinct();

// limit — take first N
elements.stream().limit(5);

// peek — debug/logging (side effect)
elements.stream()
    .peek(e -> System.out.println("Processing: " + e.getText()))
    .filter(WebElement::isDisplayed)
    .collect(Collectors.toList());

// flatMap — flatten nested collections
List<List<String>> nested = Arrays.asList(
    Arrays.asList("a", "b"), Arrays.asList("c", "d"));
nested.stream()
    .flatMap(List::stream)
    .collect(Collectors.toList()); // [a, b, c, d]

Terminal Operations

// collect
List<String> texts = elements.stream()
    .map(WebElement::getText)
    .collect(Collectors.toList());

Set<String> unique = elements.stream()
    .map(WebElement::getText)
    .collect(Collectors.toSet());

String joined = elements.stream()
    .map(WebElement::getText)
    .collect(Collectors.joining(", "));

// forEach
elements.stream()
    .filter(WebElement::isEnabled)
    .forEach(WebElement::click);

// count
long visibleCount = elements.stream()
    .filter(WebElement::isDisplayed)
    .count();

// findFirst — returns Optional
Optional<WebElement> first = elements.stream()
    .filter(e -> e.getText().contains("Submit"))
    .findFirst();

// anyMatch, allMatch, noneMatch
boolean anyVisible = elements.stream().anyMatch(WebElement::isDisplayed);
boolean allEnabled = elements.stream().allMatch(WebElement::isEnabled);
boolean noneEmpty = elements.stream().noneMatch(e -> e.getText().isEmpty());

// reduce — combine elements
Optional<String> combined = elements.stream()
    .map(WebElement::getText)
    .reduce((a, b) -> a + ", " + b);

Collectors — Advanced

// groupingBy — group elements by property
Map<String, List<WebElement>> byTag = elements.stream()
    .collect(Collectors.groupingBy(e -> e.getTagName()));

// partitioningBy — split into two groups (true/false)
Map<Boolean, List<WebElement>> partitioned = elements.stream()
    .collect(Collectors.partitioningBy(WebElement::isDisplayed));

// counting per group
Map<String, Long> countByStatus = testResults.stream()
    .collect(Collectors.groupingBy(TestResult::getStatus, Collectors.counting()));

// summarizing statistics
IntSummaryStatistics stats = salaries.stream()
    .collect(Collectors.summarizingInt(Integer::intValue));
// stats.getAverage(), stats.getMax(), stats.getMin()

Automation Use Cases — Complete Code

1. Filter Visible Elements

List<WebElement> visible = driver.findElements(By.cssSelector(".menu-item"))
    .stream()
    .filter(WebElement::isDisplayed)
    .collect(Collectors.toList());

2. Extract Text from All Elements

List<String> labels = driver.findElements(By.cssSelector("label"))
    .stream()
    .map(WebElement::getText)
    .collect(Collectors.toList());

3. Find Element Containing Specific Text

Optional<WebElement> target = driver.findElements(By.cssSelector(".row"))
    .stream()
    .filter(e -> e.getText().contains("Order #12345"))
    .findFirst();

target.ifPresent(WebElement::click);

4. Remove Duplicates from Test Data

List<String> uniqueEmails = testEmails.stream()
    .distinct()
    .collect(Collectors.toList());

5. Extract All IDs from API Response

List<Integer> ids = response.jsonPath().getList("data")
    .stream()
    .map(item -> ((Map<String, Object>) item).get("id"))
    .map(id -> ((Number) id).intValue())
    .collect(Collectors.toList());

6. Sort Test Results by Status

List<TestResult> sorted = testResults.stream()
    .sorted(Comparator.comparing(TestResult::getStatus)
        .thenComparing(TestResult::getTestName))
    .collect(Collectors.toList());

Optional

// Creating Optional
Optional<String> opt1 = Optional.of("value");        // non-null only
Optional<String> opt2 = Optional.ofNullable(getValue()); // may be null
Optional<String> opt3 = Optional.empty();

// Using Optional — avoid NullPointerException
if (opt2.isPresent()) {
    System.out.println(opt2.get());
}

opt2.ifPresent(val -> System.out.println(val));

String result = opt2.orElse("default");
String result2 = opt2.orElseGet(() -> ConfigReader.get("fallback"));
String result3 = opt2.orElseThrow(() -> new RuntimeException("Missing config"));

// Automation: optional element handling
Optional<WebElement> errorMsg = driver.findElements(By.id("error"))
    .stream().findFirst();
errorMsg.ifPresent(el -> Assert.fail("Error displayed: " + el.getText()));

// Automation: optional config value
String timeout = Optional.ofNullable(ConfigReader.get("timeout"))
    .orElse("30");

Method References

// Static method reference
.map(String::valueOf)

// Instance method reference on specific object
driver.findElements(By.tagName("a")).forEach(element::click); // invalid — use WebElement::click

// Instance method reference on arbitrary object
.map(WebElement::getText)  // equivalent to e -> e.getText()

// Constructor reference
Supplier<List<String>> listSupplier = ArrayList::new;

Coding Questions

1. Filter Even Numbers from List

// Stream solution — O(n)
List<Integer> evens = numbers.stream()
    .filter(n -> n % 2 == 0)
    .collect(Collectors.toList());

// Traditional — O(n)
List<Integer> evens = new ArrayList<>();
for (int n : numbers) {
    if (n % 2 == 0) evens.add(n);
}

2. Find Duplicates in List

// Stream solution — O(n)
List<String> duplicates = list.stream()
    .collect(Collectors.groupingBy(e -> e, Collectors.counting()))
    .entrySet().stream()
    .filter(e -> e.getValue() > 1)
    .map(Map.Entry::getKey)
    .collect(Collectors.toList());

// Traditional — O(n²) with nested loops, O(n) with HashSet
Set<String> seen = new HashSet<>();
Set<String> dups = new HashSet<>();
for (String s : list) {
    if (!seen.add(s)) dups.add(s);
}

3. Sort Employees by Salary

// Stream solution — O(n log n)
List<Employee> sorted = employees.stream()
    .sorted(Comparator.comparing(Employee::getSalary).reversed())
    .collect(Collectors.toList());

// Traditional — O(n log n)
Collections.sort(employees, (e1, e2) -> e2.getSalary() - e1.getSalary());

4. Count Occurrences of Each Word

// Stream solution — O(n)
Map<String, Long> wordCount = words.stream()
    .collect(Collectors.groupingBy(w -> w, Collectors.counting()));

// Traditional — O(n)
Map<String, Integer> wordCount = new HashMap<>();
for (String w : words) {
    wordCount.merge(w, 1, Integer::sum);
}

5. Find Highest Salary

// Stream solution — O(n)
Optional<Employee> highest = employees.stream()
    .max(Comparator.comparing(Employee::getSalary));

// Traditional — O(n)
Employee highest = employees.get(0);
for (Employee e : employees) {
    if (e.getSalary() > highest.getSalary()) highest = e;
}

Interview Q&A — Java 8

  1. Q: What is a lambda expression?
    A: Anonymous function implementing a functional interface. Syntax: (params) -> body.
  2. Q: Difference between intermediate and terminal stream operations?
    A: Intermediate ops (filter, map) return a Stream and are lazy. Terminal ops (collect, forEach) produce a result and trigger execution.
  3. Q: Is Stream reusable?
    A: No. Once a terminal operation is called, the stream is consumed. Create a new stream for another pipeline.
  4. Q: parallelStream() vs stream()?
    A: parallelStream uses ForkJoinPool for concurrent processing. Use for large datasets with CPU-bound operations; avoid with I/O-bound tasks like Selenium.
  5. Q: What is Optional and why use it?
    A: Container that may or may not contain a value. Prevents NullPointerException; forces explicit null handling.
  6. Q: map() vs flatMap()?
    A: map transforms 1-to-1. flatMap transforms 1-to-many and flattens the result (e.g., nested lists to single list).
  7. Q: What is a method reference?
    A: Shorthand for lambda calling an existing method: WebElement::getText instead of e -> e.getText().
  8. Q: Collectors.toList() vs toSet()?
    A: toList preserves order and allows duplicates. toSet removes duplicates; order not guaranteed (unless LinkedHashSet).
  9. Q: Can you use streams with WebDriver findElements?
    A: Yes — findElements returns List<WebElement>, which has .stream() in Java 8+.
  10. Q: What is @FunctionalInterface?
    A: Annotation ensuring interface has exactly one abstract method. Compiler error if violated. Allows lambda usage.
  11. Q: Predicate vs Function difference?
    A: Predicate returns boolean (test). Function returns any type (apply). Predicate filters; Function transforms.
  12. Q: How does groupingBy work?
    A: Groups stream elements into Map by classifier function. Optional downstream collector for aggregation (counting, toList).
  13. Q: findFirst() vs findAny()?
    A: findFirst returns first element in encounter order. findAny returns any element — useful in parallel streams.
  14. Q: What is peek() used for?
    A: Debugging — perform side-effect (logging) without modifying stream. Elements pass through unchanged.
  15. Q: Comparator.comparing() vs lambda comparator?
    A: comparing() is cleaner, composable (thenComparing, reversed). Preferred in Java 8+ code.
  16. Q: Why avoid get() on Optional?
    A: Throws NoSuchElementException if empty. Prefer orElse(), orElseGet(), or ifPresent().

Section 13: Multithreading

Thread Basics

Extending Thread

class ScreenshotCapture extends Thread {
    private WebDriver driver;
    private String testName;

    public ScreenshotCapture(WebDriver driver, String testName) {
        this.driver = driver;
        this.testName = testName;
    }

    @Override
    public void run() {
        File screenshot = ((TakesScreenshot) driver)
            .getScreenshotAs(OutputType.FILE);
        // save screenshot with testName
    }
}

// Usage
new ScreenshotCapture(driver, "testLogin").start();

Implementing Runnable (Preferred)

class ApiCallTask implements Runnable {
    private String endpoint;

    public ApiCallTask(String endpoint) { this.endpoint = endpoint; }

    @Override
    public void run() {
        RestAssured.get(endpoint).then().statusCode(200);
    }
}

// Usage
Thread thread = new Thread(new ApiCallTask("/api/health"));
thread.start();

Thread vs Runnable

ApproachProsCons
extends ThreadSimple for quick tasksJava single inheritance — can't extend another class
implements RunnableCan extend other classes; better separationSlightly more boilerplate

Thread Lifecycle

    NEW ──start()──> RUNNABLE ──scheduler──> RUNNING
                      ^    |                    |
                      |    |                    |
                      |    +──── CPU time ───────+
                      |                         |
                      |    sleep()/wait()/lock  |
                      |                         v
                      +──── notify()/timeout ── BLOCKED/WAITING
                                                   |
                                              run() completes
                                                   |
                                                   v
                                              TERMINATED

Key Thread Methods

  • start() — creates new thread and calls run()
  • run() — contains thread logic (don't call directly)
  • sleep(ms) — pauses current thread
  • join() — waits for thread to finish
  • interrupt() — signals thread to stop
  • isAlive() — checks if thread is running

Why Multithreading in Automation?

  • TestNG parallel execution — parallel="methods" runs tests in separate threads
  • Selenium Grid — distributes tests across nodes/threads
  • API load testing — multiple concurrent requests
  • Background tasks — screenshot capture, report generation
Danger: Shared resources (WebDriver, report writers, counters) become race-condition targets when tests run in parallel. Thread safety is non-negotiable in parallel frameworks.

Synchronization

public class ReportWriter {
    private static int passCount = 0;

    // Method-level synchronization
    public static synchronized void incrementPass() {
        passCount++; // Only one thread at a time
    }

    // Block-level synchronization
    public static void writeToFile(String result) {
        synchronized (ReportWriter.class) {
            Files.write(path, result.getBytes(), StandardOpenOption.APPEND);
        }
    }
}

Deadlock

Deadlock occurs when Thread A holds Lock 1 and waits for Lock 2, while Thread B holds Lock 2 and waits for Lock 1. Both threads block forever.

Prevention: Always acquire locks in the same order. Use timeout locks. Prefer ThreadLocal over shared synchronized resources.

Thread Safety in Automation

// THREAD-UNSAFE — DO NOT DO THIS
public class BadBaseTest {
    protected static WebDriver driver; // Shared across all threads!

    @BeforeMethod
    public void setup() {
        driver = new ChromeDriver(); // Thread B overwrites Thread A's driver
    }
}

// THREAD-SAFE — use ThreadLocal (see Section 14)
public class GoodBaseTest {
    @BeforeMethod
    public void setup() {
        DriverFactory.setDriver("chrome"); // Each thread gets own driver
    }

    @AfterMethod
    public void teardown() {
        DriverFactory.quitDriver();
    }
}

ExecutorService

import java.util.concurrent.*;

public class ParallelApiRunner {

    public void runParallelHealthChecks(List<String> endpoints) {
        ExecutorService pool = Executors.newFixedThreadPool(5);

        for (String endpoint : endpoints) {
            pool.submit(() -> {
                int status = RestAssured.get(endpoint).statusCode();
                System.out.println(endpoint + " -> " + status);
            });
        }

        pool.shutdown();
        try {
            if (!pool.awaitTermination(60, TimeUnit.SECONDS)) {
                pool.shutdownNow();
            }
        } catch (InterruptedException e) {
            pool.shutdownNow();
        }
    }
}

Interview Q&A — Multithreading

  1. Q: Thread vs Runnable — which to use?
    A: Runnable — allows extending another class; better design separation. Thread is acceptable for simple, standalone tasks.
  2. Q: start() vs run()?
    A: start() creates new thread and JVM calls run(). Calling run() directly executes in current thread — no parallelism.
  3. Q: Why is static WebDriver dangerous in parallel tests?
    A: All threads share one instance. Thread A's navigation affects Thread B's test. Causes random failures.
  4. Q: What is a race condition?
    A: Outcome depends on timing of thread execution. Two threads modifying shared counter simultaneously may lose updates.
  5. Q: synchronized method vs synchronized block?
    A: Method locks on object (instance) or class (static). Block locks on specified object — finer-grained control.
  6. Q: How does TestNG parallel execution work?
    A: TestNG creates thread pool; each test method runs in separate thread. Requires thread-safe driver management.
  7. Q: What is ExecutorService?
    A: Thread pool manager. Submits tasks, reuses threads, provides shutdown/awaitTermination for clean completion.
  8. Q: What is deadlock and how to detect it?
    A: Circular lock dependency. Detect with thread dumps (jstack), VisualVM, or avoid nested lock acquisition.
  9. Q: Can you parallelize Selenium UI tests on one machine?
    A: Yes with TestNG parallel + ThreadLocal drivers. Each thread needs its own browser instance.
  10. Q: sleep() vs wait()?
    A: sleep() is Thread class method — pauses without releasing lock. wait() is Object method — releases lock, waits for notify().
  11. Q: What is thread pool size for API tests?
    A: Depends on target server capacity. Start with 5-10; monitor response times and errors; tune accordingly.
  12. Q: How does Selenium Grid handle threading?
    A: Hub receives requests; nodes run browsers. Each session is isolated — Grid handles thread/session mapping.

Section 14: ThreadLocal — Critical for Parallel Execution

What is ThreadLocal?

ThreadLocal provides thread-confined storage — each thread accessing the variable gets its own independent copy. Changes by one thread are invisible to others. It is the cornerstone of parallel test automation.

Senior SDET Must-Know: ThreadLocal is asked in virtually every senior automation interview. If you run parallel tests, you MUST understand ThreadLocal.

Why ThreadLocal is the Most Important Concept

Problem: Shared Static WebDriver

Thread-1 (testLogin)  ──> static WebDriver ──> Chrome Browser
Thread-2 (testCheckout) ──> static WebDriver ──> SAME Chrome Browser  ← CHAOS!
Thread-3 (testSearch)   ──> static WebDriver ──> SAME Chrome Browser

Thread-1 navigates to /login
Thread-2 navigates to /checkout  ← overwrites Thread-1's page!
Thread-1 assertion fails randomly

Solution: ThreadLocal Isolation

Thread-1 ──> ThreadLocal copy ──> Chrome Browser A  (isolated)
Thread-2 ──> ThreadLocal copy ──> Chrome Browser B  (isolated)
Thread-3 ──> ThreadLocal copy ──> Chrome Browser C  (isolated)

Each thread operates on its own browser — no interference

ThreadLocal API

// Create ThreadLocal variable
ThreadLocal<WebDriver> driverThread = new ThreadLocal<>();

// withInitial — lazy initialization with default
ThreadLocal<WebDriver> driverThread = ThreadLocal.withInitial(() -> null);

// set(T value) — store value for CURRENT thread
driverThread.set(new ChromeDriver());

// get() — retrieve value for CURRENT thread
WebDriver driver = driverThread.get();

// remove() — CRITICAL! Cleanup when thread is done
driverThread.remove(); // Prevents memory leak in thread pools

Complete DriverFactory with ThreadLocal

import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.chrome.ChromeDriver;
