import org.openqa.selenium.firefox.FirefoxDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.edge.EdgeDriver;

public class DriverFactory {

    private static ThreadLocal<WebDriver> driver = new ThreadLocal<>();

    public static WebDriver getDriver() {
        return driver.get();
    }

    public static void setDriver(String browser) {
        switch (browser.toLowerCase()) {
            case "chrome":
                driver.set(new ChromeDriver());
                break;
            case "firefox":
                driver.set(new FirefoxDriver());
                break;
            case "edge":
                driver.set(new EdgeDriver());
                break;
            default:
                driver.set(new ChromeDriver());
        }
        getDriver().manage().window().maximize();
    }

    public static void quitDriver() {
        if (driver.get() != null) {
            driver.get().quit();
            driver.remove(); // Prevent memory leak!
        }
    }
}

Integration with TestNG Parallel

BaseTest

import org.testng.annotations.*;
import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;

public class BaseTest {

    protected WebDriver driver;

    @BeforeMethod
    public void setUp() {
        String browser = ConfigReader.get("browser");
        DriverFactory.setDriver(browser);
        driver = DriverFactory.getDriver();
        driver.get(ConfigReader.get("url"));
    }

    @AfterMethod
    public void tearDown() {
        DriverFactory.quitDriver(); // quit + remove()
    }
}

Test Class

public class ParallelLoginTest extends BaseTest {

    @Test
    public void testValidLogin() {
        driver.findElement(By.id("username")).sendKeys("admin");
        driver.findElement(By.id("password")).sendKeys("pass");
        driver.findElement(By.id("loginBtn")).click();
        Assert.assertTrue(driver.getCurrentUrl().contains("dashboard"));
    }

    @Test
    public void testInvalidLogin() {
        driver.findElement(By.id("username")).sendKeys("wrong");
        driver.findElement(By.id("password")).sendKeys("wrong");
        driver.findElement(By.id("loginBtn")).click();
        Assert.assertTrue(driver.findElement(By.id("error")).isDisplayed());
    }
}

testng.xml

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<!DOCTYPE suite SYSTEM "https://testng.org/testng-1.0.dtd">
<suite name="Parallel Suite" parallel="methods" thread-count="3">
    <test name="Login Tests">
        <classes>
            <class name="com.tests.ParallelLoginTest"/>
        </classes>
    </test>
</suite>

ThreadLocal for Other Thread-Confined Data

public class TestContext {

    // ExtentReports test node per thread
    private static ThreadLocal<ExtentTest> extentTest = new ThreadLocal<>();

    // RestAssured request spec per thread
    private static ThreadLocal<RequestSpecification> requestSpec = new ThreadLocal<>();

    // Scenario/test data per thread
    private static ThreadLocal<Map<String, String>> testData = new ThreadLocal<>();

    public static ExtentTest getExtentTest() { return extentTest.get(); }
    public static void setExtentTest(ExtentTest test) { extentTest.set(test); }

    public static RequestSpecification getRequestSpec() { return requestSpec.get(); }
    public static void setRequestSpec(RequestSpecification spec) { requestSpec.set(spec); }

    public static void cleanup() {
        extentTest.remove();
        requestSpec.remove();
        testData.remove();
    }
}

Common ThreadLocal Mistakes

MistakeConsequenceFix
Forgetting remove()Memory leak — old WebDriver references persist in thread poolAlways call remove() in @AfterMethod
get() before set()NullPointerExceptionInitialize in @BeforeMethod; null-check or use withInitial
Mixing static driver with ThreadLocalPartial isolation — some code uses static, some ThreadLocalConsistently use ThreadLocal everywhere
Not setting in @BeforeMethodTests fail with null driversetDriver() in @BeforeMethod of BaseTest
Sharing Page Objects across threadsPage object holds stale driver referenceCreate page objects per test method

ThreadLocal vs Static vs Instance

Variable TypeScopeParallel Safe?Use Case
StaticOne copy for entire JVMNoConstants, config readers
InstanceOne copy per objectYes (if object per thread)Page objects created per test
ThreadLocalOne copy per threadYesWebDriver, ExtentTest, request specs

Interview Q&A — ThreadLocal

  1. Q: What is ThreadLocal?
    A: Class providing thread-confined variables. Each thread has its own copy; no sharing between threads.
  2. Q: Why is ThreadLocal essential for parallel Selenium?
    A: WebDriver is not thread-safe. ThreadLocal gives each test thread its own driver instance.
  3. Q: What happens if you forget remove()?
    A: Memory leak. Thread pool reuses threads; old WebDriver references remain, preventing GC. Causes OutOfMemoryError in long CI runs.
  4. Q: ThreadLocal vs synchronized — which is better for WebDriver?
    A: ThreadLocal — no locking overhead, true isolation. Synchronized serializes access — defeats purpose of parallel execution.
  5. Q: Can two threads see each other's ThreadLocal values?
    A: No. Each thread has completely independent storage.
  6. Q: Where do you call set() and remove()?
    A: set() in @BeforeMethod. remove() in @AfterMethod after quit().
  7. Q: Is ThreadLocal used only for WebDriver?
    A: No. Also used for ExtentTest reporting, RestAssured RequestSpecification, scenario context, soft assertions.
  8. Q: ThreadLocal.withInitial() vs manual set()?
    A: withInitial provides default value on first get() without set(). Manual set() gives explicit control — preferred for WebDriver.
  9. Q: How does TestNG thread pool interact with ThreadLocal?
    A: TestNG reuses threads from pool. Without remove(), previous test's data leaks into next test on same thread.
  10. Q: ThreadLocal in inheritance — do child threads inherit?
    A: No by default. Child threads get null unless using InheritableThreadLocal.
  11. Q: Static ThreadLocal variable — is it shared?
    A: The ThreadLocal object is static (one instance), but each thread's stored value is separate. Static refers to the container, not the value.
  12. Q: How to debug ThreadLocal issues?
    A: Log thread name + driver hashCode in @BeforeMethod/@AfterMethod. Verify each thread gets unique driver.
  13. Q: ThreadLocal vs dependency injection for driver?
    A: ThreadLocal is simpler for TestNG. DI (Spring, PicoContainer) works but adds complexity. ThreadLocal is industry standard for TestNG frameworks.
  14. Q: Can ThreadLocal cause memory leak with parallel=methods?
    A: Yes, if remove() is skipped. Thread pool keeps threads alive; unreleased WebDriver instances accumulate.
  15. Q: What is InheritableThreadLocal?
    A: Subclass where child threads inherit parent's value. Rarely needed in test automation.

Section 15: equals() and hashCode() Contract

Why Important for Automation

When comparing test data objects, using objects as HashMap keys, or performing Set operations on custom classes, correct equals() and hashCode() implementations are critical. Incorrect overrides cause silent bugs — tests pass/fail unpredictably.

equals() — Default vs Override

// Default equals() — reference comparison (same as ==)
Employee e1 = new Employee("John", 50000);
Employee e2 = new Employee("John", 50000);
e1.equals(e2); // false — different objects in memory

// Override equals() — value comparison
@Override
public boolean equals(Object obj) {
    if (this == obj) return true;
    if (obj == null || getClass() != obj.getClass()) return false;
    Employee other = (Employee) obj;
    return salary == other.salary && Objects.equals(name, other.name);
}

equals() Contract

  • Reflexive: x.equals(x) is true
  • Symmetric: x.equals(y) ↔ y.equals(x)
  • Transitive: x.equals(y) and y.equals(z) → x.equals(z)
  • Consistent: Multiple calls return same result
  • Null: x.equals(null) is false

hashCode()

// Default hashCode — based on memory address
e1.hashCode() != e2.hashCode(); // even if fields are identical

// Override — consistent with equals()
@Override
public int hashCode() {
    return Objects.hash(name, salary);
}

The Contract

Golden Rule: If you override equals(), you MUST override hashCode(). If a.equals(b) is true, then a.hashCode() == b.hashCode() must be true. The reverse is NOT required — hash collision is allowed.

Bug Demo — Missing hashCode()

public class BadEmployee {
    private String name;
    // equals() overridden but hashCode() NOT overridden

    @Override
    public boolean equals(Object obj) {
        if (this == obj) return true;
        if (!(obj instanceof BadEmployee)) return false;
        return Objects.equals(name, ((BadEmployee) obj).name);
    }
    // hashCode() uses default — memory address!
}

// THE BUG:
BadEmployee e1 = new BadEmployee("John");
BadEmployee e2 = new BadEmployee("John");
e1.equals(e2);           // true — values match
e1.hashCode() == e2.hashCode(); // FALSE — different addresses!

Set<BadEmployee> set = new HashSet<>();
set.add(e1);
set.contains(e2);        // FALSE! Set can't find e2 even though equals says they're same

Map<BadEmployee, String> map = new HashMap<>();
map.put(e1, "Engineering");
map.get(e2);             // NULL! Wrong bucket due to hash mismatch

Complete Employee Class

import java.util.Objects;

public class Employee {
    private String name;
    private int salary;
    private String department;

    public Employee(String name, int salary, String department) {
        this.name = name;
        this.salary = salary;
        this.department = department;
    }

    @Override
    public boolean equals(Object obj) {
        if (this == obj) return true;
        if (obj == null || getClass() != obj.getClass()) return false;
        Employee employee = (Employee) obj;
        return salary == employee.salary
            && Objects.equals(name, employee.name)
            && Objects.equals(department, employee.department);
    }

    @Override
    public int hashCode() {
        return Objects.hash(name, salary, department);
    }

    // getters, toString...
}

Using Objects.equals() and Objects.hash()

Java 7+ utility methods simplify implementation and handle null safely:

Objects.equals(a, b)  // null-safe: returns true if both null
Objects.hash(field1, field2, field3)  // generates hash from fields

Automation Relevance

// Comparing test data objects
Employee expected = new Employee("John", 50000, "QA");
Employee actual = apiResponse.as(Employee.class);
Assert.assertEquals(actual, expected); // Uses equals()

// Custom objects as HashMap keys
Map<TestCase, TestResult> results = new HashMap<>();
TestCase tc = new TestCase("login", "validCredentials");
results.put(tc, TestResult.PASS);
results.get(new TestCase("login", "validCredentials")); // Works if equals/hashCode correct

// Set operations — find duplicates
Set<Employee> uniqueEmployees = new HashSet<>(allEmployees);
// Duplicates removed only if equals/hashCode properly implemented

Interview Q&A — equals() and hashCode()

  1. Q: What is the equals() and hashCode() contract?
    A: If two objects are equal per equals(), they must have the same hashCode(). Violating this breaks HashMap/HashSet.
  2. Q: What happens if you override equals() but not hashCode()?
    A: HashMap/HashSet break — equal objects may be stored/retrieved from different buckets.
  3. Q: Does same hashCode mean objects are equal?
    A: No. Hash collision is allowed. equals() must be used for true equality check.
  4. Q: Why use getClass() instead of instanceof in equals()?
    A: getClass() ensures exact type match. instanceof allows subclass equality which can violate symmetry.
  5. Q: What fields should be included in equals/hashCode?
    A: All fields that define object identity/equality. Exclude transient or computed fields.
  6. Q: Can you use @EqualsAndHashCode from Lombok?
    A: Yes — generates correct implementations. Specify fields with @EqualsAndHashCode.Include/Exclude.
  7. Q: How does Assert.assertEquals use equals()?
    A: Calls expected.equals(actual) for objects. Incorrect equals() causes false pass/fail.
  8. Q: == vs equals()?
    A: == compares references (memory address). equals() compares values (when overridden).
  9. Q: Why is hashCode used in HashMap?
    A: Determines bucket index. Faster lookup — check hash first, then equals() only within bucket.
  10. Q: Is hashCode() performance-critical?
    A: Yes for collections. Poor hashCode (always returns 1) degrades HashMap to linked list — O(n) lookup.

Section 16: Garbage Collection

What is Garbage Collection?

Garbage Collection (GC) is the JVM's automatic process of reclaiming memory from objects that are no longer reachable. Automation engineers don't manage memory manually, but GC behavior affects test suite performance and stability.

When Does an Object Become Eligible for GC?

  • No references point to the object
  • All references are nullified
  • Object goes out of scope (local variable in method ends)
  • Weak/Soft/Phantom references collected per reference type rules

JVM Memory Model

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    JVM Memory                        │
├─────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────┤
│   Young Generation  │       Old Generation           │
│  ┌───────┬────────┐ │  Long-lived objects promoted   │
│  │ Eden  │S0 │ S1 │ │  from Young Gen after surviving│
│  │ (new  │   │    │ │  multiple GC cycles            │
│  │ objs) │   │    │ │                                │
│  └───────┴────────┘ │                                │
├─────────────────────┴───────────────────────────────┤
│  Metaspace (Java 8+) — class metadata, static vars  │
│  (Replaced PermGen in Java 8)                       │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Flow: new object → Eden → (Minor GC) → Survivor → ... → Old Gen → (Major GC)

GC Types

CollectorDescriptionUse Case
Serial GCSingle thread, stop-the-worldSmall apps, client mode
Parallel GCMultiple threads for throughputBatch processing, default for server
G1 GCRegion-based, predictable pausesDefault since Java 9, large heaps
ZGCUltra-low latency (<10ms pauses)Large heap, latency-sensitive apps

Automation Relevance

  • WebDriver not quit — browser process + driver object leak memory
  • Large test suites — hundreds of page objects created/destroyed per run
  • Parallel execution — 5 threads = 5 browsers = 5× memory pressure + GC overhead
  • Long CI jobs — accumulated leaks cause OutOfMemoryError after hours
  • ExtentReports/screenshots — large objects held in memory if not flushed
Real Incident: A team running 500 parallel tests saw CI failures after 2 hours. Root cause: ThreadLocal WebDriver without remove(). Each thread retained quit-but-not-removed driver references. Fix: add driver.remove() in @AfterMethod.

How to Prevent Memory Issues

// 1. Always quit WebDriver
@AfterMethod
public void tearDown() {
    DriverFactory.quitDriver(); // quit() + ThreadLocal.remove()
}

// 2. Close resources with try-with-resources
try (FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream("data.xlsx");
     Workbook workbook = new XSSFWorkbook(fis)) {
    // use workbook
} // automatically closed

// 3. Nullify large collections after use
List<WebElement> elements = driver.findElements(By.tagName("div"));
// process elements...
elements = null; // help GC (optional, usually out-of-scope suffices)

// 4. JVM flags for CI pipelines
// -Xmx2g          Max heap size 2GB
// -Xms1g          Initial heap size 1GB
// -XX:+UseG1GC    Use G1 garbage collector
// -XX:+HeapDumpOnOutOfMemoryError  Dump heap for analysis

System.gc() and finalize()

// System.gc() — SUGGESTS garbage collection (NOT guaranteed)
System.gc(); // JVM may ignore this — do not rely on it

// finalize() — DEPRECATED since Java 9, removed in Java 18
// Do NOT use — unpredictable timing, performance penalty
// Use try-with-resources or explicit cleanup instead

Interview Q&A — Garbage Collection

  1. Q: What is garbage collection?
    A: Automatic reclamation of memory from unreachable objects by the JVM. No manual free() like C/C++.
  2. Q: When is an object eligible for GC?
    A: When no live reference points to it — nullified, out of scope, or reference reassigned.
  3. Q: Young Gen vs Old Gen?
    A: Young Gen (Eden + Survivor) holds new objects. Objects surviving multiple GC cycles are promoted to Old Gen.
  4. Q: What is Metaspace?
    A: Stores class metadata (replaced PermGen in Java 8). Grows dynamically; OutOfMemoryError if class loading is excessive.
  5. Q: How does GC relate to WebDriver leaks?
    A: If driver.quit() isn't called and ThreadLocal.remove() is skipped, driver objects remain reachable — GC cannot reclaim them.
  6. Q: What JVM flags do you set for CI?
    A: -Xmx (max heap), -Xms (initial heap), -XX:+UseG1GC, -XX:+HeapDumpOnOutOfMemoryError for debugging.
  7. Q: Minor GC vs Major GC?
    A: Minor GC cleans Young Gen (frequent, fast). Major/Full GC cleans entire heap including Old Gen (less frequent, slower pauses).
  8. Q: Should you call System.gc()?
    A: No. It's a hint, not a command. JVM decides when to GC. Calling it can cause unnecessary stop-the-world pauses.
  9. Q: Why was finalize() deprecated?
    A: Unpredictable execution timing, performance overhead, security issues. Use AutoCloseable/try-with-resources instead.

Section 17: Design Patterns for Automation

Design patterns are reusable solutions to common software design problems. In test automation frameworks, they solve recurring challenges: managing WebDriver instances, creating browser objects, building test configurations, switching wait strategies, and reacting to test events. Mastering these five patterns is essential for framework design interviews and real-world Selenium/TestNG projects.

Singleton Pattern

What

The Singleton pattern ensures a class has only ONE instance throughout the application lifecycle and provides a global access point to that instance. The constructor is private; creation happens via a static getInstance() method.

Why in Automation

  • ConfigReader — Read config.properties once at startup; every test class accesses the same configuration without re-parsing the file.
  • ExtentReports — One report instance accumulates all test results into a single HTML report.
  • DriverManager — Centralized driver lifecycle (often combined with ThreadLocal for parallel runs).
Framework Usage: Place Singleton classes in src/main/java/config/ or driver/. Initialize in @BeforeSuite and access anywhere via ConfigReader.getInstance().

Implementation Variants

  • Eager Singleton — Instance created at class load time.
  • Lazy Singleton — Instance created on first getInstance() call.
  • Thread-Safe Singleton — synchronized getInstance(), double-checked locking, or Bill Pugh (static inner holder class).

Complete Code: Singleton ConfigReader

package config;

import java.io.FileInputStream;
import java.io.IOException;
import java.util.Properties;

public class ConfigReader {

    private static ConfigReader instance;
    private Properties properties;

    // Private constructor — prevents external instantiation
    private ConfigReader() {
        properties = new Properties();
        try {
            FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream("src/test/resources/config.properties");
            properties.load(fis);
            fis.close();
        } catch (IOException e) {
            throw new RuntimeException("Failed to load config.properties", e);
        }
    }

    // Thread-safe lazy initialization (synchronized)
    public static synchronized ConfigReader getInstance() {
        if (instance == null) {
            instance = new ConfigReader();
        }
        return instance;
    }

    public String getProperty(String key) {
        return properties.getProperty(key);
    }

    public String getBrowser() {
        return properties.getProperty("browser", "chrome");
    }

    public String getBaseUrl() {
        return properties.getProperty("baseUrl", "https://example.com");
    }

    public int getTimeout() {
        return Integer.parseInt(properties.getProperty("timeout", "10"));
    }
}

// Usage in BaseTest:
// ConfigReader config = ConfigReader.getInstance();
// driver.get(config.getBaseUrl());

Complete Code: Bill Pugh Singleton — ExtentReportManager

package reports;

import com.aventstack.extentreports.ExtentReports;
import com.aventstack.extentreports.reporter.ExtentSparkReporter;

public class ExtentReportManager {

    // Private constructor
    private ExtentReportManager() {}

    // Bill Pugh: inner static class holds the singleton instance
    private static class ReportHolder {
        private static final ExtentReportManager INSTANCE = new ExtentReportManager();
        private static final ExtentReports EXTENT = createReport();
    }

    private static ExtentReports createReport() {
        ExtentSparkReporter spark = new ExtentSparkReporter("reports/AutomationReport.html");
        spark.config().setReportName("Automation Test Report");
        spark.config().setDocumentTitle("Test Results");
        ExtentReports extent = new ExtentReports();
        extent.attachReporter(spark);
        extent.setSystemInfo("Project", "E-Commerce Automation");
        extent.setSystemInfo("Environment", System.getProperty("env", "QA"));
        return extent;
    }

    public static ExtentReportManager getInstance() {
        return ReportHolder.INSTANCE;
    }

    public ExtentReports getReport() {
        return ReportHolder.EXTENT;
    }
}

// Usage in TestListener:
// ExtentReports extent = ExtentReportManager.getInstance().getReport();
// ExtentTest test = extent.createTest(result.getMethod().getMethodName());

Pros/Cons in Automation Context

ProsCons
Single config read — fast, consistentHard to unit test (global state)
One report instance — unified outputViolates Single Responsibility if overused
Memory efficient — no duplicate objectsThread safety requires careful design
Easy global access from any classHidden dependencies — hard to mock in isolation

Factory Pattern

What

The Factory pattern creates objects without exposing the instantiation logic to the client. The client requests an object by type/name; the factory decides which concrete class to instantiate.

Why in Automation

  • DriverFactory — Create ChromeDriver, FirefoxDriver, or EdgeDriver based on a config parameter or TestNG parameter.
  • PageFactory — Dynamically create page object instances bound to the current WebDriver.
  • BrowserType enum — Type-safe browser selection: BrowserType.CHROME → ChromeDriver.

Complete Code: BrowserFactory with Switch/Enum

package driver;

import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.chrome.ChromeDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.chrome.ChromeOptions;
import org.openqa.selenium.edge.EdgeDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.firefox.FirefoxDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.firefox.FirefoxOptions;
import io.github.bonigarcia.wdm.WebDriverManager;

public enum BrowserType {
    CHROME, FIREFOX, EDGE, HEADLESS_CHROME
}

public class BrowserFactory {

    public static WebDriver createDriver(BrowserType browser) {
        WebDriver driver;
        switch (browser) {
            case CHROME:
                WebDriverManager.chromedriver().setup();
                driver = new ChromeDriver();
                break;
            case FIREFOX:
                WebDriverManager.firefoxdriver().setup();
                driver = new FirefoxDriver();
                break;
            case EDGE:
                WebDriverManager.edgedriver().setup();
                driver = new EdgeDriver();
                break;
            case HEADLESS_CHROME:
                WebDriverManager.chromedriver().setup();
                ChromeOptions options = new ChromeOptions();
                options.addArguments("--headless", "--disable-gpu", "--window-size=1920,1080");
                driver = new ChromeDriver(options);
                break;
            default:
                throw new IllegalArgumentException("Unsupported browser: " + browser);
        }
        driver.manage().window().maximize();
        driver.manage().timeouts().implicitlyWait(java.time.Duration.ofSeconds(10));
        return driver;
    }

    // Factory method reading from config
    public static WebDriver createDriverFromConfig() {
        String browserName = config.ConfigReader.getInstance().getBrowser().toUpperCase();
        BrowserType type = BrowserType.valueOf(browserName);
        return createDriver(type);
    }
}

// Usage in BaseTest @BeforeMethod:
// WebDriver driver = BrowserFactory.createDriver(BrowserType.CHROME);

Complete Code: Page Object Factory

package pages;

import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;
import java.lang.reflect.Constructor;

public class PageFactory {

    @SuppressWarnings("unchecked")
    public static <T extends BasePage> T createPage(WebDriver driver, Class<T> pageClass) {
        try {
            Constructor<T> constructor = pageClass.getConstructor(WebDriver.class);
            return constructor.newInstance(driver);
        } catch (Exception e) {
            throw new RuntimeException("Failed to create page: " + pageClass.getSimpleName(), e);
        }
    }
}

// Usage in tests:
// LoginPage loginPage = PageFactory.createPage(driver, LoginPage.class);
// HomePage homePage = PageFactory.createPage(driver, HomePage.class);

// Dynamic page creation from TestNG parameter:
// @Parameters({"pageClass"})
// public void testPage(String pageClassName) {
//     Class<?> clazz = Class.forName("pages." + pageClassName);
//     BasePage page = PageFactory.createPage(driver, (Class) clazz);
// }

Pros/Cons

ProsCons
Centralized object creation — change browser in one placeFactory class grows with each new browser type
Tests don't depend on concrete driver classesSwitch statements violate Open/Closed Principle
Easy cross-browser testing via config/parameterReflection-based page factory adds complexity
Enum provides compile-time safetyDebugging factory failures can be harder

Builder Pattern

What

The Builder pattern constructs complex objects step by step. Instead of a constructor with 10 parameters, you chain setter-like methods and call build() at the end.

Why in Automation

  • REST Assured — RequestSpecBuilder().setBaseUri().addHeader().addQueryParam().build() creates a RequestSpecification.
  • TestConfig — Build test configuration with browser, URL, timeout, headless mode, parallel threads.
  • APIRequest — Construct API test requests with method, headers, body, and auth token.

Complete Code: TestConfig Builder

package config;

public class TestConfig {
    private final String browser;
    private final String baseUrl;
    private final int timeout;
    private final boolean headless;
    private final int parallelThreads;

    private TestConfig(Builder builder) {
        this.browser = builder.browser;
        this.baseUrl = builder.baseUrl;
        this.timeout = builder.timeout;
        this.headless = builder.headless;
        this.parallelThreads = builder.parallelThreads;
    }

    public String getBrowser() { return browser; }
    public String getBaseUrl() { return baseUrl; }
    public int getTimeout() { return timeout; }
    public boolean isHeadless() { return headless; }
    public int getParallelThreads() { return parallelThreads; }

    public static class Builder {
        private String browser = "chrome";
        private String baseUrl = "https://example.com";
        private int timeout = 10;
        private boolean headless = false;
        private int parallelThreads = 1;

        public Builder browser(String browser) {
            this.browser = browser;
            return this;
        }

        public Builder baseUrl(String baseUrl) {
            this.baseUrl = baseUrl;
            return this;
        }

        public Builder timeout(int timeout) {
            this.timeout = timeout;
            return this;
        }

        public Builder headless(boolean headless) {
            this.headless = headless;
            return this;
        }

        public Builder parallelThreads(int threads) {
            this.parallelThreads = threads;
            return this;
        }

        public TestConfig build() {
            return new TestConfig(this);
        }
    }
}

// Usage:
// TestConfig config = new TestConfig.Builder()
//     .browser("chrome")
//     .baseUrl("https://staging.example.com")
//     .timeout(15)
//     .headless(true)
//     .parallelThreads(4)
//     .build();

Complete Code: APIRequest Builder

package api;

import io.restassured.specification.RequestSpecification;
import io.restassured.builder.RequestSpecBuilder;
import java.util.HashMap;
import java.util.Map;

public class APIRequest {
    private final String method;
    private final String endpoint;
    private final Map<String, String> headers;
    private final Map<String, String> queryParams;
    private final String body;
    private final String baseUri;

    private APIRequest(Builder builder) {
        this.method = builder.method;
        this.endpoint = builder.endpoint;
        this.headers = builder.headers;
        this.queryParams = builder.queryParams;
        this.body = builder.body;
        this.baseUri = builder.baseUri;
    }

    public RequestSpecification toRequestSpec() {
        RequestSpecBuilder specBuilder = new RequestSpecBuilder()
            .setBaseUri(baseUri)
            .setContentType("application/json");
        headers.forEach(specBuilder::addHeader);
        queryParams.forEach(specBuilder::addQueryParam);
        return specBuilder.build();
    }

    public String getMethod() { return method; }
    public String getEndpoint() { return endpoint; }
    public String getBody() { return body; }

    public static class Builder {
        private String method = "GET";
        private String endpoint = "/";
        private Map<String, String> headers = new HashMap<>();
        private Map<String, String> queryParams = new HashMap<>();
        private String body = "";
        private String baseUri = "https://api.example.com";

        public Builder method(String method) { this.method = method; return this; }
        public Builder endpoint(String endpoint) { this.endpoint = endpoint; return this; }
        public Builder header(String key, String value) { this.headers.put(key, value); return this; }
        public Builder queryParam(String key, String value) { this.queryParams.put(key, value); return this; }
        public Builder body(String body) { this.body = body; return this; }
        public Builder baseUri(String baseUri) { this.baseUri = baseUri; return this; }

        public APIRequest build() { return new APIRequest(this); }
    }
}

// Usage in API test:
// APIRequest request = new APIRequest.Builder()
//     .method("POST")
//     .endpoint("/users")
//     .header("Authorization", "Bearer " + token)
//     .body("{\"name\":\"testUser\"}")
//     .build();
// given(request.toRequestSpec()).body(request.getBody()).when()
//     .post(request.getEndpoint()).then().statusCode(201);

Pros/Cons

ProsCons
Readable, fluent configuration — self-documenting testsMore boilerplate code than a simple constructor
Immutable config objects — thread-safe by defaultMust create Builder inner class for each config type
Optional parameters handled elegantlyOverkill for simple 2-3 field objects
Same pattern as REST Assured — familiar to API testersValidation logic must be added manually in build()

Strategy Pattern

What

The Strategy pattern defines a family of algorithms, encapsulates each one, and makes them interchangeable. The client chooses the strategy at runtime without changing client code.

Why in Automation

  • Wait Strategies — Switch between ExplicitWait, FluentWait, and ImplicitWait based on element behavior.
  • Locator Strategies — Swap between ID, CSS, XPath strategies for element finding.
  • Reporting Strategies — Switch between ExtentReports and Allure without changing test code.

Complete Code: WaitStrategy

package utils;

import org.openqa.selenium.By;
import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.WebElement;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.WebDriverWait;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.FluentWait;
import java.time.Duration;

// Strategy interface
public interface WaitStrategy {
    WebElement waitForElement(WebDriver driver, By locator);
}

// Concrete strategy: Explicit Wait
public class ExplicitWaitStrategy implements WaitStrategy {
    private final int timeoutSeconds;

    public ExplicitWaitStrategy(int timeoutSeconds) {
        this.timeoutSeconds = timeoutSeconds;
    }

    @Override
    public WebElement waitForElement(WebDriver driver, By locator) {
        WebDriverWait wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(timeoutSeconds));
        return wait.until(d -> d.findElement(locator).isDisplayed()
            ? d.findElement(locator) : null);
    }
}

// Concrete strategy: Fluent Wait
public class FluentWaitStrategy implements WaitStrategy {
    private final int timeoutSeconds;
    private final int pollingMillis;

    public FluentWaitStrategy(int timeoutSeconds, int pollingMillis) {
        this.timeoutSeconds = timeoutSeconds;
        this.pollingMillis = pollingMillis;
    }

    @Override
    public WebElement waitForElement(WebDriver driver, By locator) {
        FluentWait<WebDriver> wait = new FluentWait<>(driver)
            .withTimeout(Duration.ofSeconds(timeoutSeconds))
            .pollingEvery(Duration.ofMillis(pollingMillis))
            .ignoring(org.openqa.selenium.NoSuchElementException.class);
        return wait.until(d -> d.findElement(locator));
    }
}

// Context class — uses strategy
public class WaitContext {
    private WaitStrategy strategy;

    public WaitContext(WaitStrategy strategy) {
        this.strategy = strategy;
    }

    public void setStrategy(WaitStrategy strategy) {
        this.strategy = strategy;
    }

    public WebElement findElement(WebDriver driver, By locator) {
        return strategy.waitForElement(driver, locator);
    }
}

// Usage in page object:
// WaitContext waitCtx = new WaitContext(new ExplicitWaitStrategy(10));
// WebElement btn = waitCtx.findElement(driver, By.id("submit"));
// // Switch strategy for slow-loading AJAX element:
// waitCtx.setStrategy(new FluentWaitStrategy(30, 500));
// WebElement ajaxResult = waitCtx.findElement(driver, By.id("ajax-data"));

Complete Code: ReportStrategy

package reports;

import org.testng.ITestResult;

public interface ReportStrategy {
    void logPass(String testName, String message);
    void logFail(String testName, String message, ITestResult result);
    void flush();
}

public class ExtentReportStrategy implements ReportStrategy {
    private com.aventstack.extentreports.ExtentReports extent;
    private com.aventstack.extentreports.ExtentTest currentTest;

    public ExtentReportStrategy(com.aventstack.extentreports.ExtentReports extent) {
        this.extent = extent;
    }

    public void startTest(String testName) {
        currentTest = extent.createTest(testName);
    }

    @Override
    public void logPass(String testName, String message) {
        currentTest.pass(message);
    }

    @Override
    public void logFail(String testName, String message, ITestResult result) {
        currentTest.fail(message);
        currentTest.addScreenCaptureFromPath(captureScreenshot(result));
    }

    @Override
    public void flush() {
        extent.flush();
    }

    private String captureScreenshot(ITestResult result) {
        return "screenshots/" + result.getName() + ".png";
    }
}

public class AllureReportStrategy implements ReportStrategy {
    @Override
    public void logPass(String testName, String message) {
        io.qameta.allure.Allure.step(message, () -> {});
    }

    @Override
    public void logFail(String testName, String message, ITestResult result) {
        io.qameta.allure.Allure.step("FAILED: " + message);
    }

    @Override
    public void flush() {
        // Allure auto-generates report from results directory
    }
}

// Usage in TestListener — switch via config:
// ReportStrategy reporter = config.getProperty("report.type").equals("allure")
//     ? new AllureReportStrategy()
//     : new ExtentReportStrategy(extent);
// reporter.logPass("LoginTest", "User logged in successfully");

Pros/Cons

ProsCons
Swap wait/report algorithms at runtime via configMore classes and interfaces to maintain
Open/Closed Principle — add new strategy without modifying existing codeOver-engineering if you only ever use one strategy
Each strategy is independently testableClient must know which strategy to select
Clean separation — page objects don't know wait implementationStrategy selection logic adds a layer of indirection

Observer Pattern

What

The Observer pattern defines a one-to-many dependency: when one object (subject) changes state, all dependent objects (observers) are notified and updated automatically.

Why in Automation

TestNG Listeners ARE the Observer pattern. The TestNG framework (subject) fires test events; your listener classes (observers) react to those events — logging results, taking screenshots, updating reports, sending Slack notifications.

How ITestListener Works as Observer

package listeners;

import org.testng.ITestListener;
import org.testng.ITestResult;
import org.testng.ITestContext;
import reports.ExtentReportManager;
import com.aventstack.extentreports.ExtentReports;
import com.aventstack.extentreports.ExtentTest;

// Observer: reacts to test lifecycle events from TestNG (Subject)
public class TestListener implements ITestListener {

    private ExtentReports extent = ExtentReportManager.getInstance().getReport();
    private ThreadLocal<ExtentTest> extentTest = new ThreadLocal<>();

    // Observer method: notified when test STARTS
    @Override
    public void onTestStart(ITestResult result) {
        ExtentTest test = extent.createTest(result.getMethod().getMethodName());
        extentTest.set(test);
        System.out.println("TEST STARTED: " + result.getName());
    }

    // Observer method: notified when test PASSES
    @Override
    public void onTestSuccess(ITestResult result) {
        extentTest.get().pass("Test passed: " + result.getName());
        System.out.println("TEST PASSED: " + result.getName());
    }

    // Observer method: notified when test FAILS
    @Override
    public void onTestFailure(ITestResult result) {
        extentTest.get().fail("Test failed: " + result.getThrowable());
        captureScreenshot(result);
        System.out.println("TEST FAILED: " + result.getName());
    }

    // Observer method: notified when test is SKIPPED
    @Override
    public void onTestSkipped(ITestResult result) {
        extentTest.get().skip("Test skipped: " + result.getName());
    }

    // Observer method: notified when entire SUITE finishes
    @Override
    public void onFinish(ITestContext context) {
        extent.flush();
        System.out.println("SUITE FINISHED — Report generated");
    }

    private void captureScreenshot(ITestResult result) {
        // Screenshot logic on failure
        extentTest.get().addScreenCaptureFromPath("screenshots/" + result.getName() + ".png");
    }
}

// Register in testng.xml:
// <listeners>
//     <listener class-name="listeners.TestListener"/>
// </listeners>
Key Insight: You can register multiple listeners (observers) — one for reporting, one for screenshots, one for Slack alerts — and TestNG notifies ALL of them on every event. This is classic Observer pattern.

Pattern Comparison Table

PatternWhen to UseFramework LayerComplexity
SingletonOne shared resource (config, report, logger)Config / Reports / DriverLow
FactoryObject creation varies by type (browser, page)Driver / PagesLow–Medium
BuilderComplex object with many optional paramsConfig / API RequestsMedium
StrategyMultiple interchangeable algorithmsUtils / Reports / WaitsMedium
ObserverReact to events without modifying sourceListeners / ReportingLow

Interview Q&A — Design Patterns for Automation

Q1: Which design pattern is used in TestNG listeners?

A: Observer pattern. TestNG is the subject that fires events (onTestStart, onTestFailure); listener classes are observers that react to those events.

Q2: Why use Singleton for ConfigReader instead of static variables?

A: Singleton provides lazy initialization, thread safety, and encapsulation. Static variables are initialized at class load and harder to reset between test suites.

Q3: Singleton vs Factory — when to use which?

A: Singleton when you need exactly ONE instance (config, report). Factory when you need to CREATE different types of objects (browsers, page objects).

Q4: Is PageFactory (Selenium) the same as Factory pattern?

A: Selenium's PageFactory is a hybrid — it uses Factory to initialize page elements via reflection and proxy, but the core Factory pattern creates entire page object instances.

Q5: How does REST Assured use Builder pattern?

A: RequestSpecBuilder and ResponseSpecBuilder let you chain setBaseUri(), addHeader(), addQueryParam() and call build() to create immutable specification objects.

Q6: Can you combine Singleton with ThreadLocal?

A: Yes. Singleton DriverManager holds a ThreadLocal<WebDriver> — one manager instance, but each thread gets its own driver. Common in parallel TestNG execution.

Q7: What is double-checked locking in Singleton?

A: Check if instance is null twice — once without synchronization (fast path), once inside synchronized block — to avoid creating multiple instances in multi-threaded environments while minimizing lock overhead.

Q8: Strategy vs Factory — what's the difference?

A: Factory creates objects; Strategy defines interchangeable behavior/algorithms. Factory answers "which object?"; Strategy answers "which algorithm?"

Q9: How would you add a new browser to BrowserFactory?

A: Add enum value to BrowserType, add case in switch statement, configure WebDriverManager for that browser. Tests remain unchanged — they call createDriverFromConfig().

Q10: What are disadvantages of Singleton in test automation?

A: Global state makes unit testing difficult, hidden dependencies between classes, and state can leak between test suites if not properly reset in @AfterSuite.

Q11: How does Builder pattern improve test readability?

A: Instead of new TestConfig("chrome", "url", 10, true, 4), you write fluent chains: new TestConfig.Builder().browser("chrome").headless(true).build() — self-documenting and order-independent.

Q12: Give a real example of Observer in your framework.

A: TestListener implements ITestListener. On test failure, it captures screenshot, logs to ExtentReport, and sends Slack notification — all triggered automatically by TestNG without modifying test classes.

Q13: Is Enum Singleton better than synchronized getInstance()?

A: Joshua Bloch recommends enum singleton — inherently serializable, reflection-proof, and thread-safe without any synchronization code. Best for simple singletons like ConfigReader.

Q14: How do design patterns make a framework scalable?

A: Factory adds new browsers/pages without changing tests. Strategy swaps wait/report implementations via config. Builder handles growing config complexity. Observer adds new listeners without modifying TestNG or test classes.

Section 18: Page Object Model — Framework Design

What is POM?

The Page Object Model (POM) is a design pattern that separates page UI elements and actions from test logic. Each web page (or component) gets its own class containing locators (private) and action methods (public). Tests interact with pages through these methods — never directly with locators.

Why POM? — The #1 Framework Design Question

Without POM — Maintenance Nightmare

// BAD: Locators and actions mixed directly in test class
@Test
public void testLogin() {
    driver.findElement(By.id("username")).sendKeys("admin");
    driver.findElement(By.id("password")).sendKeys("pass123");
    driver.findElement(By.xpath("//button[@type='submit']")).click();
    Assert.assertTrue(driver.findElement(By.cssSelector(".welcome-msg"))
        .getText().contains("Welcome"));
    // If login button ID changes → update EVERY test file that logs in!
}

With POM — Change Once, All Tests Work

// GOOD: Test uses page object methods — no locators in test
@Test
public void testLogin() {
    LoginPage loginPage = new LoginPage(driver);
    HomePage homePage = loginPage.login("admin", "pass123");
    Assert.assertTrue(homePage.getWelcomeText().contains("Welcome"));
    // If login button ID changes → update ONLY LoginPage.java
}

POM Architecture

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                      TEST LAYER                              │
│  LoginTest.java    SearchTest.java    CheckoutTest.java     │
│       │                  │                   │               │
│       ▼                  ▼                   ▼               │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                    PAGE OBJECT LAYER                         │
│  LoginPage.java    SearchPage.java    CheckoutPage.java     │
│       │ extends          │ extends          │ extends       │
│       ▼                  ▼                   ▼               │
│              BasePage.java (common actions)                  │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                    UTILITY LAYER                             │
│  WaitUtils.java    ElementUtils.java    ConfigReader.java   │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                    DRIVER LAYER                              │
│  DriverFactory.java    ThreadLocal<WebDriver>               │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                    LISTENER LAYER                            │
│  TestListener.java (screenshots, reports, logging)         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

POM Rules

  1. One class per page/component — LoginPage, HomePage, SearchPage each get their own class.
  2. Locators: private — Never expose By locators outside the page class.
  3. Actions: public methods — enterUsername(), clickLogin() encapsulate interactions.
  4. Return type: next page object — clickLogin() returns HomePage for method chaining.
  5. NO assertions in page objects — Assertions belong in test classes only.
  6. NO test data in page objects — Pass data as method parameters from tests.

Complete Framework Architecture

src/main/java/
├── base/
│   └── BasePage.java
├── pages/
│   ├── LoginPage.java
│   ├── HomePage.java
│   ├── SearchPage.java
│   └── ProductPage.java
├── config/
│   └── ConfigReader.java
├── driver/
│   └── DriverFactory.java
└── utils/
    ├── WaitUtils.java
    └── ElementUtils.java

src/test/java/
├── base/
│   └── BaseTest.java
├── tests/
│   ├── LoginTest.java
│   └── SearchTest.java
└── listeners/
    └── TestListener.java

Complete Code: BasePage.java

package base;

import org.openqa.selenium.*;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.WebDriverWait;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.ExpectedConditions;
import org.openqa.selenium.interactions.Actions;
import java.time.Duration;

public class BasePage {
    protected WebDriver driver;
    protected WebDriverWait wait;
    protected Actions actions;

    public BasePage(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
        this.wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(15));
        this.actions = new Actions(driver);
    }

    protected void click(By locator) {
        waitForElement(locator);
        driver.findElement(locator).click();
    }

    protected void type(By locator, String text) {
        waitForElement(locator);
        WebElement element = driver.findElement(locator);
        element.clear();
        element.sendKeys(text);
    }

    protected String getText(By locator) {
        waitForElement(locator);
        return driver.findElement(locator).getText();
    }

    protected WebElement waitForElement(By locator) {
        return wait.until(ExpectedConditions.visibilityOfElementLocated(locator));
    }

    protected WebElement waitForClickable(By locator) {
        return wait.until(ExpectedConditions.elementToBeClickable(locator));
    }

    protected void scrollTo(By locator) {
        WebElement element = driver.findElement(locator);
        ((JavascriptExecutor) driver).executeScript(
            "arguments[0].scrollIntoView(true);", element);
    }

    protected boolean isDisplayed(By locator) {
        try {
            return driver.findElement(locator).isDisplayed();
        } catch (NoSuchElementException e) {
            return false;
        }
    }

    protected void selectDropdownByText(By locator, String text) {
        WebElement dropdown = waitForElement(locator);
        org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.Select select =
            new org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.Select(dropdown);
        select.selectByVisibleText(text);
    }

    protected String getPageTitle() {
        return driver.getTitle();
    }

    protected String getCurrentUrl() {
        return driver.getCurrentUrl();
    }
}

Complete Code: LoginPage.java

package pages;

import base.BasePage;
import org.openqa.selenium.By;
import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;

public class LoginPage extends BasePage {

    // Private locators — never exposed outside this class
    private By usernameField = By.id("username");
    private By passwordField = By.id("password");
    private By loginButton   = By.xpath("//button[@type='submit']");
    private By errorMessage  = By.cssSelector(".error-msg");

    public LoginPage(WebDriver driver) {
        super(driver);
    }

    public LoginPage enterUsername(String username) {
        type(usernameField, username);
        return this;
    }

    public LoginPage enterPassword(String password) {
        type(passwordField, password);
        return this;
    }

    public HomePage clickLogin() {
        click(loginButton);
        return new HomePage(driver);
    }

    // Combined action — most common usage
    public HomePage login(String username, String password) {
        enterUsername(username);
        enterPassword(password);
        return clickLogin();
    }

    public String getErrorMessage() {
        return getText(errorMessage);
    }

    public boolean isLoginPageDisplayed() {
        return isDisplayed(usernameField) && isDisplayed(loginButton);
    }
}

Complete Code: HomePage.java

package pages;

import base.BasePage;
import org.openqa.selenium.By;
import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;

public class HomePage extends BasePage {

    private By welcomeMessage  = By.cssSelector(".welcome-msg");
    private By searchLink      = By.linkText("Search");
    private By logoutButton    = By.id("logout");
    private By userProfileIcon = By.cssSelector(".user-profile");

    public HomePage(WebDriver driver) {
        super(driver);
    }

    public boolean isHomePageDisplayed() {
        return isDisplayed(welcomeMessage);
    }

    public String getWelcomeText() {
        return getText(welcomeMessage);
    }

    public SearchPage navigateToSearch() {
        click(searchLink);
        return new SearchPage(driver);
    }

    public LoginPage logout() {
        click(logoutButton);
        return new LoginPage(driver);
    }

    public String getUserProfileName() {
        return getText(userProfileIcon);
    }
}

Complete Code: BaseTest.java

package base;

import config.ConfigReader;
import driver.BrowserFactory;
import driver.DriverManager;
import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;
import org.testng.annotations.*;
import org.testng.ITestResult;
import reports.ExtentReportManager;
import com.aventstack.extentreports.ExtentReports;

public class BaseTest {

    protected WebDriver driver;
    protected ConfigReader config;

    @BeforeSuite
    public void initReports() {
        ExtentReports extent = ExtentReportManager.getInstance().getReport();
        System.out.println("Reports initialized");
    }

    @BeforeMethod
    public void setUp() {
        config = ConfigReader.getInstance();
        driver = BrowserFactory.createDriverFromConfig();
        DriverManager.setDriver(driver);
        driver.get(config.getBaseUrl());
    }

    @AfterMethod
    public void tearDown(ITestResult result) {
        if (result.getStatus() == ITestResult.FAILURE) {
            captureScreenshot(result.getName());
        }
        DriverManager.quitDriver();
    }

    private void captureScreenshot(String testName) {
        try {
            org.openqa.selenium.TakesScreenshot ts =
                (org.openqa.selenium.TakesScreenshot) driver;
            java.io.File src = ts.getScreenshotAs(
                org.openqa.selenium.OutputType.FILE);
            java.nio.file.Files.copy(src.toPath(),
                new java.io.File("screenshots/" + testName + ".png").toPath(),
                java.nio.file.StandardCopyOption.REPLACE_EXISTING);
        } catch (Exception e) {
            System.out.println("Screenshot failed: " + e.getMessage());
        }
    }
}

Complete Code: LoginTest.java

package tests;

import base.BaseTest;
import pages.HomePage;
import pages.LoginPage;
import org.testng.Assert;
import org.testng.annotations.DataProvider;
import org.testng.annotations.Test;

public class LoginTest extends BaseTest {

    @DataProvider(name = "loginData")
    public Object[][] getLoginData() {
        return new Object[][] {
            {"admin",    "admin123",  true,  "Welcome, Admin"},
            {"user1",    "user123",   true,  "Welcome, User1"},
            {"invalid",  "wrong",     false, null},
            {"",         "pass",      false, null}
        };
    }

    @Test(dataProvider = "loginData")
    public void testLogin(String username, String password,
                          boolean shouldPass, String expectedWelcome) {
        LoginPage loginPage = new LoginPage(driver);
        Assert.assertTrue(loginPage.isLoginPageDisplayed(),
            "Login page should be displayed");

        if (shouldPass) {
            HomePage homePage = loginPage.login(username, password);
            Assert.assertTrue(homePage.isHomePageDisplayed());
            Assert.assertTrue(homePage.getWelcomeText().contains(expectedWelcome));
        } else {
            loginPage.enterUsername(username).enterPassword(password);
            loginPage.clickLogin();
            Assert.assertFalse(new HomePage(driver).isHomePageDisplayed());
        }
    }

    @Test
    public void testLoginWithMethodChaining() {
        HomePage homePage = new LoginPage(driver)
            .enterUsername("admin")
            .enterPassword("admin123")
            .clickLogin();
        Assert.assertEquals(homePage.getWelcomeText(), "Welcome, Admin");
    }
}

Page Factory

@FindBy Annotation

import org.openqa.selenium.WebElement;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.FindBy;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.PageFactory;

public class LoginPagePF extends BasePage {

    @FindBy(id = "username")
    private WebElement usernameField;

    @FindBy(id = "password")
    private WebElement passwordField;

    @FindBy(xpath = "//button[@type='submit']")
    private WebElement loginButton;

    @FindBy(css = ".error-msg")
    private WebElement errorMessage;

    public LoginPagePF(WebDriver driver) {
        super(driver);
        PageFactory.initElements(driver, this); // Initializes all @FindBy elements
    }

    public void enterUsername(String username) {
        usernameField.clear();
        usernameField.sendKeys(username);
    }

    public void clickLogin() {
        loginButton.click();
    }
}

@CacheLookup — Cache Static Elements Only

@FindBy(id = "header-logo")
@CacheLookup  // Element found once, cached for subsequent calls
private WebElement headerLogo;

@FindBy(id = "dynamic-cart-count")
// NO @CacheLookup — cart count changes dynamically
private WebElement cartCount;

@FindBys (AND) vs @FindAll (OR)

// @FindBys: ALL locators must match (AND logic)
@FindBys({
    @FindBy(className = "nav-item"),
    @FindBy(linkText = "Products")
})
private WebElement productsNavLink;

// @FindAll: ANY locator matches (OR logic)
@FindAll({
    @FindBy(id = "submit-btn"),
    @FindBy(xpath = "//button[text()='Submit']"),
    @FindBy(css = "input[type='submit']")
})
private WebElement submitButton;

PageFactory Limitations

  • StaleElementReferenceException — Using @CacheLookup on dynamic elements (AJAX-loaded content) returns stale references after DOM refresh.
  • No dynamic locator support — Cannot parameterize locators: @FindBy(id = dynamicId) does not work with runtime values.
  • Hidden initialization — Elements initialized via proxy; debugging is harder than explicit driver.findElement(By).
  • Tied to WebElement — Cannot easily return By locators for custom wait strategies.

POM vs PageFactory Comparison

AspectPOM (By Locators)PageFactory (@FindBy)
Locator typeBy objects (flexible)WebElement fields (fixed)
Dynamic locatorsSupported via methodsNot supported
InitializationLazy — find on each callEager via initElements proxy
Stale element riskLow — re-finds each timeHigh with @CacheLookup
ReadabilityExplicit By declarationsClean @FindBy annotations
DebuggingEasy — standard findElementHarder — proxy indirection
Industry preferencePreferred (2024+)Declining usage
Wait integrationFull control with WebDriverWaitMust wrap WebElement calls
Industry Trend: POM with By locators is preferred over PageFactory. By locators support dynamic values, integrate cleanly with explicit waits, and avoid StaleElementReferenceException issues.

Method Chaining (Fluent Interface)

// Fluent interface — each method returns 'this' or next page
public class LoginPage extends BasePage {

    public LoginPage enterUsername(String username) {
        type(usernameField, username);
        return this;  // Returns same page for chaining
    }

    public LoginPage enterPassword(String password) {
        type(passwordField, password);
        return this;
    }

    public HomePage clickLogin() {
        click(loginButton);
        return new HomePage(driver);  // Returns NEXT page
    }
}

// Test usage — reads like English:
HomePage home = new LoginPage(driver)
    .enterUsername("admin")
    .enterPassword("pass123")
    .clickLogin();

// Multi-step navigation chain:
ProductPage product = new HomePage(driver)
    .navigateToSearch()
    .searchFor("laptop")
    .clickFirstResult();

Component-Based POM

Large pages are split into reusable components shared across multiple pages.

// HeaderComponent — shared across all pages
public class HeaderComponent extends BasePage {
    private By logoLink     = By.id("logo");
    private By cartIcon     = By.cssSelector(".cart-icon");
    private By searchBar    = By.name("q");
    private By userMenu     = By.cssSelector(".user-dropdown");

    public HeaderComponent(WebDriver driver) { super(driver); }

    public void clickLogo() { click(logoLink); }
    public int getCartItemCount() {
        return Integer.parseInt(getText(cartIcon));
    }
    public SearchPage search(String query) {
        type(searchBar, query);
        searchBar.submit();
        return new SearchPage(driver);
    }
}

// HomePage COMPOSES components (HAS-A relationship)
public class HomePage extends BasePage {
    private HeaderComponent header;
    private FooterComponent footer;
    private NavigationComponent nav;

    public HomePage(WebDriver driver) {
        super(driver);
        header = new HeaderComponent(driver);
        footer = new FooterComponent(driver);
        nav    = new NavigationComponent(driver);
    }

    public HeaderComponent getHeader() { return header; }
    public FooterComponent getFooter() { return footer; }

    public ProductPage navigateToCategory(String category) {
        nav.clickCategory(category);
        return new ProductPage(driver);
    }
}

// Test uses components:
@Test
public void testSearchFromHeader() {
    HomePage home = new LoginPage(driver).login("admin", "pass");
    SearchPage search = home.getHeader().search("selenium book");
    Assert.assertTrue(search.hasResults());
}

Interview Q&A — Page Object Model

Q1: What is Page Object Model?

A: A design pattern separating page UI elements/actions from test logic. Each page is a class with private locators and public action methods. Tests call page methods, never interact with locators directly.

Q2: Why should page objects NOT contain assertions?

A: Page objects represent UI behavior (actions/state), not test validation. Assertions in page objects violate Single Responsibility and make pages unusable for both positive and negative test scenarios.

Q3: What should clickLogin() return?

A: The next page object — HomePage. This enables method chaining and makes navigation explicit: HomePage home = loginPage.clickLogin().

Q4: POM vs PageFactory — which do you prefer?

A: POM with By locators. It supports dynamic locators, integrates with explicit waits, avoids stale element issues, and is easier to debug. PageFactory is acceptable for static pages only.

Q5: How do you handle dynamic elements in POM?

A: Use parameterized methods: By rowLocator = By.xpath("//tr[td='" + name + "']"). By locators allow runtime construction; PageFactory @FindBy does not.

Q6: What is component-based POM?

A: Splitting shared UI sections (header, footer, nav) into separate component classes. Pages compose components via HAS-A relationship instead of duplicating locators.

Q7: Where do you store test data in a POM framework?

A: External sources — JSON, Excel, CSV, properties files, or TestNG DataProvider. Never hardcode data inside page objects; pass as method parameters from tests.

Q8: How does BasePage reduce code duplication?

A: Common actions (click, type, wait, scroll, isDisplayed) are implemented once in BasePage. All page classes extend BasePage and inherit these utilities.

Q9: Can a page object represent a modal dialog?

A: Yes. Treat modals as components: ConfirmationDialogComponent with clickConfirm() and clickCancel() methods. Pages return dialog components when modals appear.

Q10: How do you handle iFrames in POM?

A: Create a method in BasePage: switchToFrame(By locator) and switchToDefault(). Page objects for iframe content call switch methods before interacting with elements.

Q11: What is the difference between page object and page factory?

A: Page Object is the design pattern (concept). Page Factory is Selenium's implementation using @FindBy annotations and initElements. You can implement POM without PageFactory.

Q12: How do you organize page objects for a SPA (Single Page Application)?

A: Use component-based POM. SPA pages don't fully reload — create components for each UI section that may appear/disappear dynamically rather than one class per URL.

Q13: Should page objects handle waits internally?

A: Yes. Page action methods should wait for elements before interacting. Tests should not contain wait logic — that's the page object's responsibility via BasePage.waitForElement().

Q14: How do you test a page object in isolation?

A: Use a mock WebDriver or a lightweight page load in @BeforeMethod. Verify action methods find correct elements and return expected page objects. Keep page objects free of assertions for easy unit testing.

Q15: What is lazy initialization in POM context?

A: With By locators, elements are found only when an action method is called — not at page object construction. This avoids StaleElementReferenceException on dynamic pages.

Section 19: Framework-Specific Java Questions

These are the most frequently asked Java questions in automation framework interviews. Each answer includes practical code examples from real Selenium/TestNG frameworks.

Q1: Why use HashMap in automation?

Answer: HashMap provides O(1) key-value lookup — ideal for config storage, test data mapping, API headers, request parameters, and element locator dictionaries. Keys are unique; values can be updated without recompilation.

// Config storage
Map<String, String> config = new HashMap<>();
config.put("browser", "chrome");
config.put("baseUrl", "https://staging.example.com");

// API headers
Map<String, String> headers = new HashMap<>();
headers.put("Authorization", "Bearer " + token);
headers.put("Content-Type", "application/json");

// Test data from Excel row
Map<String, String> testData = ExcelReader.getRowData("LoginData", 1);
loginPage.login(testData.get("username"), testData.get("password"));

// Element mapping for dynamic pages
Map<String, By> locators = new HashMap<>();
locators.put("username", By.id("user"));
locators.put("password", By.id("pass"));
driver.findElement(locators.get("username")).sendKeys("admin");

Interviewer expects: You know HashMap use cases beyond basic Java — config, data, headers, locators.

Q2: Why use Properties files instead of hardcoding?

Answer: Properties files enable environment switching (QA/Staging/Prod) without recompilation. CI/CD pipelines pass different property files per environment. Non-developers (QA leads) can update URLs and credentials without touching Java code.

// config.properties
browser=chrome
baseUrl=https://qa.example.com
timeout=10
headless=false

// ConfigReader.java
Properties props = new Properties();
props.load(new FileInputStream("src/test/resources/config.properties"));
String url = props.getProperty("baseUrl");

// CI/CD override via Maven:
// mvn test -Denv=prod  → loads config-prod.properties
String env = System.getProperty("env", "qa");
props.load(new FileInputStream("config-" + env + ".properties"));

Interviewer expects: You understand externalization of config for multi-environment frameworks.

Q3: Why use ThreadLocal in automation?

Answer: ThreadLocal provides each thread its own isolated copy of a variable. In parallel TestNG execution, each test thread gets its own WebDriver instance — preventing shared state corruption where one test quits another test's browser.

WITHOUT ThreadLocal (Parallel = BROKEN):
Thread-1 ──→ shared WebDriver ←── Thread-2
              (Thread-2 quits → Thread-1 fails!)

WITH ThreadLocal (Parallel = SAFE):
Thread-1 ──→ ThreadLocal ──→ WebDriver-1
Thread-2 ──→ ThreadLocal ──→ WebDriver-2
Thread-3 ──→ ThreadLocal ──→ WebDriver-3

public class DriverManager {
    private static ThreadLocal<WebDriver> driverThread = new ThreadLocal<>();

    public static WebDriver getDriver() {
        if (driverThread.get() == null) {
            driverThread.set(BrowserFactory.createDriverFromConfig());
        }
        return driverThread.get();
    }

    public static void setDriver(WebDriver driver) {
        driverThread.set(driver);
    }

    public static void quitDriver() {
        if (driverThread.get() != null) {
            driverThread.get().quit();
            driverThread.remove(); // CRITICAL: prevent memory leak
        }
    }
}

Interviewer expects: You know ThreadLocal + remove() to prevent memory leaks in thread pools.

Q4: Why use Singleton for DriverManager/ConfigReader?

Answer: Singleton ensures config is read once (not per test), report accumulates all results in one instance, and DriverManager provides a single access point for ThreadLocal driver management across the framework.

// Without Singleton: each test class reads config independently
ConfigReader c1 = new ConfigReader(); // reads file
ConfigReader c2 = new ConfigReader(); // reads file AGAIN (wasteful)

// With Singleton: one instance, one file read
ConfigReader config = ConfigReader.getInstance();
String url = config.getBaseUrl(); // same instance everywhere

// DriverManager Singleton + ThreadLocal combo:
DriverManager.getInstance().getDriver(); // thread-safe driver access

Interviewer expects: You understand resource efficiency and consistent state management.

Q5: How to design a scalable framework?

Answer: Layer the framework: Driver → Config → Pages → Tests → Reports. Apply design patterns at each layer. Scalability means adding new pages, tests, browsers, and environments without modifying existing code.

┌──────────────┐
│   TESTS      │  Add new test class → zero changes elsewhere
├──────────────┤
│   PAGES      │  Add new page class → extends BasePage
├──────────────┤
│   UTILS      │  WaitUtils, ElementUtils — shared helpers
├──────────────┤
│   CONFIG     │  Singleton ConfigReader — one properties file
├──────────────┤
│   DRIVER     │  Factory + ThreadLocal — any browser, parallel safe
├──────────────┤
│   REPORTS    │  Strategy pattern — Extent/Allure switchable
├──────────────┤
│   LISTENERS  │  Observer pattern — auto screenshot, logging
└──────────────┘

Scalability factors: New page = new class extending BasePage. New browser = new enum in BrowserFactory. New environment = new properties file. New report = new ReportStrategy implementation.

Interviewer expects: Clear layered architecture with patterns at each level.

Q6: How to manage test data?

Answer: Externalize test data from test code. Use Excel/JSON/CSV for structured data, Faker for random data, API/DB for dynamic data. TestNG DataProvider feeds data into test methods.

// JSON data source
ObjectMapper mapper = new ObjectMapper();
List<Map> users = mapper.readValue(
    new File("testdata/users.json"), List.class);

@DataProvider
public Object[][] loginData() {
    return users.stream()
        .map(u -> new Object[]{u.get("username"), u.get("password")})
        .toArray(Object[][]::new);
}

// Faker for random test data
Faker faker = new Faker();
String email = faker.internet().emailAddress();
String name  = faker.name().fullName();
SourceProsConsWhen to Use
ExcelNon-tech users can editSlower parsing, binary formatBusiness-driven test data
JSONLightweight, version-controllableNo built-in Java support (needs library)API test payloads, structured data
CSVSimple, universalNo data types, no nestingSimple flat datasets
DatabaseDynamic, real production-like dataSetup complexity, slowerIntegration tests, data validation
FakerRandom realistic dataNon-deterministic resultsLoad testing, registration flows
PropertiesEnvironment-specific valuesKey-value only, no complex structuresURLs, credentials, toggles

Interviewer expects: Multiple data sources and knowing when to use each.

Q7: How to handle dynamic elements?

Answer: Dynamic elements change ID/class on each page load. Use partial XPath/CSS, explicit waits, and retry patterns. Never use @CacheLookup or static locators for dynamic content.

// Dynamic XPath with partial match
By dynamicRow = By.xpath("//tr[contains(@class,'data-row') and td='" + name + "']");

// Explicit wait for dynamic element
WebDriverWait wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(15));
WebElement element = wait.until(ExpectedConditions
    .presenceOfElementLocated(By.cssSelector(".ajax-loaded-content")));

// Retry pattern for flaky dynamic elements
public WebElement findWithRetry(By locator, int maxAttempts) {
    for (int i = 0; i < maxAttempts; i++) {
        try {
            return wait.until(ExpectedConditions.visibilityOfElementLocated(locator));
        } catch (TimeoutException e) {
            if (i == maxAttempts - 1) throw e;
            driver.navigate().refresh();
        }
    }
    return null;
}

Interviewer expects: Partial locators, explicit waits, and retry — not Thread.sleep().

Q8: How to implement cross-browser testing?

Answer: BrowserFactory creates the correct driver from config or TestNG parameter. testng.xml defines parallel cross-browser suites. Selenium Grid distributes tests across browser nodes.

// testng.xml cross-browser suite
// <test name="ChromeTests">
//   <parameter name="browser" value="CHROME"/>
// </test>
// <test name="FirefoxTests">
//   <parameter name="browser" value="FIREFOX"/>
// </test>

@Parameters("browser")
@BeforeMethod
public void setUp(@Optional("CHROME") String browser) {
    BrowserType type = BrowserType.valueOf(browser);
    driver = BrowserFactory.createDriver(type);
    DriverManager.setDriver(driver);
}

Interviewer expects: Factory pattern + TestNG parameters + optional Grid integration.

Q9: How to implement environment-specific configuration?

Answer: Multiple config files per environment, selected via Maven profiles or System properties. CI/CD pipeline passes -Denv=staging to load the correct file.

// File structure:
// config/config-qa.properties
// config/config-staging.properties
// config/config-prod.properties

public class ConfigReader {
    private ConfigReader() {
        String env = System.getProperty("env", "qa");
        String path = "config/config-" + env + ".properties";
        properties.load(new FileInputStream(path));
    }
}

// Maven profile in pom.xml:
// mvn test -Pstaging  → loads config-staging.properties
// <profile><id>staging</id>
//   <properties><env>staging</env></properties>
// </profile>

Interviewer expects: Multi-file config with runtime environment selection.

Q10: How to handle test failures gracefully?

Answer: Combine RetryAnalyzer for flaky tests, automatic screenshots on failure, detailed logging, and soft assertions for non-critical validations that shouldn't abort the entire test.

// RetryAnalyzer for flaky tests
public class RetryAnalyzer implements IRetryAnalyzer {
    private int count = 0;
    private static final int MAX_RETRY = 2;

    @Override
    public boolean retry(ITestResult result) {
        if (count < MAX_RETRY) { count++; return true; }
        return false;
    }
}
@Test(retryAnalyzer = RetryAnalyzer.class)
public void flakyTest() { /* test logic */ }

// Soft assertions — collect all failures, report at end
SoftAssert soft = new SoftAssert();
soft.assertEquals(actualTitle, expectedTitle, "Title mismatch");
soft.assertTrue(isLogoDisplayed, "Logo not visible");
soft.assertAll(); // Throws if ANY assertion failed

Interviewer expects: Multi-layered failure handling — retry, screenshot, soft assert.

Additional Interview Q&A

Q11: Why use Maven in automation projects?

A: Dependency management (Selenium, TestNG, ExtentReports versions in pom.xml), standardized project structure, build lifecycle (compile → test → report), and CI/CD integration via mvn test.

Q12: What is the difference between implicit and explicit wait?

A: Implicit wait is a global timeout for findElement across the entire session. Explicit wait is a targeted condition (visibility, clickability) for a specific element. Always prefer explicit waits in frameworks.

Q13: How do you run tests in parallel with TestNG?

A: Set parallel="methods" and thread-count="4" in testng.xml. Use ThreadLocal for WebDriver isolation. Each thread gets its own driver instance via DriverManager.

Q14: What is PageFactory.initElements() doing internally?

A: It scans the class for @FindBy annotations, creates proxy WebElement objects, and binds them to the WebDriver. Elements are lazily located on first interaction via proxy invocation handler.

Q15: How do you integrate ExtentReports with TestNG?

A: Create ExtentReports instance in @BeforeSuite. Implement ITestListener to call extent.createTest() on start, pass/fail on result, and extent.flush() on finish. Register listener in testng.xml.

Q16: What is the difference between @BeforeMethod and @BeforeClass?

A: @BeforeMethod runs before EACH test method — use for fresh browser launch. @BeforeClass runs once per class — use for expensive setup like DB connection or API auth token generation.

Q17: How do you handle authentication in API automation?

A: Store token in a Singleton AuthManager. Use REST Assured RequestSpecBuilder to add Authorization header. Refresh token in @BeforeSuite if it expires during long test runs.

Q18: What is Log4j and why use it over System.out.println?

A: Log4j provides log levels (DEBUG, INFO, WARN, ERROR), file/console output, timestamp formatting, and runtime configuration. Essential for debugging failed CI/CD runs where console output is the only evidence.

Q19: How do you version-control test data?

A: Store JSON/CSV/Properties in src/test/resources/ alongside code in Git. Data changes are tracked in pull requests. Sensitive data (passwords) goes in encrypted properties or CI/CD secrets, never in Git.

Q20: What is the role of BaseTest in a framework?

A: BaseTest is the parent of all test classes. It handles @BeforeMethod (launch browser, navigate to URL), @AfterMethod (screenshot on fail, quit driver), and @BeforeSuite (init reports). Tests inherit this setup/teardown automatically.

Q21: How do you handle file uploads in Selenium?

A: Use sendKeys(absoluteFilePath) on the file input element — Selenium bypasses the OS file dialog. Store test files in src/test/resources/testfiles/.

Q22: What is Selenium Grid and when do you use it?

A: Grid distributes tests across multiple machines/browsers. Hub receives tests; Nodes execute on specific browsers/OS. Use when you need parallel cross-browser execution at scale beyond local ThreadLocal parallelism.

Section 20: Top 200 Java Interview Questions for Automation Engineers

Grouped by topic. Each entry includes the question, a concise answer, what the interviewer expects, and a follow-up question to prepare for.

OOP — Class, Object, Constructor (Q1–Q10)

Q1: What is a class in Java?

Answer: A class is a blueprint that defines fields (attributes) and methods (behavior). In automation, LoginPage is a class defining locators and login actions.

Interviewer Expects: Blueprint analogy applied to page objects.

Follow-up: What is the difference between a class and an object?

Q2: What is an object in Java?

Answer: An object is a runtime instance of a class created with new. LoginPage loginPage = new LoginPage(driver) creates a LoginPage object bound to a WebDriver instance.

Interviewer Expects: Instance creation with real automation example.

Follow-up: How many objects can you create from one class?

Q3: What is a constructor?

Answer: A constructor initializes object state when new is called. Page objects use constructors to accept WebDriver: public LoginPage(WebDriver driver) { super(driver); }

Interviewer Expects: Constructor chaining with super() in page objects.

Follow-up: Can a constructor be private? Give an automation example.

Q4: What is constructor overloading?

Answer: Multiple constructors with different parameter lists in the same class. BrowserFactory could have BrowserFactory() and BrowserFactory(String browserName) for default vs specified browser.

Interviewer Expects: Practical overloading, not just definition.

Follow-up: Can constructors be inherited?

Q5: What is the default constructor?

Answer: Java provides a no-arg constructor if none is defined. Page objects typically define explicit constructors to require WebDriver, preventing accidental new LoginPage() without driver.

Interviewer Expects: Why explicit constructors matter in frameworks.

Follow-up: What happens if you define a parameterized constructor but no default?

Q6: What is this keyword?

Answer: Refers to the current object instance. In fluent POM, return this; enables method chaining: loginPage.enterUsername("admin").enterPassword("pass").

Interviewer Expects: Method chaining pattern in page objects.

Follow-up: What is the difference between this and super?

Q7: What is super keyword?

Answer: Refers to the parent class. super(driver) in LoginPage constructor calls BasePage constructor to initialize WebDriver, wait, and actions.

Interviewer Expects: Inheritance chain in POM hierarchy.

Follow-up: Can you call super() from a static method?

Q8: What is a static variable?

Answer: Belongs to the class, not any instance. Shared across all objects. Example: private static ConfigReader instance in Singleton — one config for entire framework.

Interviewer Expects: Static vs instance in Singleton/ConfigReader context.
