        int expectedSum = n * (n + 1) / 2;
        int actualSum = 0;
        for (int num : arr) actualSum += num;
        return expectedSum - actualSum;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        int[] testIds = {1, 2, 3, 5, 6, 7, 8}; // N=8, missing 4
        System.out.println("Missing test ID: TC_" + findMissing(testIds, 8));
        // Output: Missing test ID: TC_4
    }
}

Optimized — XOR:

public static int findMissingXOR(int[] arr, int n) {
    int xor = 0;
    for (int i = 1; i <= n; i++) xor ^= i;
    for (int num : arr) xor ^= num;
    return xor;
}

Time Complexity: O(n) | Space Complexity: O(1)

Interview Discussion: XOR avoids integer overflow for large N. Sum formula simpler but overflow risk with large arrays. Both are O(n).

4. Move Zeros to End

Problem Statement: Move all zeros to end while maintaining relative order of non-zero elements. Automation use: compact test result arrays removing skipped/null entries.

Approach: Two-pointer — one for iteration, one for next non-zero position.

Brute Force — New Array:

public class MoveZeros {
    public static int[] moveZeros(int[] arr) {
        int[] result = new int[arr.length];
        int idx = 0;
        for (int num : arr) {
            if (num != 0) result[idx++] = num;
        }
        return result;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        int[] results = {1, 0, 3, 0, 0, 5, 0, 7};
        int[] moved = moveZeros(results);
        System.out.println(java.util.Arrays.toString(moved));
        // Output: [1, 3, 5, 7, 0, 0, 0, 0]
    }
}

Optimized — In-Place Two Pointer:

public static void moveZerosInPlace(int[] arr) {
    int nonZero = 0;
    for (int i = 0; i < arr.length; i++) {
        if (arr[i] != 0) {
            int temp = arr[nonZero];
            arr[nonZero] = arr[i];
            arr[i] = temp;
            nonZero++;
        }
    }
}

Time Complexity: O(n) | Space Complexity: O(n) brute, O(1) in-place

Interview Discussion: In-place two-pointer is preferred. Minimize swaps — swap only when nonZero != i for better performance.

5. Find Duplicate Numbers

Problem Statement: Find duplicate numbers in array of 1 to N. Automation use: detect duplicate test case IDs in execution queue.

Approach: HashSet for detection, Floyd's cycle for O(1) space.

Brute Force — HashSet:

public class FindDuplicates {
    public static java.util.List<Integer> findDuplicates(int[] arr) {
        java.util.Set<Integer> seen = new java.util.HashSet<>();
        java.util.List<Integer> duplicates = new java.util.ArrayList<>();
        for (int num : arr) {
            if (!seen.add(num)) duplicates.add(num);
        }
        return duplicates;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        int[] testIds = {1, 3, 4, 2, 3, 5, 1, 7};
        System.out.println("Duplicate IDs: " + findDuplicates(testIds));
        // Output: Duplicate IDs: [3, 1]
    }
}

Optimized — Floyd's Cycle (for 1-N range):

public static int findDuplicateFloyd(int[] arr) {
    int slow = arr[0], fast = arr[0];
    do {
        slow = arr[slow];
        fast = arr[arr[fast]];
    } while (slow != fast);
    slow = arr[0];
    while (slow != fast) {
        slow = arr[slow];
        fast = arr[fast];
    }
    return slow;
}

Time Complexity: O(n) | Space Complexity: O(n) HashSet, O(1) Floyd

Interview Discussion: HashSet is simpler and handles multiple duplicates. Floyd's cycle works when array represents linked list (values 1-N, index as pointer). Know both approaches.

6. Maximum Difference (Buy-Sell Stock)

Problem Statement: Find maximum difference between two elements where larger comes after smaller. Automation use: find best time window for performance improvement (max response time drop).

Approach: Track minimum seen so far, calculate max difference at each step (Kadane's variant).

Brute Force — All Pairs:

public class MaxDifference {
    public static int maxDifference(int[] arr) {
        int maxDiff = 0;
        for (int i = 0; i < arr.length; i++) {
            for (int j = i + 1; j < arr.length; j++) {
                maxDiff = Math.max(maxDiff, arr[j] - arr[i]);
            }
        }
        return maxDiff;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        int[] responseTimes = {800, 650, 1200, 400, 900, 300, 1100};
        System.out.println("Max improvement window: " + maxDifference(responseTimes) + "ms");
        // Output: Max improvement window: 800ms (400-1200 or 300-1100)
    }
}

Optimized — Kadane's Approach:

public static int maxDifferenceOpt(int[] arr) {
    int minVal = arr[0], maxDiff = 0;
    for (int i = 1; i < arr.length; i++) {
        maxDiff = Math.max(maxDiff, arr[i] - minVal);
        minVal = Math.min(minVal, arr[i]);
    }
    return maxDiff;
}

Time Complexity: O(n²) brute, O(n) optimized | Space Complexity: O(1)

Interview Discussion: Classic "Best Time to Buy and Sell Stock" problem. Kadane's variant tracks running minimum. Return 0 if array is decreasing.

7. Rotate Array by K Positions

Problem Statement: Rotate array right by K positions. Automation use: rotate test execution order, circular buffer for test retry queue.

Approach: Reverse entire array, then reverse first K and rest separately.

Brute Force — One by One:

public class RotateArray {
    public static void rotate(int[] arr, int k) {
        k = k % arr.length;
        for (int i = 0; i < k; i++) {
            int last = arr[arr.length - 1];
            for (int j = arr.length - 1; j > 0; j--) {
                arr[j] = arr[j - 1];
            }
            arr[0] = last;
        }
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        int[] testOrder = {1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7};
        rotate(testOrder, 3);
        System.out.println(java.util.Arrays.toString(testOrder));
        // Output: [5, 6, 7, 1, 2, 3, 4]
    }
}

Optimized — Reverse Approach:

public static void rotateReverse(int[] arr, int k) {
    k = k % arr.length;
    reverse(arr, 0, arr.length - 1);
    reverse(arr, 0, k - 1);
    reverse(arr, k, arr.length - 1);
}
private static void reverse(int[] arr, int start, int end) {
    while (start < end) {
        int temp = arr[start];
        arr[start++] = arr[end];
        arr[end--] = temp;
    }
}

Time Complexity: O(n*k) brute, O(n) reverse | Space Complexity: O(1)

Interview Discussion: Reverse approach is elegant — explain three reverses. Handle k > array.length with k % n. Follow-up: rotate left instead of right?

Collections (4 Questions)

1. Sort Employees by Salary (Comparable)

Problem Statement: Sort employees by salary using Comparable. Automation use: sort test results by execution duration, prioritize test cases by severity.

Approach: Implement Comparable in Employee class, use Collections.sort().

Complete Code:

import java.util.*;

class TestResult implements Comparable<TestResult> {
    String testName;
    long durationMs;
    String status;

    TestResult(String name, long duration, String status) {
        this.testName = name; this.durationMs = duration; this.status = status;
    }

    @Override
    public int compareTo(TestResult other) {
        return Long.compare(this.durationMs, other.durationMs);
    }

    @Override
    public String toString() {
        return testName + " (" + durationMs + "ms, " + status + ")";
    }
}

public class SortBySalary {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        List<TestResult> results = new ArrayList<>(Arrays.asList(
            new TestResult("LoginTest", 1200, "PASS"),
            new TestResult("SearchTest", 450, "PASS"),
            new TestResult("CheckoutTest", 3200, "FAIL"),
            new TestResult("ProfileTest", 890, "PASS")
        ));
        Collections.sort(results);
        System.out.println("Sorted by duration (fastest first):");
        results.forEach(System.out::println);
        // Output: SearchTest (450ms) → ProfileTest (890ms) → LoginTest (1200ms) → CheckoutTest (3200ms)
    }
}

Time Complexity: O(n log n) | Space Complexity: O(1)

Interview Discussion: Comparable for natural ordering (one sort criteria). Comparator for multiple/alternative sort orders. compareTo must be consistent with equals.

2. Sort HashMap by Value

Problem Statement: Sort HashMap entries by value. Automation use: rank pages by failure count, sort API endpoints by response time.

Approach: Stream entrySet, sort by value, collect to LinkedHashMap.

Complete Code:

import java.util.*;
import java.util.stream.*;

public class SortMapByValue {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Map<String, Integer> failureCount = new HashMap<>();
        failureCount.put("LoginPage", 12);
        failureCount.put("SearchPage", 3);
        failureCount.put("CheckoutPage", 25);
        failureCount.put("ProfilePage", 7);

        Map<String, Integer> sorted = failureCount.entrySet().stream()
            .sorted(Map.Entry.comparingByValue())
            .collect(Collectors.toMap(
                Map.Entry::getKey, Map.Entry::getValue,
                (a, b) -> a, LinkedHashMap::new));

        System.out.println("Pages ranked by failures (least first):");
        sorted.forEach((page, count) ->
            System.out.println("  " + page + " → " + count + " failures"));
        // Output: SearchPage→3, ProfilePage→7, LoginPage→12, CheckoutPage→25
    }
}

Time Complexity: O(n log n) | Space Complexity: O(n)

Interview Discussion: LinkedHashMap preserves sorted order. reversed() for descending. TreeMap natural order alternative if keys should be sorted.

3. Word Count in Paragraph

Problem Statement: Count word frequencies in a paragraph. Automation use: analyze test log output, count error message occurrences.

Approach: Split by whitespace, HashMap frequency count.

Complete Code:

import java.util.*;

public class WordCount {
    public static Map<String, Integer> countWords(String paragraph) {
        Map<String, Integer> wordCount = new HashMap<>();
        for (String word : paragraph.toLowerCase().split("\\s+")) {
            word = word.replaceAll("[^a-zA-Z0-9]", "");
            if (!word.isEmpty()) {
                wordCount.merge(word, 1, Integer::sum);
            }
        }
        return wordCount;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        String log = "Test FAILED on LoginPage Test FAILED on CheckoutPage " +
                     "Test PASSED on SearchPage Test FAILED on LoginPage";
        countWords(log).entrySet().stream()
            .sorted(Map.Entry.<String, Integer>comparingByValue().reversed())
            .forEach(e -> System.out.println(e.getKey() + " → " + e.getValue()));
        // Output: test→4, failed→3, on→4, loginpage→2, ...
    }
}

Time Complexity: O(n) | Space Complexity: O(k) unique words

Interview Discussion: Handle punctuation with regex cleanup. Case-insensitive with toLowerCase(). Stream groupingBy as alternative one-liner.

4. Remove Duplicates Preserving Order

Problem Statement: Remove duplicates from list while maintaining insertion order. Automation use: deduplicate test case names while preserving execution order.

Approach: LinkedHashSet automatically deduplicates with order preservation.

Complete Code:

import java.util.*;
import java.util.stream.*;

public class RemoveDuplicates {
    public static List<String> removeDuplicates(List<String> testNames) {
        return new ArrayList<>(new LinkedHashSet<>(testNames));
    }

    public static List<String> removeDuplicatesStream(List<String> testNames) {
        return testNames.stream().distinct().collect(Collectors.toList());
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        List<String> tests = Arrays.asList(
            "LoginTest", "SearchTest", "LoginTest", "CheckoutTest",
            "SearchTest", "ProfileTest", "LoginTest");
        System.out.println("Original: " + tests);
        System.out.println("Deduped:  " + removeDuplicates(tests));
        // Output: Deduped: [LoginTest, SearchTest, CheckoutTest, ProfileTest]
    }
}

Time Complexity: O(n) | Space Complexity: O(n)

Interview Discussion: LinkedHashSet is the cleanest approach. Stream distinct() also preserves order (since Java 8). HashSet loses order — wrong answer if order matters.

Java 8 Streams (4 Questions)

1. Stream Sorting (Multiple Criteria)

Problem Statement: Sort test results by status (FAIL first) then by duration (longest first). Automation use: prioritize failed tests in report, then slowest.

Approach: Comparator chaining with thenComparing().

Complete Code:

import java.util.*;
import java.util.stream.*;

public class StreamMultiSort {
    static class TestResult {
        String name; String status; long durationMs;
        TestResult(String n, String s, long d) { name=n; status=s; durationMs=d; }
        public String toString() { return name + " [" + status + ", " + durationMs + "ms]"; }
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        List<TestResult> results = Arrays.asList(
            new TestResult("LoginTest", "PASS", 1200),
            new TestResult("CheckoutTest", "FAIL", 3200),
            new TestResult("SearchTest", "PASS", 450),
            new TestResult("ProfileTest", "FAIL", 890),
            new TestResult("CartTest", "FAIL", 1500)
        );

        results.stream()
            .sorted(Comparator
                .comparing((TestResult r) -> r.status.equals("PASS") ? 1 : 0)
                .thenComparing(r -> r.durationMs, Comparator.reverseOrder()))
            .forEach(System.out::println);
        // Output: CheckoutTest [FAIL, 3200ms] → CartTest [FAIL, 1500ms] →
        //         ProfileTest [FAIL, 890ms] → LoginTest [PASS, 1200ms] → SearchTest [PASS, 450ms]
    }
}

Time Complexity: O(n log n) | Space Complexity: O(n)

Interview Discussion: Comparator.comparing() + thenComparing() for multi-field sort. reversed() for descending. Method references vs lambdas in comparators.

2. Stream Filtering (Complex Conditions)

Problem Statement: Filter test results that FAILED with duration > 1000ms and name contains "Test". Automation use: identify slow failing tests for investigation.

Approach: Predicate composition with and/or/negate.

Complete Code:

import java.util.*;
import java.util.stream.*;
import java.util.function.Predicate;

public class StreamFilter {
    static class TestResult {
        String name; String status; long durationMs;
        TestResult(String n, String s, long d) { name=n; status=s; durationMs=d; }
        public String toString() { return name + " [" + status + ", " + durationMs + "ms]"; }
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        List<TestResult> results = Arrays.asList(
            new TestResult("LoginTest", "FAIL", 1200),
            new TestResult("SearchTest", "PASS", 450),
            new TestResult("CheckoutTest", "FAIL", 3200),
            new TestResult("APIHealth", "FAIL", 200),
            new TestResult("ProfileTest", "FAIL", 890)
        );

        Predicate<TestResult> isFailed = r -> r.status.equals("FAIL");
        Predicate<TestResult> isSlow = r -> r.durationMs > 1000;
        Predicate<TestResult> hasTest = r -> r.name.contains("Test");

        System.out.println("Slow failing tests:");
        results.stream()
            .filter(isFailed.and(isSlow).and(hasTest))
            .forEach(System.out::println);
        // Output: LoginTest [FAIL, 1200ms], CheckoutTest [FAIL, 3200ms]
    }
}

Time Complexity: O(n) | Space Complexity: O(1)

Interview Discussion: Predicate.and/or/negate for readable complex filters. Extract predicates as named variables for clarity. Alternative: single lambda with && operators.

3. Grouping by Department

Problem Statement: Group test cases by module/department. Automation use: group test results by page module for per-module pass/fail summary.

Approach: Collectors.groupingBy() with optional downstream collector.

Complete Code:

import java.util.*;
import java.util.stream.*;

public class StreamGrouping {
    static class TestCase {
        String name; String module; String status;
        TestCase(String n, String m, String s) { name=n; module=m; status=s; }
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        List<TestCase> tests = Arrays.asList(
            new TestCase("testLogin", "Auth", "PASS"),
            new TestCase("testLogout", "Auth", "PASS"),
            new TestCase("testSearch", "Search", "FAIL"),
            new TestCase("testFilter", "Search", "PASS"),
            new TestCase("testCheckout", "Cart", "FAIL"),
            new TestCase("testAddToCart", "Cart", "PASS")
        );

        Map<String, List<TestCase>> byModule =
            tests.stream().collect(Collectors.groupingBy(t -> t.module));

        byModule.forEach((module, cases) -> {
            long failed = cases.stream().filter(t -> t.status.equals("FAIL")).count();
            System.out.println(module + ": " + cases.size() + " tests, " + failed + " failed");
        });
        // Output: Auth: 2 tests, 0 failed
        //         Search: 2 tests, 1 failed
        //         Cart: 2 tests, 1 failed
    }
}

Time Complexity: O(n) | Space Complexity: O(n)

Interview Discussion: groupingBy with counting downstream: groupingBy(module, counting()). partitioningBy for binary split (pass/fail). Multi-level grouping with nested groupingBy.

4. Counting Elements by Category

Problem Statement: Count test results by status category (PASS/FAIL/SKIP). Automation use: generate test summary dashboard counts.

Approach: groupingBy + counting downstream collector.

Complete Code:

import java.util.*;
import java.util.stream.*;

public class StreamCounting {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        List<String> testStatuses = Arrays.asList(
            "PASS", "PASS", "FAIL", "PASS", "SKIP",
            "FAIL", "PASS", "FAIL", "SKIP", "PASS",
            "PASS", "FAIL", "PASS", "PASS", "SKIP"
        );

        Map<String, Long> statusCounts = testStatuses.stream()
            .collect(Collectors.groupingBy(s -> s, Collectors.counting()));

        System.out.println("=== Test Execution Summary ===");
        statusCounts.forEach((status, count) ->
            System.out.printf("  %-6s: %d (%.1f%%)%n", status, count,
                count * 100.0 / testStatuses.size()));

        long totalFailed = statusCounts.getOrDefault("FAIL", 0L);
        System.out.println("\nPass rate: " +
            String.format("%.1f%%", (1 - totalFailed * 1.0 / testStatuses.size()) * 100));
        // Output: PASS: 8 (53.3%), FAIL: 4 (26.7%), SKIP: 3 (20.0%)
        //         Pass rate: 73.3%
    }
}

Time Complexity: O(n) | Space Complexity: O(k) categories

Interview Discussion: groupingBy + counting is the idiomatic Java 8 approach. Alternative: Collectors.counting() vs manual increment. Follow-up: count by module AND status (multi-level grouping).

Interview Tip: Always mention automation context when solving coding problems — "I'd use this HashMap frequency count to detect duplicate test IDs" shows you connect Java fundamentals to real testing work. Interviewers value domain awareness over pure algorithm memorization.

Section 22: SDET Coding Rounds — Company-Wise Questions

Top 50 coding questions from real SDET and automation interviews at major service and product companies. Each solution is runnable Java with framework context where relevant.

How to use: Practice writing each solution on paper first, then relate it to your framework — HashMap for test data lookup, ThreadLocal for parallel WebDriver, Stream API for report filtering.

INFOSYS / TCS / WIPRO (Entry–Mid Level)

Q1. Reverse a String

FieldDetails
CompanyInfosys, TCS, Wipro
QuestionReverse a given string and return the result.
ApproachTwo pointers on char array swapping from both ends; or StringBuilder.reverse().
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(n) for new char array
Interview TipMention String immutability — cannot reverse in-place on String object itself.

Step-by-Step Explanation

  1. Convert String to char[] for mutability.
  2. Set left=0, right=length-1; swap and move inward.
  3. Return new String from char array.

Complete Solution Code

public class ReverseString {
    public static String reverse(String input) {
        if (input == null) return null;
        char[] chars = input.toCharArray();
        int left = 0, right = chars.length - 1;
        while (left < right) {
            char temp = chars[left];
            chars[left++] = chars[right];
            chars[right--] = temp;
        }
        return new String(chars);
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(reverse("automation")); // noitamotua
    }
}

Alternative Approach

new StringBuilder(input).reverse().toString() — one line but allocates StringBuilder object.

Q2. Check Palindrome

FieldDetails
CompanyInfosys, TCS, Wipro
QuestionDetermine if a string reads the same forward and backward.
ApproachTwo-pointer comparison; optionally skip non-alphanumeric and ignore case.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipClarify whether spaces and punctuation matter — common follow-up.

Step-by-Step Explanation

  1. Use two pointers from both ends.
  2. Skip non-alphanumeric characters if required.
  3. Compare lowercase chars; return false on mismatch.

Complete Solution Code

public class PalindromeCheck {
    public static boolean isPalindrome(String s) {
        if (s == null) return false;
        int l = 0, r = s.length() - 1;
        while (l < r) {
            while (l < r && !Character.isLetterOrDigit(s.charAt(l))) l++;
            while (l < r && !Character.isLetterOrDigit(s.charAt(r))) r--;
            if (Character.toLowerCase(s.charAt(l++)) != Character.toLowerCase(s.charAt(r--)))
                return false;
        }
        return true;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(isPalindrome("A man a plan a canal Panama"));
    }
}

Q3. Find Factorial

FieldDetails
CompanyInfosys, TCS, Wipro
QuestionCompute n! iteratively or recursively.
ApproachIterative loop from 2 to n — avoids stack overflow.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipUse long for n > 12; relate to combinatorial test case generation.

Step-by-Step Explanation

  1. Handle n=0 and n=1 returning 1.
  2. Multiply result from 2 to n.
  3. Return factorial value.

Complete Solution Code

public class Factorial {
    public static long factorial(int n) {
        if (n < 0) throw new IllegalArgumentException("n must be >= 0");
        long result = 1;
        for (int i = 2; i <= n; i++) result *= i;
        return result;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(factorial(5)); // 120
    }
}

Alternative Approach

Recursive: factorial(n-1) * n — O(n) time, O(n) stack space.

Q4. Fibonacci Series

FieldDetails
CompanyInfosys, TCS, Wipro
QuestionPrint first n Fibonacci numbers or return nth value.
ApproachIterative with two variables — optimal for interviews.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipAvoid naive recursion O(2^n); mention memoization if asked.

Step-by-Step Explanation

  1. Initialize a=0, b=1.
  2. Loop n times: print a, then shift a,b to next pair.
  3. For nth value, loop until index n.

Complete Solution Code

public class Fibonacci {
    public static void printSeries(int n) {
        int a = 0, b = 1;
        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
            System.out.print(a + " ");
            int next = a + b; a = b; b = next;
        }
    }
    public static int nth(int n) {
        if (n <= 1) return n;
        int a = 0, b = 1;
        for (int i = 2; i <= n; i++) {
            int next = a + b; a = b; b = next;
        }
        return b;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        printSeries(10);
        System.out.println("\n10th: " + nth(10));
    }
}

Q5. Count Vowels and Consonants

FieldDetails
CompanyInfosys, TCS, Wipro
QuestionCount vowels and consonants in a string.
ApproachSingle pass checking each letter against vowel set.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipUseful for validating random test data generators in frameworks.

Step-by-Step Explanation

  1. Define vowel string a,e,i,o,u (case insensitive).
  2. Iterate chars; increment vowel or consonant counter.
  3. Return int array with both counts.

Complete Solution Code

public class VowelConsonantCount {
    public static int[] count(String s) {
        int vowels = 0, consonants = 0;
        String v = "aeiouAEIOU";
        for (char c : s.toCharArray()) {
            if (Character.isLetter(c)) {
                if (v.indexOf(c) >= 0) vowels++;
                else consonants++;
            }
        }
        return new int[]{vowels, consonants};
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        int[] r = count("Automation Framework");
        System.out.println("Vowels: " + r[0] + ", Consonants: " + r[1]);
    }
}

FieldDetails

QuestionSwap two integers without a third variable.
ApproachXOR swap or arithmetic add/subtract.
Time ComplexityO(1)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipMention overflow risk with arithmetic; XOR works cleanly for integers.

Step-by-Step Explanation

  1. Apply XOR: a = a ^ b; b = a ^ b; a = a ^ b.
  2. Verify with sample values.
  3. Discuss readability vs cleverness trade-off.

Complete Solution Code

public class SwapWithoutTemp {

        int a = 10, b = 20;
        a = a ^ b; b = a ^ b; a = a ^ b;

Q7. Check Prime Number

FieldDetails
CompanyInfosys, TCS, Wipro
QuestionReturn true if n is a prime number.
ApproachCheck divisibility from 2 to sqrt(n); skip even numbers after 2.
Time ComplexityO(sqrt n)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipEdge cases: n <= 1 false, n == 2 true.

Step-by-Step Explanation

  1. Return false for n < 2.
  2. Return false if n is even (except 2).
  3. Test odd divisors from 3 to sqrt(n).

Complete Solution Code

public class PrimeCheck {
    public static boolean isPrime(int n) {
        if (n <= 1) return false;
        if (n == 2) return true;
        if (n % 2 == 0) return false;
        for (int i = 3; i * i <= n; i += 2)
            if (n % i == 0) return false;
        return true;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(isPrime(29));
    }
}

Q8. Find Largest in Array

FieldDetails
CompanyInfosys, TCS, Wipro
QuestionReturn the maximum element in an integer array.
ApproachSingle pass tracking running maximum.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipRelate to finding max wait timeout from a config list.

Step-by-Step Explanation

  1. Initialize max = arr[0].
  2. Compare each element and update max.
  3. Return max.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.Arrays;
public class FindLargest {
    public static int findMax(int[] arr) {
        if (arr == null || arr.length == 0)
            throw new IllegalArgumentException("Empty array");
        int max = arr[0];
        for (int n : arr) if (n > max) max = n;
        return max;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(findMax(new int[]{3, 9, 1, 7}));
    }
}

Alternative Approach

Arrays.stream(arr).max().orElseThrow() — concise Java 8 style.

Q9. Sort Array (Bubble Sort)

FieldDetails
CompanyInfosys, TCS, Wipro
QuestionSort an integer array in ascending order.
ApproachBubble sort — swap adjacent elements; early exit if no swaps.
Time ComplexityO(n²)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipMention Arrays.sort() uses TimSort O(n log n) in production code.

Step-by-Step Explanation

  1. Outer loop for number of passes.
  2. Inner loop compares arr[j] and arr[j+1]; swap if out of order.
  3. Break early if no swaps in a pass.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.Arrays;
public class BubbleSort {
    public static void sort(int[] arr) {
        for (int i = 0; i < arr.length - 1; i++) {
            boolean swapped = false;
            for (int j = 0; j < arr.length - 1 - i; j++) {
                if (arr[j] > arr[j + 1]) {
                    int t = arr[j]; arr[j] = arr[j + 1]; arr[j + 1] = t;
                    swapped = true;
                }
            }
            if (!swapped) break;
        }
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        int[] a = {5, 1, 4, 2};
        sort(a);
        System.out.println(Arrays.toString(a));
    }
}

Q10. Find Duplicate in Array

FieldDetails
CompanyInfosys, TCS, Wipro
QuestionFind duplicate in array of n+1 elements containing values 1..n.
ApproachHashSet tracks seen elements; Floyd cycle for O(1) space variant.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(n)
Interview TipFramework link: detect duplicate test IDs in DataProvider list.

Step-by-Step Explanation

  1. Create HashSet for seen values.
  2. If add() returns false, element is duplicate.
  3. Return duplicate value.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.HashSet;
import java.util.Set;
public class FindDuplicate {
    public static int findDuplicate(int[] nums) {
        Set<Integer> seen = new HashSet<>();
        for (int n : nums) {
            if (!seen.add(n)) return n;
        }
        throw new IllegalArgumentException("No duplicate");
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(findDuplicate(new int[]{1, 3, 4, 2, 2}));
    }
}

Alternative Approach

Floyd tortoise-hare on index-as-pointer graph — O(1) space.

COGNIZANT / CAPGEMINI / ACCENTURE (Mid Level)

Q11. Find Second Largest in Array

FieldDetails
CompanyCognizant, Capgemini, Accenture
QuestionFind the second largest distinct element in an array.
ApproachTrack largest and secondLargest in one pass.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipHandle duplicates and arrays with fewer than 2 distinct elements.

Step-by-Step Explanation

  1. Initialize first and second to Integer.MIN_VALUE.
  2. Update both when finding a new maximum.
  3. Return second; throw if not found.

Complete Solution Code

public class SecondLargest {
    public static int findSecond(int[] arr) {
        int first = Integer.MIN_VALUE, second = Integer.MIN_VALUE;
        for (int n : arr) {
            if (n > first) { second = first; first = n; }
            else if (n > second && n != first) second = n;
        }
        if (second == Integer.MIN_VALUE) throw new IllegalStateException("No second largest");
        return second;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(findSecond(new int[]{12, 35, 1, 10, 35}));
    }
}

Q12. Remove Duplicates from String

FieldDetails
CompanyCognizant, Capgemini, Accenture
QuestionRemove duplicate characters preserving insertion order.
ApproachLinkedHashSet maintains order while deduplicating.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(n)
Interview TipSimilar to deduplicating test case names before suite execution.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.LinkedHashSet;
public class RemoveDuplicatesString {
    public static String removeDuplicates(String s) {
        LinkedHashSet<Character> set = new LinkedHashSet<>();
        for (char c : s.toCharArray()) set.add(c);
        StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder();
        for (char c : set) sb.append(c);
        return sb.toString();
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(removeDuplicates("programming"));
    }
}

Q13. Anagram Check

FieldDetails
CompanyCognizant, Capgemini, Accenture
QuestionCheck if two strings are anagrams.
ApproachCount char frequencies in int[26] or HashMap.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(1) for fixed alphabet
Interview TipSort approach is O(n log n) — mention both.

Complete Solution Code

public class AnagramCheck {
    public static boolean isAnagram(String a, String b) {
        if (a.length() != b.length()) return false;
        int[] count = new int[26];
        for (char c : a.toCharArray()) count[c - 'a']++;
        for (char c : b.toCharArray()) if (--count[c - 'a'] < 0) return false;
        return true;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(isAnagram("listen", "silent"));
    }
}

Q14. Find Missing Number in Array

FieldDetails
CompanyCognizant, Capgemini, Accenture
QuestionArray contains 1..n with one missing; find it.
ApproachGauss sum formula: expected - actual.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipXOR all indices and values for same complexity.

Complete Solution Code

public class MissingNumber {
    public static int findMissing(int[] arr, int n) {
        int expected = n * (n + 1) / 2;
        int actual = 0;
        for (int x : arr) actual += x;
        return expected - actual;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(findMissing(new int[]{1, 2, 4, 5}, 5));
    }
}

Q15. Two Sum Problem

FieldDetails
CompanyCognizant, Capgemini, Accenture
QuestionFind indices of two numbers that sum to target.
ApproachHashMap stores complement -> index.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(n)
Interview TipState brute force O(n²) first, then optimize.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.*;
public class TwoSum {
    public static int[] twoSum(int[] nums, int target) {
        Map<Integer, Integer> map = new HashMap<>();
        for (int i = 0; i < nums.length; i++) {
            int need = target - nums[i];
            if (map.containsKey(need)) return new int[]{map.get(need), i};
            map.put(nums[i], i);
        }
        throw new IllegalArgumentException("No solution");
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(Arrays.toString(twoSum(new int[]{2,7,11,15}, 9)));
    }
}

Q16. Reverse Words in Sentence

FieldDetails
CompanyCognizant, Capgemini, Accenture
QuestionReverse word order: "hello world" -> "world hello".
ApproachSplit, two-pointer swap words, join.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(n)
Interview TipUsed when parsing log lines or BDD step text.

Complete Solution Code

public class ReverseWords {
    public static String reverseWords(String s) {
        String[] words = s.trim().split("\\s+");
        int l = 0, r = words.length - 1;
        while (l < r) { String t = words[l]; words[l++] = words[r]; words[r--] = t; }
        return String.join(" ", words);
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(reverseWords("  automation   test  suite  "));
    }
}

Q17. Character Frequency using HashMap

FieldDetails
CompanyCognizant, Capgemini, Accenture
QuestionCount frequency of each character in a string.
ApproachHashMap.merge or getOrDefault increment pattern.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(k) unique chars
Interview TipCount failure types from test report strings.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.*;
public class CharFrequency {
    public static Map<Character, Integer> frequency(String s) {
        Map<Character, Integer> map = new HashMap<>();
        for (char c : s.toCharArray()) map.merge(c, 1, Integer::sum);
        return map;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(frequency("selenium"));
    }
}

Q18. First Non-Repeated Character

FieldDetails
CompanyCognizant, Capgemini, Accenture
QuestionFind the first character with frequency 1.
ApproachLinkedHashMap for ordered single-pass counting.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(k)
Interview TipTwo-pass with HashMap also acceptable.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.*;
public class FirstNonRepeated {
    public static Character firstNonRepeated(String s) {
        LinkedHashMap<Character, Integer> map = new LinkedHashMap<>();
        for (char c : s.toCharArray()) map.merge(c, 1, Integer::sum);
        for (Map.Entry<Character, Integer> e : map.entrySet())
            if (e.getValue() == 1) return e.getKey();
        return null;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(firstNonRepeated("swiss"));
    }
}

Q19. Sort HashMap by Value

FieldDetails
CompanyCognizant, Capgemini, Accenture
QuestionSort map entries by value descending.
ApproachStream sorted with Map.Entry.comparingByValue.
Time ComplexityO(n log n)
Space ComplexityO(n)
Interview TipSort test failure counts for triage dashboards.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.*;
import java.util.stream.*;
public class SortHashMapByValue {
    public static Map<String, Integer> sortByValue(Map<String, Integer> map) {
        return map.entrySet().stream()
            .sorted(Map.Entry.<String, Integer>comparingByValue().reversed())
            .collect(Collectors.toMap(Map.Entry::getKey, Map.Entry::getValue,
                (a, b) -> a, LinkedHashMap::new));
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Map<String, Integer> m = new HashMap<>();
        m.put("LoginTest", 5); m.put("CheckoutTest", 12);
        System.out.println(sortByValue(m));
    }
}

Q20. Merge Two Sorted Arrays

FieldDetails
CompanyCognizant, Capgemini, Accenture
QuestionMerge two sorted arrays into one sorted array.
ApproachTwo pointers compare and copy smaller element.
Time ComplexityO(m + n)
Space ComplexityO(m + n)
Interview TipMerge sorted test result lists from parallel CI jobs.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.Arrays;
public class MergeSortedArrays {
    public static int[] merge(int[] a, int[] b) {
        int[] result = new int[a.length + b.length];
        int i = 0, j = 0, k = 0;
        while (i < a.length && j < b.length)
            result[k++] = (a[i] <= b[j]) ? a[i++] : b[j++];
        while (i < a.length) result[k++] = a[i++];
        while (j < b.length) result[k++] = b[j++];
        return result;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(Arrays.toString(merge(new int[]{1,3,5}, new int[]{2,4,6})));
    }
}

EPAM / GLOBANT / LTIMINDTREE (Senior Level)

Q21. Longest Substring Without Repeating

FieldDetails
CompanyEPAM, Globant, LTIMindtree
QuestionFind length of longest substring with all unique characters.
ApproachSliding window with HashSet; shrink on duplicate.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(min(n, m)) charset size
Interview TipSliding window pattern applies to rate-limit testing windows.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.*;
public class LongestSubstring {
    public static int lengthOfLongest(String s) {
        Set<Character> set = new HashSet<>();
        int max = 0, left = 0;
        for (int right = 0; right < s.length(); right++) {
            while (set.contains(s.charAt(right))) set.remove(s.charAt(left++));
            set.add(s.charAt(right));
            max = Math.max(max, right - left + 1);
        }
        return max;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(lengthOfLongest("abcabcbb"));
    }
}

Q22. Valid Parentheses (Stack)

FieldDetails
CompanyEPAM, Globant, LTIMindtree
QuestionValidate balanced brackets: (), {}, [].
ApproachStack push opening; pop and match on closing.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(n)
Interview TipStack models nested TestNG group/suite structure.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.*;
public class ValidParentheses {
    public static boolean isValid(String s) {
        Map<Character, Character> map = Map.of(')', '(', '}', '{', ']', '[');
        Deque<Character> stack = new ArrayDeque<>();
        for (char c : s.toCharArray()) {
            if (map.containsValue(c)) stack.push(c);
            else if (map.containsKey(c)) {
                if (stack.isEmpty() || stack.pop() != map.get(c)) return false;
            }
        }
        return stack.isEmpty();
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(isValid("{[()]}"));
    }
}

Q23. Move Zeros to End

FieldDetails
CompanyEPAM, Globant, LTIMindtree
QuestionMove all zeros to end preserving non-zero order.
ApproachTwo-pointer write index for non-zero elements.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipIn-place compaction like filtering null WebDriver references.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.Arrays;
public class MoveZeros {
    public static void moveZeroes(int[] nums) {
        int w = 0;
        for (int n : nums) if (n != 0) nums[w++] = n;
        while (w < nums.length) nums[w++] = 0;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        int[] a = {0,1,0,3,12};
        moveZeroes(a);
        System.out.println(Arrays.toString(a));
    }
}

Q24. Maximum Subarray Sum (Kadane's)

FieldDetails
CompanyEPAM, Globant, LTIMindtree
QuestionFind maximum sum of contiguous subarray.
ApproachTrack currentMax and globalMax at each index.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipClassic DP — explain subproblem at each index.

Complete Solution Code

public class MaxSubarray {
    public static int maxSubArray(int[] nums) {
        int current = nums[0], best = nums[0];
        for (int i = 1; i < nums.length; i++) {
            current = Math.max(nums[i], current + nums[i]);
            best = Math.max(best, current);
        }
        return best;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(maxSubArray(new int[]{-2,1,-3,4,-1,2,1,-5,4}));
    }
}

Q25. Rotate Array by K Positions

FieldDetails
CompanyEPAM, Globant, LTIMindtree
QuestionRotate array right by k steps.
ApproachReverse entire array, then reverse two segments.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipCircular buffer pattern in retry queues.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.Arrays;
public class RotateArray {
    private static void reverse(int[] a, int l, int r) {
        while (l < r) { int t = a[l]; a[l++] = a[r]; a[r--] = t; }
    }
    public static void rotate(int[] nums, int k) {
        if (nums.length == 0) return;
        k %= nums.length;
        reverse(nums, 0, nums.length - 1);
        reverse(nums, 0, k - 1);
        reverse(nums, k, nums.length - 1);
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        int[] a = {1,2,3,4,5,6,7};
        rotate(a, 3);
        System.out.println(Arrays.toString(a));
    }
}

Q26. Group Anagrams using HashMap

FieldDetails
CompanyEPAM, Globant, LTIMindtree
QuestionGroup strings that are anagrams of each other.
ApproachKey = sorted string or char-count signature.
Time ComplexityO(n * k log k)
Space ComplexityO(n * k)
Interview TipGroup test methods by feature tag in custom runners.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.*;
public class GroupAnagrams {
    public static List<List<String>> group(String[] words) {
        Map<String, List<String>> map = new HashMap<>();
        for (String w : words) {
            char[] c = w.toCharArray();
            Arrays.sort(c);
            String key = new String(c);
            map.computeIfAbsent(key, k -> new ArrayList<>()).add(w);
        }
        return new ArrayList<>(map.values());
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(group(new String[]{"eat","tea","tan","ate","nat","bat"}));
    }
}

Q27. Find Intersection of Two Arrays

FieldDetails
CompanyEPAM, Globant, LTIMindtree
QuestionReturn unique common elements between two arrays.
ApproachHashSet for arr1; check arr2 membership.
Time ComplexityO(m + n)
Space ComplexityO(m)
Interview TipFind common tags between two test suites.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.*;
public class ArrayIntersection {
    public static List<Integer> intersect(int[] a, int[] b) {
        Set<Integer> set = new HashSet<>();
        for (int x : a) set.add(x);
        Set<Integer> result = new HashSet<>();
        for (int x : b) if (set.contains(x)) result.add(x);
        return new ArrayList<>(result);
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(intersect(new int[]{1,2,2,1}, new int[]{2,2}));
    }
}

Q28. String Compression

FieldDetails
CompanyEPAM, Globant, LTIMindtree
QuestionCompress "aabcc" to "a2b1c2".
ApproachCount consecutive same characters in one pass.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(n)
Interview TipRun-length encoding for compact log storage.

Complete Solution Code

public class StringCompression {
    public static String compress(String s) {
        if (s.isEmpty()) return s;
        StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder();
        int count = 1;
        for (int i = 1; i <= s.length(); i++) {
            if (i < s.length() && s.charAt(i) == s.charAt(i - 1)) count++;
            else { sb.append(s.charAt(i - 1)).append(count); count = 1; }
        }
        return sb.toString();
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(compress("aabcccccaaa"));
    }
}

Q30. Find Pairs with Given Sum

FieldDetails

QuestionPrint all pairs in array summing to target.
ApproachHashSet tracks seen; check target - num.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(n)
Interview TipPairwise config keys for matrix testing.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.*;
public class PairsWithSum {
    public static void findPairs(int[] arr, int target) {
        Set<Integer> seen = new HashSet<>();
        for (int n : arr) {
            if (seen.contains(target - n)) System.out.println((target - n) + " + " + n);
            seen.add(n);
        }
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        findPairs(new int[]{1, 5, 7, -1, 5}, 6);
    }
}

Q31. Two Sum with HashMap O(n)

FieldDetails
CompanyAmazon, Google, Microsoft
QuestionOptimal Two Sum — single pass HashMap.
ApproachStore value->index; lookup complement each step.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(n)
Interview TipAlways state brute force first, then optimize — product pattern.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.*;
public class TwoSumOptimal {
    public static int[] twoSum(int[] nums, int target) {
        Map<Integer, Integer> idx = new HashMap<>();
        for (int i = 0; i < nums.length; i++) {
            int comp = target - nums[i];
            if (idx.containsKey(comp)) return new int[]{idx.get(comp), i};
            idx.put(nums[i], i);
        }
        return new int[]{};
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(Arrays.toString(twoSum(new int[]{3,2,4}, 6)));
    }
}

Q32. Three Sum Problem

FieldDetails
CompanyAmazon, Google, Flipkart
QuestionFind all unique triplets summing to zero.
ApproachSort + fix one element + two-pointer on remainder.
Time ComplexityO(n²)
Space ComplexityO(1) excluding output
Interview TipSkip duplicate values at i, lo, hi to avoid duplicate triplets.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.*;
public class ThreeSum {
    public static List<List<Integer>> threeSum(int[] nums) {
        Arrays.sort(nums);
        List<List<Integer>> res = new ArrayList<>();
        for (int i = 0; i < nums.length - 2; i++) {
            if (i > 0 && nums[i] == nums[i-1]) continue;
            int lo = i + 1, hi = nums.length - 1;
            while (lo < hi) {
                int sum = nums[i] + nums[lo] + nums[hi];
                if (sum == 0) {
                    res.add(Arrays.asList(nums[i], nums[lo], nums[hi]));
                    while (lo < hi && nums[lo] == nums[lo+1]) lo++;
                    while (lo < hi && nums[hi] == nums[hi-1]) hi--;
                    lo++; hi--;
                } else if (sum < 0) lo++; else hi--;
            }
        }
        return res;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(threeSum(new int[]{-1,0,1,2,-1,-4}));
    }
}

Q33. Sliding Window Maximum

FieldDetails
CompanyAmazon, Microsoft
QuestionFind max in each sliding window of size k.
ApproachMonotonic deque storing indices in decreasing value order.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(k)
Interview TipAdvanced but frequently asked at product companies.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.*;
public class SlidingWindowMax {
    public static int[] maxSlidingWindow(int[] nums, int k) {
        Deque<Integer> dq = new ArrayDeque<>();
        int[] result = new int[nums.length - k + 1];
        for (int i = 0; i < nums.length; i++) {
            while (!dq.isEmpty() && dq.peekFirst() <= i - k) dq.pollFirst();
            while (!dq.isEmpty() && nums[dq.peekLast()] <= nums[i]) dq.pollLast();
            dq.offerLast(i);
            if (i >= k - 1) result[i - k + 1] = nums[dq.peekFirst()];
        }
        return result;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(Arrays.toString(maxSlidingWindow(new int[]{1,3,-1,-3,5,3,6,7}, 3)));
    }
}

Q34. LRU Cache Design

FieldDetails
CompanyGoogle, Amazon
QuestionDesign LRU cache with O(1) get and put.
ApproachHashMap + doubly linked list for order.
Time ComplexityO(1) per operation
Space ComplexityO(capacity)
Interview TipSame pattern as caching Page Object elements or API responses.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.*;
public class LRUCache {
    class Node { int key, val; Node prev, next; Node(int k, int v){key=k;val=v;} }
    private final int cap;
    private final Map<Integer, Node> map = new HashMap<>();
    private final Node head = new Node(0,0), tail = new Node(0,0);
    public LRUCache(int capacity) { cap = capacity; head.next = tail; tail.prev = head; }
    public int get(int key) {
        if (!map.containsKey(key)) return -1;
        Node n = map.get(key); moveToHead(n); return n.val;
    }
    public void put(int key, int value) {
        if (map.containsKey(key)) { map.get(key).val = value; moveToHead(map.get(key)); }
        else {
            Node n = new Node(key, value); map.put(key, n); addToHead(n);
            if (map.size() > cap) { Node rem = tail.prev; remove(rem); map.remove(rem.key); }
        }
    }
    private void moveToHead(Node n){ remove(n); addToHead(n); }
    private void addToHead(Node n){ n.prev=head; n.next=head.next; head.next.prev=n; head.next=n; }
    private void remove(Node n){ n.prev.next=n.next; n.next.prev=n.prev; }
}

Q35. Stack using Queue

FieldDetails
CompanyMicrosoft, Flipkart
QuestionImplement stack using one or two queues.
ApproachPush-costly: enqueue then rotate size-1 times.
Time ComplexityO(n) push, O(1) pop
Space ComplexityO(n)
Interview TipShows ADT conversion — relate to custom event queues.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.*;
public class StackUsingQueue {
    private Queue<Integer> q = new LinkedList<>();
    public void push(int x) {
        q.offer(x);
        for (int i = 0; i < q.size() - 1; i++) q.offer(q.poll());
    }
    public int pop() { return q.poll(); }
    public int top() { return q.peek(); }
    public boolean empty() { return q.isEmpty(); }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        StackUsingQueue s = new StackUsingQueue();
        s.push(1); s.push(2);
        System.out.println(s.top()); System.out.println(s.pop());
    }
}

Q36. Binary Search Variations

FieldDetails
CompanyGoogle, Amazon
QuestionFind target in sorted array; know first/last occurrence variants.
ApproachStandard binary search with lo, hi, mid.
Time ComplexityO(log n)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipAlso know search in rotated sorted array.

Complete Solution Code

public class BinarySearch {
    public static int search(int[] arr, int target) {
        int lo = 0, hi = arr.length - 1;
        while (lo <= hi) {
            int mid = lo + (hi - lo) / 2;
            if (arr[mid] == target) return mid;
            if (arr[mid] < target) lo = mid + 1; else hi = mid - 1;
        }
        return -1;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(search(new int[]{1,3,5,7,9}, 7));
    }
}

Alternative Approach

First occurrence: when found, set hi = mid - 1 and save answer.

Q37. Linked List Cycle Detection (Floyd's)

FieldDetails
CompanyAmazon, Microsoft
QuestionDetect if a linked list has a cycle.
ApproachSlow and fast pointers — meet if cycle exists.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipDetect infinite retry loops in flaky test handlers.

Complete Solution Code

public class LinkedListCycle {
    static class Node { int val; Node next; Node(int v){val=v;} }
    public static boolean hasCycle(Node head) {
        Node slow = head, fast = head;
        while (fast != null && fast.next != null) {
            slow = slow.next; fast = fast.next.next;
            if (slow == fast) return true;
        }
        return false;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Node n1 = new Node(1), n2 = new Node(2), n3 = new Node(3);
        n1.next = n2; n2.next = n3; n3.next = n2;
        System.out.println(hasCycle(n1));
    }
}

Q38. Word Ladder Problem

FieldDetails
CompanyGoogle, Amazon
QuestionShortest transformation from beginWord to endWord.
ApproachBFS — try changing each char to a-z.
Time ComplexityO(M² × N)
Space ComplexityO(M × N)
Interview TipExplain BFS shortest path with queue + visited set.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.*;
public class WordLadder {
    public static int ladderLength(String begin, String end, List<String> wordList) {
        Set<String> dict = new HashSet<>(wordList);
        if (!dict.contains(end)) return 0;
        Queue<String> q = new LinkedList<>();
        q.offer(begin);
        int level = 1;
        while (!q.isEmpty()) {
            int size = q.size();
            for (int i = 0; i < size; i++) {
                char[] word = q.poll().toCharArray();
                for (int j = 0; j < word.length; j++) {
                    char orig = word[j];
                    for (char c = 'a'; c <= 'z'; c++) {
                        word[j] = c;
                        String next = new String(word);
                        if (next.equals(end)) return level + 1;
                        if (dict.contains(next)) { q.offer(next); dict.remove(next); }
                    }
                    word[j] = orig;
                }
            }
            level++;
        }
        return 0;
    }
}

Q39. Roman to Integer

FieldDetails
CompanyAmazon, Flipkart
QuestionConvert Roman numeral string to integer.
ApproachSubtract if smaller symbol precedes larger.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipParse config version strings in legacy test env files.

Complete Solution Code

import java.util.Map;
public class RomanToInt {
    public static int romanToInt(String s) {
        Map<Character, Integer> map = Map.of(
            'I',1,'V',5,'X',10,'L',50,'C',100,'D',500,'M',1000);
        int total = 0;
        for (int i = 0; i < s.length(); i++) {
            int val = map.get(s.charAt(i));
            if (i + 1 < s.length() && val < map.get(s.charAt(i + 1))) total -= val;
            else total += val;
        }
        return total;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(romanToInt("MCMXCIV"));
    }
}

Q40. Integer to Roman

FieldDetails
CompanyAmazon, Microsoft
QuestionConvert integer to Roman numeral.
ApproachGreedy with value-symbol pairs including subtractive forms.
Time ComplexityO(1)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipPredefine pairs: 900, 400, 90, 40, 9, 4, 1.

Complete Solution Code

public class IntToRoman {
    public static String intToRoman(int num) {
        int[] vals = {1000,900,500,400,100,90,50,40,10,9,5,4,1};
        String[] syms = {"M","CM","D","CD","C","XC","L","XL","X","IX","V","IV","I"};
        StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder();
        for (int i = 0; i < vals.length; i++)
            while (num >= vals[i]) { sb.append(syms[i]); num -= vals[i]; }
        return sb.toString();
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(intToRoman(1994));
    }
}

SDET-SPECIFIC (Framework / Automation Focused)

Q41. Write Singleton DriverFactory

FieldDetails
CompanyAll SDET interviews
QuestionThread-safe singleton WebDriver factory reading browser from config.
ApproachDouble-checked locking with volatile instance.
Time ComplexityO(1)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipExplain why singleton alone fails in parallel — lead to ThreadLocal (Q42).

Complete Solution Code

import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.chrome.ChromeDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.firefox.FirefoxDriver;

public class DriverFactory {
    private static volatile DriverFactory instance;
    private WebDriver driver;

    private DriverFactory() {}

    public static DriverFactory getInstance() {
        if (instance == null) {
            synchronized (DriverFactory.class) {
                if (instance == null) instance = new DriverFactory();
            }
        }
        return instance;
    }

    public WebDriver getDriver(String browser) {
        if (driver == null) {
            driver = "firefox".equalsIgnoreCase(browser)
                ? new FirefoxDriver() : new ChromeDriver();
        }
        return driver;
    }

    public void quitDriver() {
        if (driver != null) { driver.quit(); driver = null; }
    }
}

Q42. Write ThreadLocal WebDriver Manager

FieldDetails
CompanySDET 4+ years
QuestionIsolated WebDriver per TestNG thread for parallel execution.
ApproachThreadLocal set in @BeforeMethod, remove in @AfterMethod.
Time ComplexityO(1)
Space ComplexityO(threads)
Interview TipStandard production pattern — always call remove() to prevent leaks.

Complete Solution Code

import org.openqa.selenium.WebDriver;
import org.openqa.selenium.chrome.ChromeDriver;

public class DriverManager {
    private static final ThreadLocal<WebDriver> DRIVER = new ThreadLocal<>();

    public static void setDriver(String browser) {
        WebDriver driver = new ChromeDriver(); // extend for browser switch
        DRIVER.set(driver);
    }

    public static WebDriver getDriver() {
        WebDriver driver = DRIVER.get();
        if (driver == null)
            throw new IllegalStateException("WebDriver not initialized for thread");
        return driver;
    }

    public static void removeDriver() {
        WebDriver driver = DRIVER.get();
        if (driver != null) driver.quit();
        DRIVER.remove();
    }
}

Q43. Create Custom Retry Mechanism

FieldDetails
CompanySDET / Lead interviews
QuestionRetry failed tests n times with configurable count.
ApproachTestNG IRetryAnalyzer + IAnnotationTransformer.
Time ComplexityO(attempts)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipDiscuss idempotent tests and screenshot on final failure only.

Complete Solution Code

import org.testng.IRetryAnalyzer;
import org.testng.ITestResult;

public class RetryAnalyzer implements IRetryAnalyzer {
    private int count = 0;
    private static final int MAX = 2;

    @Override
    public boolean retry(ITestResult result) {
        if (count < MAX) { count++; return true; }
        return false;
    }
}
// Usage: @Test(retryAnalyzer = RetryAnalyzer.class)

Q44. Design Data-Driven Framework Utility

FieldDetails
CompanySDET interviews
QuestionRead test data and feed TestNG @DataProvider.
ApproachReturn Object[][] from List<Map<String,String>>.
Time ComplexityO(rows × cols)
Space ComplexityO(rows × cols)
Interview TipSeparate data layer from test logic — core framework principle.

Complete Solution Code

import org.testng.annotations.DataProvider;
import java.util.*;

public class DataDrivenUtil {
    public static List<Map<String, String>> readTestData() {
        List<Map<String, String>> rows = new ArrayList<>();
        rows.add(Map.of("username", "admin", "password", "pass123"));
        rows.add(Map.of("username", "guest", "password", "guest"));
        return rows;
    }

    @DataProvider(name = "loginData")
    public Object[][] loginData() {
        List<Map<String, String>> data = readTestData();
        Object[][] out = new Object[data.size()][1];
        for (int i = 0; i < data.size(); i++) out[i][0] = data.get(i);
        return out;
    }
}

Q45. Parse JSON and Extract Values

FieldDetails
CompanyAPI + UI hybrid SDET
QuestionRead JSON test data and extract nested field values.
ApproachJackson ObjectMapper + JsonNode navigation.
Time ComplexityO(n)
Space ComplexityO(n)
Interview TipStandard in REST Assured + JSON-driven UI test data.

Complete Solution Code

import com.fasterxml.jackson.databind.JsonNode;
import com.fasterxml.jackson.databind.ObjectMapper;

public class JsonParserUtil {
    private static final ObjectMapper MAPPER = new ObjectMapper();

    public static String extract(String json, String field) throws Exception {
        JsonNode root = MAPPER.readTree(json);
        return root.get(field).asText();
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception {
        String json = "{\"user\":{\"name\":\"sdet\",\"role\":\"automation\"}}";
        JsonNode node = MAPPER.readTree(json);
        System.out.println(node.get("user").get("role").asText());
    }
}

Q46. Read Excel and Return List<Map>

FieldDetails
CompanyData-driven framework interviews
QuestionApache POI reads .xlsx into List<Map<String,String>>.
ApproachRow 0 = headers; each row becomes a Map.
Time ComplexityO(rows × cols)
Space ComplexityO(rows × cols)
Interview TipMost common data-driven pattern in Java Selenium interviews.

Complete Solution Code

import org.apache.poi.ss.usermodel.*;
import org.apache.poi.xssf.usermodel.XSSFWorkbook;
import java.io.FileInputStream;
import java.util.*;

public class ExcelReader {
    public static List<Map<String, String>> read(String path, String sheetName) throws Exception {
        List<Map<String, String>> data = new ArrayList<>();
        try (Workbook wb = new XSSFWorkbook(new FileInputStream(path))) {
            Sheet sheet = wb.getSheet(sheetName);
            Row header = sheet.getRow(0);
            for (int i = 1; i <= sheet.getLastRowNum(); i++) {
                Row row = sheet.getRow(i);
                Map<String, String> map = new LinkedHashMap<>();
                for (int j = 0; j < header.getLastCellNum(); j++)
                    map.put(header.getCell(j).getStringCellValue(),
                            row.getCell(j).getStringCellValue());
                data.add(map);
            }
        }
        return data;
    }
}

Q47. Write Custom Wait Utility

FieldDetails
CompanySelenium framework interviews
QuestionFluent wait wrapper with logging and config-driven timeout.
ApproachWebDriverWait + ExpectedConditions + polling interval.
Time ComplexityO(wait time)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipNever use Thread.sleep — always explicit waits in framework code.

Complete Solution Code

import org.openqa.selenium.*;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.*;
import java.time.Duration;

public class WaitUtil {
    public static WebElement waitVisible(WebDriver driver, By locator, int seconds) {
        return new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(seconds))
            .pollingEvery(Duration.ofMillis(500))
            .until(ExpectedConditions.visibilityOfElementLocated(locator));
    }
}

Q48. Implement Builder Pattern for Test Config

FieldDetails
CompanySenior SDET
QuestionImmutable TestConfig built step-by-step with Builder.
ApproachStatic nested Builder with chained setters.
Time ComplexityO(1)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipKeeps BaseTest setup readable: browser, url, headless flags.

Complete Solution Code

public class TestConfig {
    private final String browser, url;
    private final boolean headless;

    private TestConfig(Builder b) { browser=b.browser; url=b.url; headless=b.headless; }
    public String getBrowser(){ return browser; }
    public String getUrl(){ return url; }
    public boolean isHeadless(){ return headless; }

    public static class Builder {
        private String browser = "chrome", url = "about:blank";
        private boolean headless = false;
        public Builder browser(String v){ browser=v; return this; }
        public Builder url(String v){ url=v; return this; }
        public Builder headless(boolean v){ headless=v; return this; }
        public TestConfig build(){ return new TestConfig(this); }
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        TestConfig cfg = new TestConfig.Builder()
            .browser("chrome").url("https://qa.app.com").headless(true).build();
        System.out.println(cfg.getUrl());
    }
}

Q49. Create Custom Annotation Processor

FieldDetails
CompanyLead SDET / Architect
Question@RetryCount meta-annotation read via reflection in TestNG listener.
ApproachRetentionPolicy.RUNTIME + IInvokedMethodListener.
Time ComplexityO(1)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipShows framework extensibility beyond basic Page Object Model.

Complete Solution Code

import java.lang.annotation.Retention;
import java.lang.annotation.RetentionPolicy;
import java.lang.reflect.Method;

@Retention(RetentionPolicy.RUNTIME)
@interface RetryCount { int value() default 1; }

public class AnnotationProcessor {
    public static int getRetryCount(Method method) {
        if (method.isAnnotationPresent(RetryCount.class))
            return method.getAnnotation(RetryCount.class).value();
        return 1;
    }
}
// @Test @RetryCount(3) public void flakyLoginTest() { ... }

Q50. Design Page Object Base Class

FieldDetails
CompanyAll SDET levels
QuestionAbstract BasePage with driver, wait, and common actions.
ApproachConstructor injection + PageFactory.initElements.
Time ComplexityO(1)
Space ComplexityO(1)
Interview TipCore POM pattern — every SDET must whiteboard this confidently.

Complete Solution Code

import org.openqa.selenium.*;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.*;
import org.openqa.selenium.support.ui.*;
import java.time.Duration;

public abstract class BasePage {
    protected WebDriver driver;
    protected WebDriverWait wait;

    protected BasePage(WebDriver driver) {
        this.driver = driver;
        this.wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, Duration.ofSeconds(20));
        PageFactory.initElements(driver, this);
    }

    protected void click(WebElement element) {
        wait.until(d -> element.isDisplayed() && element.isEnabled());
        element.click();
    }

    protected void type(WebElement element, String text) {
        wait.until(d -> element.isDisplayed());
        element.clear();
        element.sendKeys(text);
    }
}

ThreadLocal Quick Reference

MethodPurposeFramework Pattern
set(value)Bind value to current threadDRIVER.set(new ChromeDriver()) in @BeforeMethod
get()Retrieve thread-bound valueWebDriver d = DRIVER.get() in Page Object
remove()Clear binding; prevent memory leakDRIVER.remove() in @AfterMethod after quit()
ThreadLocal pattern: set() in setup → get() throughout test → quit() + remove() in teardown. Never share one WebDriver across parallel threads.

private static ThreadLocal<WebDriver> driver = new ThreadLocal<>();

public static WebDriver get() { return driver.get(); }
public static void quit() { if (driver.get()!=null) driver.get().quit(); driver.remove(); }

List<String> failed = results.stream()
    .filter(r -> "FAIL".equals(r.getStatus()))
    .map(TestResult::getName).collect(Collectors.toList());

Map<String, Integer> freq = new HashMap<>();
for (String s : failures) freq.merge(s, 1, Integer::sum);
freq.forEach((k,v) -> System.out.println(k + ": " + v));

Section 24: 1-Day Interview Revision Notes

Condensed revision for SDET interviews — read once in the morning, practice 5 coding problems in the afternoon, mock framework design in the evening.

Top 25 Most Asked Java Questions for SDET

#Question2-Line Answer
1What is JDK vs JRE vs JVM?JDK compiles and develops; JRE runs apps; JVM executes bytecode. Automation needs JDK on CI for Maven compilation.
2Why is String immutable?Security (credentials), thread safety (String pool), and hash stability. Use StringBuilder for loop concatenation in report builders.
3== vs .equals()?== compares references; equals() compares content. Always use equals() for String comparison in assertions.
4What is method overloading?Same method name, different parameters — compile time. Example: click(By) and click(WebElement) in BasePage.
5What is method overriding?Subclass redefines parent method — runtime polymorphism. Example: @BeforeMethod setup() in child BaseTest.
6Abstract class vs Interface?Abstract class: partial implementation + state. Interface: contract only (Java 8+ default methods). DriverFactory often uses interface.
7What is encapsulation?Hide fields, expose via getters/setters. Page Objects hide WebElement locators from test classes.
8Checked vs Unchecked exception?Checked: must handle (IOException). Unchecked: RuntimeException (NoSuchElementException). Selenium throws mostly unchecked.
9What is final keyword?final class = no inheritance; final method = no override; final variable = constant. Config URLs often final static.
10What is static keyword?Belongs to class, not instance. ConfigReader.get() is static — shared across all tests in JVM.
11How does HashMap work internally?Array of buckets; hashCode → bucket index; collision via linked list/tree (Java 8). O(1) average get/put.
12ArrayList vs LinkedList?ArrayList: fast random access O(1). LinkedList: fast insert/delete O(1). Use ArrayList for test name lists.
13What is ThreadLocal?Thread-bound variable storage. Each TestNG thread gets its own WebDriver instance via ThreadLocal.
14What is synchronized?Lock for thread-safe access. Rare in tests; prefer ThreadLocal over synchronized WebDriver access.
15What are Java 8 lambdas?Anonymous functions enabling functional-style code. Filter failed tests: results.stream().filter(r -> r.isFailed()).
16What is Optional?Container avoiding NullPointerException. findFirst() returns Optional — use orElse/orElseThrow safely.
17Comparable vs Comparator?Comparable: natural order (implements compareTo). Comparator: custom order. Sort tests by duration with Comparator.
18What is garbage collection?JVM reclaims unreferenced objects. driver.quit() releases browser; null references help GC reclaim memory.
19What is autoboxing?Primitive ↔ wrapper automatic conversion. int ↔ Integer in collections and stream operations.
20What is serialization?Object → byte stream for storage/transmission. Save Cucumber test context or session cookies to file.
21What is reflection?Inspect/modify classes at runtime. TestNG uses reflection to invoke @Test methods; read custom annotations.
22What is Singleton pattern?One instance per JVM. ConfigReader and ReportManager — but NOT WebDriver in parallel (use ThreadLocal).
23What is Factory pattern?Centralized object creation. DriverFactory.createDriver(browser) returns correct WebDriver implementation.
24What is Builder pattern?Step-by-step object construction. TestConfig.Builder().browser("chrome").url(url).build().
25What is Page Object Model?UI locators + actions in page classes; tests call business methods. Reduces duplication and maintenance cost.

Top 25 Most Asked Coding Questions

#QuestionApproach Hint
1Reverse a StringTwo pointers on char[] or StringBuilder.reverse()
2Check PalindromeTwo pointers; skip non-alphanumeric
3Find duplicate in arrayHashSet or Floyd cycle detection
4Two SumHashMap complement lookup O(n)
5Valid parenthesesStack push open, pop match close
6First non-repeated charLinkedHashMap frequency count

Frequently Confused Topics

50 Quick Revision Points

1–10: OOP Essentials

  1. Four pillars: Encapsulation, Inheritance, Polymorphism, Abstraction.
  2. Page Object Model is encapsulation applied to UI automation.
  3. WebDriver is an interface — ChromeDriver/FirefoxDriver are implementations.
  4. Overloading: same name, different parameters — compile time binding.
  5. Overriding: subclass method replaces parent — runtime binding with @Override.
  6. Abstract class can have constructors; interface cannot (until Java changes).
  7. Java supports single inheritance for classes; multiple interfaces allowed.
  8. super() calls parent constructor; super.method() calls parent method.
  9. this() calls another constructor in same class.
  10. Composition (has-a) preferred over deep inheritance for test utilities.

11–20: String Essentials

  1. String is immutable — every modification creates new object.
  2. String pool interns literal strings for memory efficiency.
  3. StringBuilder for single-thread string building in loops.
  4. String.join(",", list) replaces manual comma concatenation.
  5. String.format("//a[text()='%s']", name) for dynamic XPath.
  6. split("\\s+") handles multiple spaces in log parsing.
  7. equalsIgnoreCase for browser name from config comparison.
  8. trim() before comparing Excel cell values.
  9. isBlank() (Java 11) checks empty or whitespace-only strings.
  10. Never use == for String content comparison in assertions.

21–30: Collections Essentials

  1. ArrayList: default choice for ordered test case lists.
  2. HashMap: default for key-value test data and config cache.
  3. HashSet: deduplicate test IDs or tags.
  4. LinkedHashMap preserves Excel column order in row maps.
  5. ConcurrentHashMap for thread-safe shared state in parallel runs.
  6. Iterator.remove() safe during iteration; avoid ConcurrentModificationException.
  7. Collections.sort() vs list.sort(Comparator) — prefer latter in Java 8+.
  8. Map.getOrDefault(key, default) avoids null checks on config keys.
  9. Map.merge(key, 1, Integer::sum) for frequency counting.
  10. Arrays.asList() returns fixed-size list — use new ArrayList<>() if mutating.

31–40: Java 8 Essentials

  1. Lambda: (param) -> expression — replaces anonymous inner classes.
  2. Method reference: TestResult::getName shorthand for t -> t.getName().
  3. Stream pipeline: source → intermediate → terminal operation.
  4. filter + map + collect is the most common stream pattern in reports.
  5. Predicate<T> for filtering; Function<T,R> for mapping.
  6. Optional.ofNullable avoids NullPointerException on findFirst results.
  7. Collectors.groupingBy groups test results by status/pass/fail.
  8. Collectors.toMap builds lookup from test name to TestResult.
  9. forEach is terminal — use for side effects like logging.
  10. Parallel streams rarely help in Selenium tests (I/O bound, not CPU bound).

41–50: Framework / Design Essentials

  1. ThreadLocal WebDriver: set → get → quit → remove per test thread.
  2. Singleton ConfigReader: load properties once in static block.
  3. Factory pattern: DriverFactory.createDriver(browser) centralizes creation.
  4. Builder pattern: fluent TestConfig construction with validation.
  5. Page Object: @FindBy locators + public action methods + no assertions in page.
  6. BaseTest: @BeforeMethod driver setup, @AfterMethod teardown + screenshot on fail.
  7. Explicit waits (WebDriverWait) — never Thread.sleep in framework code.
  8. DataProvider returns Object[][] from Excel/JSON reader utility.
  9. IRetryAnalyzer for flaky test retry with max attempt limit.
  10. Layered framework: Tests → Page Objects → Utilities → Config/Data.

Common Interview Mistakes for 4+ Years

  1. Saying "I know Java" but can't write code — always practice on whiteboard/paper.
  2. Not explaining framework architecture — draw layers: config, driver, pages, tests, reports.
  3. Confusing overloading/overriding — overload = same class; override = inheritance.
  4. Not knowing HashMap internal working — hashCode, bucket, collision chain/tree.
  5. Can't explain ThreadLocal — per-thread WebDriver isolation for parallel TestNG.
  6. Not knowing design patterns — Singleton, Factory, Builder, Page Object minimum.
  7. Poor coding — no edge cases (null, empty), no error handling.
  8. Not discussing time complexity — always state Big-O for coding solutions.
  9. Not relating Java to automation — connect every concept to framework usage.
  10. Using deprecated practices — findElementBy* instead of By locators; Thread.sleep.
  11. Not knowing Java 8 features — streams, lambdas, Optional expected at 4+ years.
  12. Poor problem-solving approach — clarify input/output, examples, edge cases before coding.

Interview Tips for Senior SDET (10 Points)

  1. Start with requirements clarification — ask about parallel execution, browsers, CI environment.
  2. Whiteboard framework architecture before diving into code — show system thinking.
  3. Discuss trade-offs: Singleton vs ThreadLocal, implicit vs explicit waits, POM vs Screenplay.
  4. Mention scalability: Selenium Grid, Docker, parallel TestNG threads, thread-safe utilities.
  5. Cover error handling: screenshot on failure, retry strategy, logging, report integration.
  6. Reference real project experience — "In my framework, I used..." with specific patterns.
  7. Know CI/CD integration — Maven profiles, Jenkins pipeline, test tagging for smoke/regression.
  8. Demonstrate API + UI hybrid knowledge — REST Assured, JSON parsing, same Java codebase.
  9. Ask thoughtful questions about team test strategy, flakiness, coverage metrics.
  10. Stay calm on unknowns — explain your approach even if you can't finish optimal solution.

Section 25: Career Roadmap

Career planning for Automation Engineers with ~4 years experience targeting Senior SDET, Lead, or Architect roles in 12–18 months.

Current: Automation Engineer (4 Years) — Skills Self-Assessment

Rating guide: 1=Aware, 2=Basic usage, 3=Independent, 4=Advanced/Design, 5=Expert/Mentor. Be honest — gaps drive your 6-week plan.

Career Path 1: Senior AE → Lead QA → QA Manager → Director of QA

  • Focus: Team leadership, process improvement, test strategy, stakeholder management.
  • Key skills: People management, Agile ceremonies, metrics (defect escape rate, automation coverage), budgeting.
  • Java relevance: Code review automation frameworks; guide team on standards — not daily coding.
  • Timeline: Senior AE (4–5 yrs) → Lead (6–8 yrs) → Manager (8–12 yrs) → Director (12+ yrs).

Career Path 2: SDET II → SDET III → Staff SDET → Principal SDET

  • Focus: Technical depth, framework architecture, tooling, performance, platform engineering.
  • Key skills: System design, Java advanced, CI/CD pipelines, test infrastructure, mentoring engineers.
  • Java relevance: Daily — build libraries, custom TestNG listeners, REST frameworks, Grid solutions.
  • Timeline: SDET II (3–5 yrs) → SDET III (5–7 yrs) → Staff (7–10 yrs) → Principal (10+ yrs).

Career Path 3: Test Architect → Engineering Manager

  • Focus: System design, cross-team impact, quality strategy across org, build vs buy decisions.
  • Key skills: Architecture diagrams, scalability, microservices testing, cloud (AWS/GCP), leadership.
  • Java relevance: Design multi-module Maven projects, shared automation libraries, SDK for internal teams.
  • Timeline: Test Architect (7–9 yrs) → EM (9+ yrs) if transitioning to people management.

Networking and Visibility

  • Contribute to one open-source test project (WebDriverManager, REST Assured docs).
  • Write a Medium/LinkedIn post on a framework pattern you implemented — builds credibility.
  • Join local QA meetups or Ministry of Testing chapters for referral opportunities.
  • Maintain GitHub portfolio with: framework skeleton, API test suite, CI pipeline YAML.
  • Request LinkedIn recommendations from Lead/Dev who saw your automation impact.
